[B30] PRESSES -- B30 relates to presses, devices that apply force to shape, compact, or assemble materials. It includes hydraulic, pneumatic, mechanical and stamping presses used in metalworking, plastics molding, food processing and other manufacturing processes, as well as related control and safety mechanisms.
[B30B] PRESSES IN GENERAL -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Presses in general and also those presses, for particular purposes, which are not provided for elsewhere.
[B30B 1/00] Presses, using a press ram, characterised by the features of the drive therefor, pressure being transmitted directly, or through simple thrust or tension members only, to the press ram or platen -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Presses using a press ram characterised by the features of the drive therefor in general and also those presses using a press ram characterised by the features of the drive therefor, for particular purposes, which are not provided for elsewhere. The driving system is decomposed, if necessary, in simple fluid actuation units (e.g. a cylinder/piston) and simple mechanical force multipliers (e.g. a lever, a toggle, a screw/nut system).
[B30B 1/001] by explosive charges -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Presses for which the fluid pressure is generated by explosive charges in a cylinder/piston unit or in a chamber. Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group:  DE-A-2122605
[B30B 1/002] by internal combustion mechanism -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Presses for which the fluid pressure is generated by internal combustion mechanism in a cylinder/piston unit. Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group:  FR-A-2046587
[B30B 1/003] by an elastic bag or diaphragm expanded by fluid pressure -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Presses for which the fluid is injected in a bag or in a chamber presenting a diaphragm. Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group:  WO-A-9114569
[B30B 1/005] by thermal expansion or evaporation -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group:  US-A-4260582
[B30B 1/006] by a scissor or lazy-tongs mechanism -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Presses for which one part of the scissor or lazy-tongs mechanism is in direct contact or in contact through simple thrust or tension members only, to the press ram or platen. Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group:  DE-A-4013107
[B30B 1/007] using a fluid connection between the drive means and the press ram -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Presses for which the driving unit is classified per se. Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group:  US-A-6539853
[B30B 1/008] by a rod swinging between a fixed plane and the ram -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Presses for which one end of the rod follows a path on a fixed plane and the other end of the rod is in direct contact or in contact through simple thrust or tension members only, to the press ram or platen. Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group:  GB-A-1489575
[B30B 1/02] by lever mechanism -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Presses for which one part of the lever is in direct contact or in contact through simple thrust or tension members only, to the press ram or platen.  Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group:  WO-A-9015268
[B30B 1/04] operated by hand or foot -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Presses for which another part of the lever is in direct or indirect contact with the hand or the foot of an operator applying a force. Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group:  US-A-5329846
[B30B 1/06] operated by cams, eccentrics, or cranks -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Presses for which another part of the lever is in direct or indirect contact with a cam, eccentric, or crank unit applying a force. Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group:  DE-A-10241107
[B30B 1/08] operated by fluid-pressure means -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Presses for which another part of the lever is in direct or indirect contact with a fluid-pressure unit applying a force. Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group:  US-A-4329865
[B30B 1/10] by toggle mechanism -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Presses for which one part of the toggle is in direct contact or in contact through simple thrust or tension members only, to the press ram or platen. The driving force is applied transversally to the line that can be drawn between the two ends of the two bars system constituting the toggle. Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group:  US-A-4302412

[B30B 11/22] Extrusion presses -- B30B 11/22 relates to extrusion presses, a subset of presses specially adapted for forming shaped articles from material in a particulate or plastic state. These machines force material through a die or onto a moving surface to produce continuous or discrete products such as briquettes, tablets or extruded profiles. The class covers the mechanical design and operation of such equipment.

[B31] MAKING ARTICLES OF PAPER, CARDBOARD OR MATERIAL WORKED IN A MANNER ANALOGOUS TO PAPER -- B31 covers processes for producing paper, cardboard and other sheet-like materials, encompassing steps such as pulping, forming, drying and finishing. The subclass also includes methods for making analogous non-paper sheets such as synthetic or composite boards.
[B31B] MAKING CONTAINERS OF PAPER, CARDBOARD OR MATERIAL WORKED IN A MANNER ANALOGOUS TO PAPER -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Making wound articles, e.g. wound tubes -> B31C - Combined making and filling -> B65B  **Glossary:** - Envelopes or bags: essentially flexible containers, the final shape of which is determined by their contents - Boxes or cartons: including bags formed similarly to cartons, trays with upstanding side-walls, barrels, tubes and cups, other than articles formed by winding
[B31B 2100/00] Indexing scheme associated with group -- B31B 2100/00 covers the indexing scheme used to organise groups of patents dealing with the manufacture of paper, cardboard or analogous material containers. It classifies methods, apparatus and related technical features for producing such containers, providing a systematic way to locate documents within the broader "making containers of paper, cardboard or material worked in a manner analogous to paper" category.
[B31B 2100/002] characterised by the shape of the blank from which they are formed -- B31B 2100/002 refers to methods of producing paper, cardboard or analogous material containers in which the defining feature is the shape of the blank from which the container is formed, such as pre-cut, folded, or tubular blanks that determine the final geometry. This subclass falls under performing operations, specifically the making of articles and containers from paper-like materials.
[B31B 2100/0022] made from tubular webs or blanks, including by tube or bottom forming operations -- The CPC subclass B31B 2100/0022 covers processes for producing paper or paper-analog containers from tubular webs or blanks, including tube-forming and bottom-forming techniques. It falls under the hierarchy of performing operations, specifically the making of paper, cardboard or similar material articles and the subsequent formation of containers from those sheets.
[B31B 2100/0024] having all side walls attached to the bottom -- The code B31B 2100/0024 denotes paper, cardboard or analogous material containers whose side walls are permanently joined to the bottom, typically formed from a single blank and sealed together. This includes fold-over cartons, boxes and similar packaging where the walls and base are integral rather than detachable.
[B31B 2100/0026] having two opposite first side walls attached to the bottom and the other side walls being attached to the first side walls -- This CPC subgroup covers paper or paper-like containers whose construction features two opposite side walls fastened directly to the bottom panel, while the remaining side walls are attached to those first side walls, defining a specific box architecture used in manufacturing.
[B31B 2100/0028] made by first folding a sheet to a U-shape, constituting the bottom and two first side walls, after which the two other side walls are formed from these first side walls -- The B31B 2100/0028 entry covers a method for producing paper containers in which a sheet is first folded into a U-shape that forms the bottom and two initial side walls, after which the remaining side walls are created from those first walls, completing the container.
[B31B 2105/00] Rigid or semi-rigid containers made by assembling separate sheets, blanks or webs -- This CPC subclass covers rigid or semi-rigid containers formed by joining separate sheets, blanks or webs of paper, cardboard or analogous materials, such as boxes, trays and similar articles. It addresses the assembly techniques used to create these containers from individual layers.
[B31B 2105/001] made from laminated webs, e.g. including laminating the webs -- This CPC subclass deals with making rigid or semi-rigid containers by assembling separate sheets, blanks or webs that have been laminated together. It includes processes where the individual web layers are bonded through laminating before or during formation of the container.
[B31B 2105/002] Making boxes characterised by the shape of the blanks from which they are formed -- This subclass covers methods for producing rigid or semi-rigid containers of paper, cardboard or analogous material where the shape of the blank determines the final box geometry, including cutting, scoring, folding and assembling separate sheets or webs to form the finished container.
[B31B 2105/0022] Making boxes from tubular webs or blanks, e.g. with separate bottoms, including tube or bottom forming operations -- This subclass concerns the manufacture of rigid or semi-rigid containers such as boxes by shaping tubular webs or flat blanks, including operations that form separate bottoms and the tube itself. It applies to paper, cardboard or similar sheet-like materials processed in an analogous manner.
[B31B 2105/0024] Making boxes having all side walls attached to the bottom -- This CPC subgroup concerns processes for producing rigid or semi-rigid paper containers in which the side walls are permanently connected to the bottom, such as by folding and adhesive or welding of a single sheet or pre-cut blanks to form a box.
[B31B 2105/0025] Making boxes by uniting two U-shaped blanks -- The CPC subclass B31B 2105/0025 covers processes for making rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers by joining two U-shaped blanks to form a box, typically through folding, bonding or other uniting operations.
[B31B 2105/0027] Making boxes from blanks consisting of side wall panels integral with a bottom panel and additional side wall panels -- This subclass covers the production of rigid or semi-rigid paper or cardboard boxes formed from a single blank in which the side wall panels are joined to a bottom panel and may include additional side panels. The process involves cutting or stamping the integral blank and folding it into a container without requiring separate sheet assembly.
[B31B 2110/00] Shape of rigid or semi-rigid containers -- The subclass covers the geometric design of rigid or semi-rigid containers made from paper, cardboard or similar materials, focusing on the overall shape, dimensions, contours and cross-section that define the container's form. It is used to classify patents that specify particular container shapes rather than their composition or manufacturing process.
[B31B 2110/10] having a cross section of varying size or shape, e.g. conical or pyramidal -- The subclass B31B 2110/10 classifies rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous material containers whose cross-section changes along their length, such as conical or pyramidal shapes. It falls under the hierarchy of making articles of paper and specifically the shape of containers.
[B31B 2110/20] having a curved cross section, e.g. circular -- This CPC subclass pertains to rigid or semi-rigid containers made of paper, cardboard or analogous materials whose cross-section is curved, such as circular or other rounded shapes, as opposed to rectangular or angular profiles. It classifies the shape feature of the container.
[B31B 2110/30] having a polygonal cross section -- The subclass B31B 2110/30 applies to rigid or semi-rigid containers made of paper, cardboard or analogous material whose cross-section is polygonal, such as boxes, trays or cans having rectangular, triangular or other multi-sided shapes. It is part of the CPC hierarchy for making paper containers.
[B31B 2110/35] rectangular, e.g. square -- B31B 2110/35 defines containers made of paper, cardboard or analogous material whose overall shape is rectangular, for example a square. It classifies the geometry of rigid or semi-rigid paper containers within the broader group of making containers of paper, cardboard or similar material.
[B31B 2110/40] without sidewalls -- The subclass B31B 2110/40 covers rigid or semi-rigid containers made of paper, cardboard or analogous material that are formed without sidewalls, such as open trays, pallets or molds that have only a bottom (and possibly a cover) but no enclosing walls.
[B31B 2120/00] Construction of rigid or semi-rigid containers -- The CPC subclass B31B 2120/00 covers methods and apparatus for constructing rigid or semi-rigid containers from paper, cardboard or equivalent sheet materials, including shaping, joining, reinforcing and finishing operations such as cutting, folding, gluing, molding or sealing to produce boxes, trays, tubes and similar packaging forms.
[B31B 2120/002] having contracted or rolled necks, having shoulders -- The subclass covers containers made of paper, cardboard or analogous material that have necks formed by contraction or rolling and include shoulders, features typical of rigid or semi-rigid container designs.
[B31B 2120/004] the bottom of which includes a rim projecting at the edges -- B31B 2120/004 covers the construction of rigid or semi-rigid containers made of paper, cardboard or analogous material where the bottom includes a rim that projects outward at the edges to reinforce the base and aid stacking or handling.
[B31B 2120/10] provided with covers, e.g. lids -- The B31B 2120/10 subclass covers containers of paper, cardboard or similar materials that are equipped with covers such as lids, including rigid or semi-rigid forms used for packaging or storage.
[B31B 2120/102] with a hinged cover -- B31B 2120/102 relates to the construction of rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous material containers that incorporate a hinged cover, detailing features of the hinge mechanism and its integration into the container's structure.
[B31B 2120/20] provided with two or more compartments -- This subclass covers the construction of rigid or semi-rigid containers made of paper, cardboard or analogous materials that are formed with two or more separate compartments, such as divided trays or multi-section boxes. It pertains to manufacturing processes and designs that create internal subdivisions within a single paper-based package.
[B31B 2120/25] formed by partitions or like inserts not integral with walls -- The B31B 2120/25 subclass covers paper, cardboard or analogous material containers whose interior is divided by separate partitions or inserts that are not permanently attached to the container walls. This includes rigid or semi-rigid boxes, trays or crates that gain compartmentalisation through removable or loosely fixed dividers rather than integral wall structures.
[B31B 2120/30] collapsible -- B31B 2120/30 covers the design and production of rigid or semi-rigid containers made from paper, cardboard or similar sheet-material that can be folded flat and later expanded into a functional shape, i.e., collapsible containers. It falls under the broader class of making containers of paper and related materials.
[B31B 2120/302] collapsible into a flat condition -- The subclass includes designs for paper, cardboard or analogous material containers that can be transformed from a three-dimensional shape to a flat condition for easy handling, storage or shipment. It addresses folding, rolling or other mechanisms that allow rigid or semi-rigid containers to be collapsed without damaging the material.
[B31B 2120/40] lined or internally reinforced -- The CPC subclass B31B 2120/40 relates to rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers that incorporate a lining or internal reinforcement. Such reinforcement may be a coating, laminate, or insert of another material applied to improve strength, barrier or durability of the container. It is used for items like cartons, trays or boxes that require added protection beyond the base paper structure.
[B31B 2120/402] by applying a liner to already made boxes, e.g. opening or distending of the liner or the box -- The subclass B31B 2120/402 covers processes for applying a liner to already formed paper or cardboard containers, for example opening, inserting or inflating a liner within a box to create a rigid or semi-rigid container. It is part of the group on making containers of paper, cardboard or analogous materials, under the broader category of making articles of paper.
[B31B 2120/404] using vacuum or pressure means to force the liner against the wall -- The subclass covers methods of forming paper, cardboard or analogous material containers in which vacuum or pressure is applied to push the liner against the container wall, ensuring proper adhesion, shaping and rigidity of the finished container.
[B31B 2120/406] the lining material being a plunger, a web, a sheet or a bag to be forced into the box, e.g. by using heat -- This subclass covers methods for inserting a lining material such as a plunger, web, sheet or bag into a rigid or semi-rigid paper or cardboard container, typically by forcing it in and optionally using heat to shape the liner. It pertains to the construction of such containers where the liner is formed in-situ.
[B31B 2120/407] involving forming of the liner before inserting -- This CPC subclass covers processes for producing rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers in which the liner is formed separately before being inserted into the container's mold or core, emphasizing pre-formed liners as a step in the container-making operation.
[B31B 2120/408] by folding a sheet or blank around an inner tubular liner -- The code refers to a process for producing rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or similar containers by folding a sheet or blank around an inner tubular liner, creating the container wall. It is a subcategory of making containers of paper, cardboard or analogous materials within the performing-operations section.
[B31B 2120/50] covered or externally reinforced -- The code B31B 2120/50 covers containers of paper, cardboard or paper-analogous material that are provided with a covering or external reinforcement, such as a metal, plastic or composite layer, to increase rigidity or protect the container. This subcategory falls under making containers of paper-based material and specifically addresses the construction of rigid or semi-rigid containers with added outer reinforcement.
[B31B 2120/501] by applying wrapping material only on the side wall part of a box -- This subcategory pertains to processes for constructing rigid or semi-rigid paper containers where a wrapping material such as film or foil is applied solely to the side-wall part of the box, leaving the top and bottom untreated. It relates to methods of reinforcing or decorating containers by side-wall-only wrapping.
[B31B 2120/502] having integral corner posts or reinforcements -- B31B 2120/502 covers the construction of rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers that incorporate built-in corner posts or reinforcements. The classification applies to methods and structures where the supporting elements are formed as an integral part of the container's walls.
[B31B 2120/60] of drawer-and-shell type -- The CPC code B31B 2120/60 covers the manufacture of rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous material containers that employ a drawer-and-shell configuration, where a separate tray or drawer slides within a surrounding shell to form the finished packaging. This sub-group falls under making containers of paper or similar material, specifically addressing the construction of such drawer-type containers.
[B31B 2120/70] having corrugated or pleated walls -- This subclass covers containers made from paper or analogous material that incorporate corrugated or pleated wall structures to provide stiffness and strength, typically used for rigid or semi-rigid packaging. The feature is defined by the presence of regular folds or ribs in the wall which may be formed by embossing or folding.
[B31B 2150/00] Indexing scheme associated with group -- The Cooperative Patent Classification code B31B 2150/00 is an indexing scheme that provides additional information for inventions related to making containers of paper, cardboard, or similar materials, enhancing the classification within this specific subgroup.
[B31B 2150/001] with square or cross bottom -- This CPC subclass covers processes for forming paper, cardboard or analogous material containers that incorporate a square or cross-shaped bottom, a detail of the bottom geometry used to provide stability and support. It falls under performing operations for making such containers within the broader category of making articles of paper or comparable material.
[B31B 2150/0012] having their openings facing in the direction of movement -- This CPC subgroup covers paper or cardboard containers such as boxes or cartons whose openings are oriented toward the direction in which the container will be moved or transported. The design facilitates loading, unloading, or dispensing by aligning the opening with the motion path. It is part of the hierarchy for making paper containers.
[B31B 2150/0014] having their openings facing transversally to the direction of movement -- This CPC subgroup covers paper or paper-like containers whose openings are positioned transversely to the direction in which the container moves, such as side-open boxes or tubes that are fed or conveyed lengthwise while the opening faces sideways.
[B31B 2150/0016] made from already formed bags -- The CPC class B31B 2150/0016 covers the production of paper, cardboard or analogous material containers that are formed by reusing already-manufactured bags as the starting material. It falls under the hierarchy of making containers from such materials, rather than from raw pulp.
[B31B 2150/002] by joining superimposed sheets, e.g. with separate bottom sheets -- This CPC group covers the manufacture of paper or cardboard containers in which the walls are formed by superimposing multiple sheets and bonding them together, often with a separate bottom sheet that is attached by a joining step such as gluing, welding or stitching.
[B31B 2150/003] made from tubular sheets -- B31B 2150/003 covers processes for making paper, cardboard or similar material containers by forming tubular sheets, including rolling, shaping and sealing to produce items such as tubes, cups or cans. It falls under the CPC hierarchy of Performing Operations → Making Articles of Paper, Cardboard or Material Worked in a Manner Analogous to Paper → Making Containers of Paper, Cardboard or Material Worked in a Manner Analogous to Paper.
[B31B 2150/10] the longitudinal axes of the containers being parallel to the direction in which the sheets or blanks are fed -- This CPC subclass concerns paper, cardboard or analogous-material containers whose longitudinal axis is aligned with the direction in which the sheet or blank is fed during production, covering items such as boxes, tubes or trays formed from a continuous web that travel lengthwise along the feed line.
[B31B 2150/20] the longitudinal axes of the containers being perpendicular to the direction in which the sheets or blanks are fed -- B31B 2150/20 covers the manufacture of paper, cardboard or analogous material containers in which the longitudinal axes of the containers run perpendicular to the direction the sheets or blanks are fed into the forming machine. This sub-group relates to processes that create the containers by forming them across the web rather than along the web direction.
[B31B 2155/00] Flexible containers made from webs -- Flexible containers made from webs are paper or analogous material bags, pouches or sacks formed by folding, sealing or joining a continuous web without a separate body. They are produced by shaping, cutting and bonding the web to create containers that can be filled, stored or transported.
[B31B 2155/001] by folding webs longitudinally -- B31B 2155/001 covers the manufacture of flexible containers such as boxes or tubes made from paper, cardboard or similar materials in which a web is folded lengthwise (longitudinally) to form the container shape, typically followed by sealing or joining steps. This subclass falls under the broader categories of performing operations, making articles of paper or analogous material, and specifically making paper containers.
[B31B 2155/0012] having their openings facing in the direction of movement -- This subclass pertains to flexible containers formed from paper, cardboard or similar web-based materials whose openings are oriented to face the direction of movement, such as forward-facing bags or pouches that allow contents to be dispensed or accessed as the container advances.
[B31B 2155/0014] having their openings facing transversally to the direction of movement -- This subclass covers flexible containers, such as bags or pouches, formed from a paper, cardboard or similar web, where the opening is situated across the width of the container and faces transversely to the direction the web moves during manufacture. It includes designs in which the flap or mouth of the container is perpendicular to the line of travel of the material as it is formed.
[B31B 2155/002] by joining superimposed webs, e.g. with separate bottom webs -- B31B 2155/002 covers flexible paper or analogous material containers produced by joining superimposed webs, often using a separate bottom web to form the container shape. It falls under the class for making containers of paper, cardboard or similar materials within the broader group of performing operations.
[B31B 2155/003] starting from tubular webs -- The subclass B31B 2155/003 covers methods for producing flexible paper, cardboard or similar containers that begin with a tubular web as the raw material. It includes operations in which the tubular web is formed, shaped or sealed to create the final container, fitting within the broader category of making containers from paper-like materials.
[B31B 2160/00] Shape of flexible containers -- The CPC code B31B 2160/00 relates to the shape of flexible containers made from paper, cardboard or similar sheet-forming materials. It covers inventions that define the geometry, folding, forming or overall configuration of bags, pouches and other pliable packaging items, focusing on how the container's shape is achieved and functions.
[B31B 2160/10] rectangular and flat, i.e. without structural provision for thickness of contents -- This subclass denotes flexible paper, cardboard or analogous containers that are rectangular and flat, meaning they lack any structural feature to accommodate a defined thickness of the product they hold. It applies to containers whose walls lie essentially in one plane and are intended for items that do not require a three-dimensional cavity.
[B31B 2160/102] obtained from essentially rectangular sheets -- The subclass B31B 2160/102 covers flexible containers made of paper, cardboard or analogous material that are formed from essentially rectangular sheets, where the container's shape results from the sheet's geometry and subsequent folding, joining or sealing.
[B31B 2160/104] obtained from rhombus shaped sheets -- B31B 2160/104 covers flexible containers whose shape is derived from rhombus-shaped sheets, such as boxes or bags made from paper or analogous material formed by folding or assembling sheets cut in a rhombus pattern.
[B31B 2160/106] obtained from sheets cut from larger sheets or webs before finishing the bag forming operations -- This subgroup covers methods for producing flexible paper, cardboard or similar containers in which the required shape is created by cutting individual pieces from larger sheets or continuous webs before the final bag-forming operations. It relates to the pre-forming stage of container manufacture, distinguishing it from processes that shape the material after it has been formed into a bag.
[B31B 2160/20] with structural provision for thickness of contents -- B31B 2160/20 covers flexible paper, cardboard or analogous containers that incorporate a structural feature to control the thickness of the material placed inside, such as internal ribs, stiffeners or reinforced zones. This provision helps maintain a defined volume or shape of the contents during handling, storage or use.
[B31B 2160/30] pointed or tapered -- B31B 2160/30 covers flexible paper, cardboard or analogous containers that have a pointed or tapered shape, such as funnels, spouts or elongated ends, used to direct flow or facilitate handling. It is a sub-category of making containers of paper, specifically addressing the geometry of flexible packaging.
[B31B 2170/00] Construction of flexible containers -- B31B 2170/00 covers the construction of flexible containers made from paper, cardboard, or similar sheet-like materials. It includes methods for shaping, joining, sealing and reinforcing such containers, such as bags, pouches, or collapsible boxes. The classification falls under making containers of paper or analogous material in the CPC hierarchy.
[B31B 2170/10] interconnected -- The B31B 2170/10 subclass pertains to flexible paper, cardboard or equivalent containers that are produced by interconnecting separate sections or compartments, forming a larger or composite container. It includes methods of joining, overlapping or fusing individual elements to create a continuous flexible container.
[B31B 2170/20] having multi-layered walls, e.g. laminated or lined -- The code B31B 2170/20 covers flexible paper, cardboard or analogous material containers whose walls consist of multiple layers, such as laminated or lined structures, providing enhanced strength, barrier properties or functionality. It falls under the subclass for making containers of paper, cardboard or similar materials within the broader field of performing operations and making articles of paper.
[B31B 2170/202] having liners applied in already made bags, e.g. including turning the bags inside out -- The CPC entry B31B 2170/202 covers techniques for adding a liner to a flexible paper, cardboard or analogous container after the bag has been formed, such as inserting the liner and turning the bag inside out to secure it. This includes processes where the liner is applied to an already-made bag rather than being incorporated during initial formation.
[B31B 2170/204] involving folding a web about an already tubular web -- This group covers methods of making flexible paper or analogous containers where a sheet of material is folded around an existing tubular web, forming a multi-layered structure such as a double-walled tube or a reinforced container. The process is used for producing cartons, tubes, and similar packaging.
[B31B 2170/30] having corrugated or pleated walls -- This subclass covers flexible paper or paper-like containers whose side walls are formed by corrugations or pleats, providing added stiffness and cushioning. It includes designs for boxes, cartons, or bags where the walls are ridged or folded rather than flat, enabling lightweight yet strong structures.
[B31B 2241/00] Making bags or boxes intended for a specific use -- The B31B 2241/00 subclass covers processes for producing paper, cardboard or analogous material bags and boxes that are shaped, cut, folded or joined for a particular purpose such as specific packaging, transport or storage applications. It falls under the broader category of making containers of paper, cardboard or material worked in a manner analogous to paper.
[B31B 2241/001] Making bottle carriers -- The B31B 2241/001 subclass covers the manufacture of carriers specifically designed to hold bottles, typically using paper, cardboard or similar materials. It includes processes and apparatus for forming, shaping and assembling such carriers, often intended for retail or distribution of beverage containers.
[B31B 2241/002] Making egg cartons -- B31B 2241/002 covers the manufacture of egg cartons, a specific type of container made from paper, cardboard or analogous materials. It falls under the CPC hierarchy for performing operations, making articles of paper, and making containers, specifically bags or boxes intended for a particular use.
[B31B 2241/003] Making cigarette boxes -- The code B31B 2241/003 covers processes for producing paper or cardboard containers specifically designed as cigarette boxes, including shaping, folding, joining, and finishing steps that create the final packaging. It falls under the broader category of making containers of paper, cardboard or analogous material.
[B31B 2241/005] Making paper bottles -- B31B 2241/005 covers the manufacture of containers shaped as bottles from paper, cardboard or similar fibrous material. It includes forming, shaping and assembling steps that produce a paper bottle intended for a specific use.
[B31B 2241/006] Making envelopes holding bar-shaped objects, e.g. cigar holders -- This CPC subclass covers processes for producing paper or cardboard envelopes designed to contain elongated, bar-shaped items such as cigar tubes, cigarette holders or similar products. The method includes shaping, folding and sealing the envelope to securely hold the object during handling, storage or transport.
[B31B 2241/007] Making recording disc envelopes -- The B31B 2241/007 entry concerns methods for producing envelopes or sleeves that house recorded discs such as CDs, DVDs or Blu-ray discs. It includes steps for cutting, folding, and sealing paper, cardboard or analogous material to form protective containers adapted to the disc shape and intended use. The classification falls within the broader group for making paper-based containers.
[B31B 2241/008] Making suction cleaner bags -- The subclass B31B 2241/008 covers the manufacture of suction cleaner bags, typically made from paper, cardboard or comparable materials, and includes steps such as forming, shaping, sealing and adding filter elements for use in vacuum or dust-collection devices. It falls under the CPC hierarchy for making containers of paper and analogues.
[B31B 2247/00] Manual operations for making bags or boxes -- B31B 2247/00 covers manual steps used in forming paper, cardboard or similar containers such as bags and boxes, including hand-folding, shaping, sealing and assembling operations performed without mechanised equipment. It falls under the broader class of performing operations for making paper-based articles and more specifically under making containers of paper or analogous materials.
[B31B 50/00] Making rigid or semi-rigid containers, e.g. boxes or cartons -- In this group, it is desirable to add the indexing codes of groups B31B2100/00 – B31B2120/00 .
[B31B 50/002] Prebreaking -- B31B 50/002 Prebreaking covers the preliminary breaking or cutting of sheet material before it is formed into rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers such as boxes and cartons. This step prepares the material for subsequent folding, scoring or assembling operations in the container-making process.
[B31B 50/003] Straightening the side walls of boxes; Squaring collapsed folded box blanks; Deforming boxes -- The CPC subclass B31B 50/003 relates to processes that straighten the side walls of paper or cardboard containers, restore collapsed folded box blanks to a square shape, and otherwise deform rigid or semi-rigid boxes to achieve proper geometry during manufacturing.
[B31B 50/004] Closing boxes -- B31B 50/004 covers the closure of rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers such as boxes and cartons. It includes devices, mechanisms and methods that secure the container by means such as latches, adhesives, tapes, fasteners or folding actions. The classification is used for patents relating to the final step of sealing or locking paper packaging.
[B31B 50/0042] the boxes having their opening facing in horizontal direction -- The CPC entry B31B 50/0042 falls under Performing Operations → Making Articles of Paper, Cardboard or Material Worked in a Manner Analogous to Paper → Making Containers of Paper, Cardboard or Material Worked in a Manner Analogous to Paper. It specifically relates to rigid or semi-rigid paper-based containers such as boxes or cartons whose opening is oriented horizontally.
[B31B 50/0044] the boxes having their opening facing upwardly -- The CPC subclass B31B 50/0044 refers to rigid or semi-rigid containers made of paper, cardboard or similar material whose opening faces upward. It includes boxes such as cartons or packaging designed for top-opening use, often for stacking or dispensing.
[B31B 50/0045] the boxes being cylindrical -- This subclass pertains to the manufacture of rigid or semi-rigid containers made of paper, cardboard or similar material that have a cylindrical shape, such as tubes, cans or drums, and includes the processes for forming, shaping, joining and finishing these cylindrical boxes for packaging, storage or transport.
[B31B 50/005] involving a particular layout of the machinery or relative arrangement of its subunits -- This subclass covers patents where the invention relates to the specific configuration or arrangement of equipment used in producing rigid or semi-rigid paper-based containers such as boxes or cartons, including the layout of machines or the relative positioning of their subunits.
[B31B 50/006] Controlling; Regulating; Measuring; Improving safety -- The CPC class B31B 50/006 covers techniques for controlling, regulating, measuring, or improving safety during the manufacture of rigid or semi-rigid containers made of paper, cardboard or analogous materials, such as boxes and cartons. It includes process monitoring, safety interlocks and quality-control devices applied to forming, cutting, folding or assembly steps.
[B31B 50/02] Feeding or positioning sheets, blanks or webs -- The B31B 50/02 entry pertains to the handling of sheets, blanks or webs in the production of rigid or semi-rigid paper containers such as boxes and cartons. It covers feeding, aligning, positioning or otherwise preparing the material for forming, folding or assembling steps in the manufacturing process.
[B31B 50/022] Holders for feeding or positioning blanks or webs -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Holders for the work piece.  Holders carrying feeding and guiding means.

[B31B 50/044] involving aligning -- The CPC subclass B31B 50/044 covers processes for producing rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers such as boxes and cartons that include an aligning step to position material or formed parts before further assembly or sealing.
[B31B 50/046] involving changing orientation or changing direction of transport -- B31B 50/046 covers processes for handling rigid or semi-rigid paper containers in which the orientation or transport direction of the articles is altered, such as turning, rotating, or re-orienting boxes and cartons during production, filling or packaging.
[B31B 50/06] from stacks -- B31B 50/06 covers the production of rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or equivalent-material containers such as boxes, cartons or other similar vessels, focusing on the manufacturing steps that form these containers from stacked material.
[B31B 50/062] from the underside of a magazine -- B31B 50/062 covers processes for producing rigid or semi-rigid paper or cardboard containers by using the underside of a magazine as the starting material, such as forming boxes or cartons directly from the magazine's back cover.
[B31B 50/064] by being moved in the plane they are lying in -- The CPC subclass B31B 50/064 refers to rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous material containers-such as boxes or cartons-that are moved while remaining in the plane on which they lie, i.e., transported horizontally without changing orientation.
[B31B 50/066] from above a magazine -- B31B 50/066 covers the step of forming rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers by feeding a stack of sheets (a magazine) from above and shaping it into boxes or cartons. [B31B 50/07] by air pressure or suction -- B31B 50/07 covers processes for forming rigid or semi-rigid containers from paper, cardboard or analogous material by using air pressure or suction, such as blowing or vacuum-forming blanks into boxes or cartons.

[B31B 50/102] using rolls, belts or chains -- B31B 50/102 relates to the manufacture of rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous material containers such as boxes or cartons, where the material is conveyed, shaped or processed by rolls, belts or chains.
[B31B 50/104] involving aligning -- This CPC sub-group covers methods for making rigid or semi-rigid paper or cardboard containers where aligning of the material or its components is part of the process, such as aligning panels, flaps or blanks before forming, folding, gluing or assembling boxes, cartons or similar containers.
[B31B 50/106] involving changing orientation or changing direction of transport -- This group covers methods of producing rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers in which the web or sheet is re-oriented or its transport direction is altered, such as turning, folding or redirecting the material during forming operations.
[B31B 50/12] by air pressure or suction -- This subclass covers shaping rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous material containers by applying air pressure or suction, such as vacuum-forming or pressurised molding processes used to produce boxes, cartons or similar packages.

[B31B 50/22] Notching -- Notching refers to cutting or forming notches in paper, cardboard or similar materials to enable folding, interlocking or opening of containers. It is a manufacturing step used in producing rigid or semi-rigid boxes, cartons and comparable packaging.

[B31B 50/256] using tools mounted on a drum -- B31B 50/256 covers methods of making rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers in which cutting, forming, embossing or other shaping tools are mounted on a rotating drum that contacts the web of material, enabling continuous or rotary processing to produce boxes, cartons or similar containers.
[B31B 50/26] Folding sheets, blanks or webs -- This subclass covers processes for forming rigid or semi-rigid paper containers by folding pre-cut sheets, blanks or continuous webs into the desired shape. [B31B 50/262] involving folding, leading, or trailing flaps of blanks -- This subclass covers processes for making rigid or semi-rigid paper containers in which the method involves folding, leading or trailing flaps of a paperboard blank, such as creating closure or reinforcement flaps for boxes or cartons. [B31B 50/28] around mandrels, e.g. for forming bottoms -- This subclass covers processes or devices in which paper or similar material is formed into rigid or semi-rigid containers by shaping the bottom portion around a mandrel. It relates to making boxes, cartons or similar containers where the bottom is produced by molding over a core.
[B31B 50/282] involving stripping-off formed boxes from mandrels -- B31B 50/282 relates to the step of stripping formed paper, cardboard or similar containers such as boxes or cartons from the mandrels on which they were shaped, encompassing methods for releasing rigid or semi-rigid containers after molding.
[B31B 50/30] the mandrels moving -- The subclass B31B 50/30 covers manufacturing steps in which mandrels, or shaping cores, are moved while forming rigid or semi-rigid containers such as boxes or cartons from paper, cardboard or analogous materials. It addresses the dynamic handling of these mandrels during the container-forming operation.
[B31B 50/32] in circular paths -- The code B31B 50/32 covers the manufacture of rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous material containers in which the material is shaped while moving along a circular path, such as rotary or spiral forming processes used for boxes, cartons and similar containers.
[B31B 50/322] the mandrels extending radially from the periphery of a drum -- The subclass covers apparatus in which mandrels project radially from the periphery of a rotating drum to shape, support or form paper, cardboard or analogous material during the production of rigid or semi-rigid containers such as boxes or cartons. It relates to methods of forming these containers by using the drum-mounted mandrels to define the container walls or seams.
[B31B 50/324] the mandrels being parallel to the axis of a drum -- The CPC subclass B31B 50/324 covers methods for forming rigid or semi-rigid paper or cardboard containers in which the mandrels used to shape the material are positioned parallel to the axis of a rotating drum, facilitating the production of boxes, cartons or similar containers.
[B31B 50/326] the mandrels extending tangentially to the periphery of a drum -- B31B 50/326 pertains to the use of mandrels that project tangentially from the outer edge of a rotating drum during the formation of rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or similar containers. The mandrels shape or support the material as it is wrapped around the drum, enabling the production of boxes, cartons or other container blanks. This subclass falls under the broader category of making containers from paper-type materials.
[B31B 50/34] about their own axes -- This classification code pertains to the manufacturing process of rigid or semi-rigid paper-based containers, specifically focusing on those that are made by rotating about their own axes. This includes techniques for forming boxes or cartons through rotational movements during production.
[B31B 50/36] by continuously feeding the sheets, blanks or webs to stationary members, e.g. plates, ploughs or cores -- This subclass covers processes for producing rigid or semi-rigid paper or cardboard containers such as boxes or cartons, where sheets, blanks or webs are continuously fed to stationary forming elements like plates, ploughs or cores.
[B31B 50/38] the members being forming-tubes -- This subclass covers the production of rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous material containers in which the individual members are formed as tubes. It includes methods for extruding or shaping tube sections that are subsequently cut, folded, joined or assembled into boxes, cartons or similar containers.
[B31B 50/40] acting internally -- The CPC subclass B31B 50/40 covers manufacturing steps where the interior of a rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous container is directly acted upon, such as internal shaping, folding, cutting, coating or forming of walls from within the container during production. It is a subcategory of making containers of paper analogues.
[B31B 50/42] acting externally -- B31B 50/42 covers external operations applied to rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers such as boxes and cartons, including processes like coating, printing, labeling, sealing or other treatments performed on the outside surface of the container. This subclass falls under the hierarchy for making paper-based containers within the Performing Operations section of the CPC.
[B31B 50/44] by plungers moving through folding dies -- This subclass covers methods of forming rigid or semi-rigid paper or cardboard containers such as boxes or cartons by using plungers that move through folding dies to shape and fold the material in a single operation.
[B31B 50/442] having several cooperating plungers and dies fitted on a rotating table or on moving chains -- The B31B 50/442 subclass covers forming rigid or semi-rigid paper or cardboard containers by using multiple plungers and dies that operate together on a rotating table or on moving chains, enabling continuous or semi-continuous production of boxes, cartons and similar containers.
[B31B 50/444] having several plungers moving in a closed path and cooperating with stationary folding dies -- The entry B31B 50/444 covers apparatus for making rigid or semi-rigid paper or cardboard containers that uses multiple plungers traveling in a closed loop to drive material against stationary folding dies, thereby forming boxes, cartons or similar containers. This mechanism coordinates the plungers' motion with the fixed dies to achieve successive folding steps in a continuous process.
[B31B 50/46] and interconnecting side walls -- B31B 50/46 covers the step of joining side walls of rigid or semi-rigid paper or cardboard containers, such as boxes or cartons, by means of folding, gluing, welding or other bonding techniques that interconnect the walls to form the container shape.
[B31B 50/48] by folding or tucking in locking flaps -- B31B 50/48 covers the manufacture of rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous material containers, such as boxes or cartons, by folding or tucking in locking flaps. It is a subclass of making paper containers within the broader performing-operations group for paper articles.
[B31B 50/50] by interengaging tongues and slots -- The CPC subclass B31B 50/50 covers making rigid or semi-rigid containers such as boxes or cartons from paper, cardboard or similar material where the parts are assembled by interengaging tongues and slots. It specifies methods that join the container walls through a snap-fit or mechanical lock without adhesives or separate fasteners.
[B31B 50/52] by reciprocating or oscillating members, e.g. fingers -- This CPC subclass covers processes for producing rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers in which the material is shaped by reciprocating or oscillating finger-like members, such as moving forming tools that fold, crease or press the sheet into a box or carton.
[B31B 50/54] operating on moving material -- The B31B 50/54 subgroup covers techniques for handling and processing a continuously moving web or sheet of paper, cardboard or similar material while it is being formed into rigid or semi-rigid containers such as boxes or cartons, including operations such as cutting, folding, sealing or printing performed on the material in motion.
[B31B 50/56] by rotary members co-operating with blades -- This subclass covers processes for forming rigid or semi-rigid paper containers using rotary tools that work together with cutting blades. It includes methods where a rotating member such as a drum or screw cooperates with blades to shape, cut, or separate the material into boxes, cartons, or similar containers.
[B31B 50/58] by moving endless belts -- B31B 50/58 covers a method for producing rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers in which the sheet material is conveyed and processed by one or more endless belts. The belts can transport, shape, fold, or assemble the material to form containers such as boxes or cartons during the manufacturing operation.
[B31B 50/585] by air jets -- B31B 50/585 describes a method of forming rigid or semi-rigid paper or cardboard containers, such as boxes or cartons, by using air jets to shape or weld the material. The technique falls under the CPC class for making containers of paper or analogous materials within the broader category of performing operations and making articles of paper.
[B31B 50/59] Shaping sheet material under pressure -- The subclass B31B 50/59 relates to processes that shape sheet material by applying pressure, for example molding or forming paper, cardboard or comparable substrates into rigid or semi-rigid containers such as boxes or cartons. It is part of the CPC group for making containers of paper-based materials.
[B31B 50/592] using punches or dies -- This subclass covers processes where punches or dies are employed to shape or cut paper, cardboard, or analogous materials into rigid or semi-rigid containers such as boxes or cartons. It falls under making containers of paper in the CPC hierarchy.
[B31B 50/594] Modifying the shape of tubular boxes or of paper bottle necks -- B31B 50/594 relates to processes that alter the geometry of tubular paper containers or the neck region of paper bottles, such as shaping, molding, tapering or cutting to achieve a desired profile. It covers equipment and methods for reshaping rigid or semi-rigid paper boxes and cartons.
[B31B 50/60] Uniting opposed surfaces or edges -- B31B 50/60 relates to techniques for joining opposite surfaces or edges of rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers such as boxes and cartons. It covers adhesives, heat sealing, folding, stitching or other mechanical means that create a sealed or reinforced joint.
[B31B 50/61] Uniting opposed edges by injecting thermoplastic material -- This subclass covers methods for sealing the opposite edges of paper or cardboard containers by injecting a thermoplastic resin into the joint, forming a solid bond that holds the edges together. It is used for producing rigid or semi-rigid boxes, cartons and similar containers.
[B31B 50/62] by adhesives -- The CPC code B31B 50/62 pertains to methods of forming rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers-such as boxes or cartons-by using adhesives to bond the material together. It falls under the broader categories of performing operations, making articles of paper or analogous material, and specifically making containers of that material.
[B31B 50/622] Applying glue on already formed boxes -- B31B 50/622 covers the step of applying glue to already formed paper or cardboard containers such as boxes or cartons. It falls under the CPC hierarchy for making rigid or semi-rigid paper containers, and addresses adhesive bonding of pre-shaped packaging before further processing or use.
[B31B 50/624] Applying glue on blanks -- This subclass covers methods of applying adhesive to pre-formed paper, cardboard or analogous blanks before they are folded or assembled into rigid or semi-rigid containers such as boxes or cartons, focusing on the gluing step in the packaging manufacturing process.
[B31B 50/626] Arrangements for permitting the glue to set -- The code B31B 50/626 relates to container-making processes in which the glue used to join paper, cardboard or analogous material is allowed to cure before handling. It covers arrangements such as holding, drying or immobilising the bonded parts to ensure the adhesive sets properly, typically applied to rigid or semi-rigid boxes, cartons and similar containers.
[B31B 50/64] by applying heat or pressure, e.g. by welding -- The subclass B31B 50/64 covers processes for making rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous material containers in which the parts are joined by applying heat or pressure, such as welding, to create sealed seams.
[B31B 50/642] using sealing jaws or sealing dies -- This subclass covers the sealing of paper, cardboard or similar containers by means of sealing jaws or sealing dies, where the jaws press together the edges or flaps to form a permanent seal. It applies to the manufacture of rigid or semi-rigid containers such as boxes and cartons.
[B31B 50/644] Making seals parallel to the direction of movement, i.e. longitudinal sealing -- This CPC subclass covers processes for sealing paper, cardboard or analogous material where the seal runs parallel to the direction of movement, creating longitudinal seams in rigid or semi-rigid containers such as boxes and cartons. It includes methods and equipment that apply heat, adhesive or other means to form continuous lengthwise seals.
[B31B 50/645] Making seals transversally to the direction of movement -- The subclass B31B 50/645 covers methods for sealing paper, cardboard or similar containers by applying a seal perpendicular to the material's travel direction. It is used for rigid or semi-rigid boxes, cartons or similar packages where a transverse seal joins flaps or panels during formation.
[B31B 50/648] using tools mounted on belts or chains -- The CPC subclass B31B 50/648 covers the manufacture of rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers-such as boxes or cartons-employing tools that are mounted on belts or chains to perform operations like cutting, folding or assembling. This classification falls under the broader group for making paper articles and specifically containers, indicating mechanised, continuous-process equipment as the principal means of production.
[B31B 50/649] using tools mounted on a drum -- The B31B 50/649 subclass relates to methods of producing rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers in which tools are mounted on a rotating drum to perform operations such as cutting, folding, scoring or gluing during the manufacturing process.
[B31B 50/66] by high-frequency electric heating -- This subclass covers methods of producing rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers such as boxes and cartons by applying high-frequency electric heating to shape or dry the material. It falls under manufacturing of paper articles, specifically container making, and addresses heating techniques that use radio-frequency energy.
[B31B 50/68] by stitching, stapling or riveting -- This subclass covers the manufacture of rigid or semi-rigid paper or cardboard containers, such as boxes or cartons, where the material is joined by stitching, stapling or riveting.
[B31B 50/682] for closing the bottom flaps of boxes, or for securing bottoms or caps to box bodies -- The subclass B31B 50/682 covers techniques or apparatus for closing the bottom flaps of paper or cardboard boxes, or for attaching bottoms or caps to the bodies of such containers, in the manufacture of rigid or semi-rigid paper packaging.
[B31B 50/684] for joining the overlapping edges of collapsed blanks to form tubular blanks -- This subclass covers methods and apparatus for bonding the overlapping edges of flattened paper, cardboard or analogous blanks after they have been collapsed, thereby forming a tubular blank that can be opened into a rigid or semi-rigid container such as a box or carton.
[B31B 50/686] for attaching hinged covers to boxes -- B31B 50/686 covers methods and devices for attaching hinged lids or covers to rigid or semi-rigid paper or cardboard containers such as boxes or cartons. It falls under the making containers of paper, cardboard or analogous material within the CPC hierarchy.
[B31B 50/70] by corner stapling -- The B31B 50/70 entry covers methods for producing rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers, such as boxes or cartons, by joining their corners with staples. Corner stapling secures the intersecting edges of the container walls, forming a stable structure without the need for adhesives or welding. This technique is used in the manufacturing of packaging where quick assembly and structural integrity are required.
[B31B 50/72] by applying and securing strips or sheets -- The subclass covers methods for forming rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers by applying and securing strips or sheets to create the container walls. Techniques include gluing, welding, stitching or other means of joining the sheet material to build boxes, cartons or similar packages.
[B31B 50/722] on already formed boxes -- The subclass concerns operations applied to containers that have already been shaped, such as rigid or semi-rigid boxes and cartons, for purposes such as joining, sealing, coating, printing, or otherwise modifying the pre-formed article.
[B31B 50/724] Applying tapes on the corners of set-up boxes, e.g. involving setting-up -- B31B 50/724 covers the step of applying tape to the corners of set-up paper or cardboard boxes, a method used to reinforce or seal the corners during assembly of rigid or semi-rigid containers such as cartons and boxes.
[B31B 50/726] for uniting meeting edges of collapsed boxes -- B31B 50/726 refers to techniques for joining the edges of a collapsed paper or cardboard container, such as a box or carton, so that it can be erected into a rigid or semi-rigid shape. The methods covered include adhesives, stitching, sealing, or other means of uniting the meeting edges of the flat blank before it is folded and assembled into a finished container. This subclass falls under making containers of paper-type materials.
[B31B 50/73] by mechanically interlocking integral parts, e.g. by tongues and slots -- This subgroup covers the manufacture of rigid or semi-rigid paper or cardboard containers by mechanically interlocking integral sections, for example using tongues, slots or similar fittings. The interlocking joins the parts without adhesives, relying on geometry to hold the container together.
[B31B 50/732] by folding or tucking-in locking flaps -- The B31B 50/732 subclass covers forming rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous material containers where the closure is achieved by folding or tucking-in locking flaps. It falls under the hierarchy of performing operations, making articles of paper or similar material, and specifically making containers such as boxes or cartons. This method secures the container walls without adhesives or separate fasteners.
[B31B 50/734] interengaging tongues and slots -- B31B 50/734 covers the use of interengaging tongues and slots in the construction of rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers such as boxes and cartons, describing how these complementary features lock together to secure the container walls.
[B31B 50/74] Auxiliary operations -- B31B 50/74 covers auxiliary operations used in the manufacture of rigid or semi-rigid paper containers such as boxes or cartons. It includes supporting steps like feeding, aligning, cutting, forming, or handling of sheet material that are performed in addition to the primary container-forming processes.
[B31B 50/741] Moistening; Drying; Cooling; Heating; Sterilizing -- The CPC subclass B31B 50/741 relates to methods used in producing rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers, such as boxes and cartons, where the focus is on applying moisture, drying, cooling, heating or sterilising steps. These operations modify the material's properties or ensure sanitary condition during or after formation.
[B31B 50/742] Coating; Impregnating; Waterproofing; Decoating -- B31B 50/742 relates to processes for treating paper, cardboard or analogous containers, specifically the application or removal of protective layers. The classification falls within the CPC group for making containers of paper-like materials.
[B31B 50/743] Coating or impregnating edges or corners -- The subclass B31B 50/743 covers methods of applying a coating or impregnation specifically to the edges or corners of rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers, such as boxes or cartons, to enhance properties like strength, moisture resistance or surface finish. This treatment is performed after the container is formed and may involve liquids, films or other agents applied only to the peripheral parts.
[B31B 50/745] Coating or impregnating formed boxes -- B31B 50/745 covers methods of applying a coating or impregnating pre-formed paper or cardboard containers such as boxes or cartons to impart properties like moisture resistance, strength or barrier functions. The subclass is part of the CPC group dealing with making containers of paper, cardboard or analogous materials.
[B31B 50/747] Coating or impregnating blanks or webs -- The subclass covers processes in which paper, cardboard or analogous sheets are coated with a layer or impregnated with a substance before being formed into rigid or semi-rigid containers such as boxes or cartons, including the application of adhesives, barrier films, functional or decorative coatings.
[B31B 50/75] by immersing in a bath -- This subclass covers processes for producing rigid or semi-rigid containers of paper, cardboard or analogous material by immersing a pre-formed web or pulp in a bath, allowing the shape to set before drying and finishing.
[B31B 50/753] by spraying -- The CPC code B31B 50/753 covers the manufacture of rigid or semi-rigid paper or cardboard containers such as boxes or cartons using a spraying method. It sits within the hierarchy of performing operations, making articles of paper or analogous material, and specifically making containers of that material.
[B31B 50/756] only the interior of the boxes -- B31B 50/756 concerns features that relate solely to the interior of rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers such as boxes or cartons. It includes arrangements, compartments, liners, inserts or other structural elements that affect the inside space, without covering the external shape or material of the container.
[B31B 50/76] Opening and distending flattened articles -- B31B 50/76 covers methods or devices for opening flattened paper, cardboard or analogous material containers and for expanding them into their three-dimensional shape, such as unsealing and unfolding boxes, cartons or similar rigid or semi-rigid packages. The classification applies to processes that transform a flat blank into a usable container.
[B31B 50/78] Mechanically -- B31B 50/78 pertains to the mechanical processes involved in making rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard, or analogous material containers, such as boxes or cartons. This classification covers specific machinery and methods used for shaping and forming these types of containers.
[B31B 50/782] by pushing the opposite ends of collapsed blanks towards each other -- The subclass B31B 50/782 describes a forming technique for rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous material containers in which a collapsed blank is shaped by pushing its opposite ends together, causing the edges to meet and lock, thereby creating a box, carton or similar container.
[B31B 50/784] for setting up boxes having their opening facing upwardly -- B31B 50/784 covers methods and devices for arranging rigid or semi-rigid paper or cardboard containers so that the box opening faces upward during set-up, typically used in packaging operations that fill the container from the top.
[B31B 50/786] by introducing opening fingers in the collapsed blanks -- B31B 50/786 covers a method of forming rigid or semi-rigid paper containers in which openings are created by cutting or forming fingers in the flattened blank before it is erected into a box or carton. The technique allows the container to be opened or expanded without additional tooling after folding.
[B31B 50/787] Rotating fingers; Two or more fingers moving relatively to each other -- The classification covers devices where two or more fingers rotate or move relative to each other to shape, fold, or transfer paper, cardboard or analogous material during production of rigid or semi-rigid containers such as boxes or cartons. It includes mechanisms that use rotating fingers to grip, bend or separate the web material.
[B31B 50/788] by introducing the blanks into undeformable holders, e.g. on a drum or on chains -- This CPC subgroup covers a method for producing rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers in which sheet blanks are placed into solid, non-deformable holders such as drums or chain-mounted fixtures before being formed into the final shape. The technique emphasizes the use of fixed carriers to guide the blanks during the shaping process.
[B31B 50/80] Pneumatically -- B31B 50/80 Pneumatically covers the use of air pressure or vacuum to shape, form, or assemble rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous material containers such as boxes or cartons. It includes blowing, inflating or suction techniques applied during the manufacturing process.
[B31B 50/802] for setting-up boxes having their opening facing upwardly -- This subclass deals with methods for assembling rigid or semi-rigid paper containers such as boxes or cartons where the opening is oriented upward during the setting-up step. It covers arranging flaps, folding, or forming the container so the lid or opening faces the top before sealing or filling.
[B31B 50/804] using two or more suction devices on a rotating element -- B31B 50/804 covers methods of forming rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous material containers in which two or more suction devices are applied to a rotating element to hold and shape the material during the forming process.
[B31B 50/81] Forming or attaching accessories, e.g. opening devices, closures or tear strings -- B31B 50/81 covers the processes for forming or attaching accessories to rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers, such as opening devices, closures, or tear strings, used in the manufacture of boxes, cartons and similar packaging. [B31B 50/811] Applying strips, strings, laces or ornamental edgings to formed boxes -- The subclass B31B 50/811 covers the step of attaching strips, strings, laces or decorative edgings to pre-formed paper, cardboard or analogous containers such as boxes or cartons, as part of the process for making rigid or semi-rigid packaging. This includes affixing ornamental trims that enhance the appearance or functionality of the finished container.
[B31B 50/812] Applying tabs, patches, strips or strings on blanks or webs -- The classification B31B 50/812 covers methods for attaching tabs, patches, strips or strings to sheet material or webs during the production of rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers such as boxes and cartons. It relates to the forming stage where these supplementary elements are applied to the blanks before they are shaped into containers.
[B31B 50/8121] Applying tabs on corners of box blanks -- The B31B 50/8121 class covers the step in paper or cardboard container production where tabs are applied to the corners of pre-cut box blanks to enable folding and securing the container shape, facilitating the creation of rigid or semi-rigid boxes and cartons. This operation is part of making containers from paper-based materials.
[B31B 50/8122] Applying patches -- The CPC subclass B31B 50/8122 covers the operation of affixing patches or reinforcement pieces to paper, cardboard or similar containers, typically to strengthen, seal or repair boxes, cartons or other rigid or semi-rigid paper packages. This step follows the formation of the container and precedes its final assembly.
[B31B 50/8123] the blanks remaining stationary during application of the patches -- A method for producing rigid or semi-rigid paper or cardboard containers in which the container blank is kept stationary while patches-such as printed, adhesive or reinforcing sections-are applied to its surface, typically to form handles, reinforcement or decorative areas.
[B31B 50/8124] the patches being taken out of a magazine -- This CPC subclass covers processes for extracting individual patches from a supply magazine and placing them into rigid or semi-rigid paper containers such as boxes or cartons, focusing on the handling and packaging of patch articles during manufacturing.
[B31B 50/8125] Applying strips or strings, e.g. tear strips or strings -- B31B 50/8125 classifies processes for making rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers that involve attaching strips or strings, such as tear-off strips or reinforcing strings, to the container during manufacture.
[B31B 50/8126] parallel to the direction of movement of the webs or the blanks -- B31B 50/8126 refers to the configuration of forming steps for rigid or semi-rigid paper containers in which any folding, cutting, creasing or other treatment of the web or blanks is arranged parallel to the direction in which the web moves through the machine. This orientation is used to produce boxes, cartons or similar containers during continuous web-based manufacturing.
[B31B 50/8127] perpendicular to the direction of movement of the webs or the blanks -- The code refers to methods of producing paper, cardboard or analogous containers in which actions such as cutting, creasing or folding are carried out at right angles to the web or blank travel direction, a typical arrangement in continuous box-making lines. This perpendicular orientation allows precise placement of features while the material moves forward.
[B31B 50/8128] the webs or blanks remaining stationary during application of the strips or strings -- This subclass covers processes for forming rigid or semi-rigid paper containers in which the main web or blank is held stationary while reinforcing strips, strings, or bands are applied to shape or strengthen the container. It pertains to the manufacturing stage where the base material does not move during the addition of the reinforcement elements.
[B31B 50/8129] the webs or blanks moving during application of the strips or strings -- The code B31B 50/8129 covers steps in which a paper or analogous web or blank is moving while strips, strings or similar banding are applied to it, typically to reinforce or seal the material during the formation of rigid or semi-rigid containers such as boxes or cartons. This is a sub-category of making paper containers in the CPC hierarchy.
[B31B 50/813] obliquely to the direction of movement of the webs or blanks or in an irregular path -- The code B31B 50/813 covers methods for forming rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers in which the web or blank is processed at an angle to its feed direction or follows a non-linear path, such as diagonal folding, skewed cutting or serpentine movement during box or carton manufacture.
[B31B 50/814] Applying closure elements to blanks, webs or boxes -- B31B 50/814 relates to methods for attaching closure elements such as lids, flaps, seals or fasteners to paper, cardboard or similar material blanks, webs or pre-formed boxes, enabling the creation of sealed rigid or semi-rigid containers. It includes adhesive bonding, mechanical fastening, heat sealing and other techniques for applying closures to packaged articles.
[B31B 50/8142] Applying button-and-string or washer like closure elements -- The subclass B31B 50/8142 covers processes for attaching button-and-string or washer-type closure elements to rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers such as boxes and cartons, including methods of securing these closures by mechanical fastening, adhesives or other means to seal the container.
[B31B 50/8144] Applying hook-and-loop-type fasteners -- This subclass describes methods for affixing hook-and-loop fasteners, such as Velcro-type strips, to paper, cardboard or analogous containers during or after their formation. [B31B 50/82] Forming or attaching windows -- B31B 50/82 pertains to the manufacture of rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous material containers in which a window-an opening that may be transparent, translucent or left empty-is formed or attached. [B31B 50/84] Forming or attaching means for filling or dispensing contents, e.g. valves or spouts -- B31B 50/84 covers devices that form or attach elements for filling or dispensing a container's contents, such as valves, spouts or other dispensing fittings, used in rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous containers.
[B31B 50/85] Applying patches or flexible valve inserts, e.g. applying film-like valves -- B31B 50/85 relates to the step of affixing patches or flexible valve inserts, such as film-like valves, onto rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or similar containers, enabling controlled flow or sealing functions in boxes, cartons or other paper-based packaging.
[B31B 50/86] Forming integral handles -- B31B 50/86 covers methods and apparatus for creating handles that are formed as an integral part of a rigid or semi-rigid paper, cardboard or analogous material container, such as boxes or cartons, without separate attachment. [B31B 50/87] Fitting separate handles on boxes, e.g. on drinking cups -- B31B 50/87 covers methods and devices for attaching separate handles to paper or cardboard containers such as boxes, cartons or drinking cups, enabling ergonomic gripping or hanging. [B31B 50/88] Printing -- B31B 50/88 relates to the printing of rigid or semi-rigid paper containers such as boxes, cartons or similar packages. [B31B 50/92] Delivering -- B31B 50/92 covers the delivery of rigid or semi-rigid paper containers such as boxes or cartons, including mechanisms for moving, conveying, or placing the containers after they are formed. [B31B 50/94] singly or in succession -- B31B 50/94 relates to methods for producing rigid or semi-rigid paper or cardboard containers where each container is formed individually or in a continuous sequence, such as cutting, folding and joining steps performed one after another.
[B31B 50/96] in an overlapping arrangement -- The CPC code B31B 50/96 relates to making rigid or semi-rigid containers of paper, cardboard or similar material in which the parts are arranged in an overlapping configuration, such as flaps that fold over one another to form boxes or cartons. It falls under the hierarchy of making containers of paper, cardboard or analogous material.
[B31B 50/98] in stacks or bundles -- This subclass concerns methods or apparatus for arranging rigid or semi-rigid paper containers, such as boxes or cartons, in stacked or bundled configurations for storage, transport, or handling. It includes techniques for forming, packing or securing multiple containers together as a unit.
[B31B 50/99] using hand tools -- B31B 50/99 covers the manufacture of rigid or semi-rigid paper-based containers such as boxes or cartons by means of hand tools. It is situated under performing operations, specifically making articles of paper, cardboard or analogous materials and then making containers from those materials. This subclass addresses manual processes used to shape and assemble the containers.
[B31B 70/00] Making flexible containers, e.g. envelopes or bags -- Processes or apparatus for making both flexible containers and rigid or semi-rigid containers are classified in group B31B50/00 . In this group, it is desirable to add the indexing codes of groups B31B2150/00 - B31B2170/00 .
[B31B 70/001] Shaping, other than by folding, sheet material under pressure -- The subclass B31B 70/001 covers methods for shaping sheet material, such as paper or cardboard, into flexible containers by applying pressure rather than folding, for example forming envelopes or bags. It is part of the broader group for making containers of paper, cardboard or analogous materials.
