It focuses on the arrangement of rollers, molds, feeding devices or other components that affect the forming process.
[B31B 70/006] Controlling; Regulating; Measuring; Safety measures -- The code refers to features integrated into flexible paper or cardboard containers that monitor or control internal conditions such as pressure, temperature, or flow, and include safety mechanisms like burst valves or tamper-evident closures. It covers sensors, regulators, and control apparatus designed specifically for paper-based packaging.

[B31C] MAKING WOUND ARTICLES, e.g. WOUND TUBES, OF PAPER, CARDBOARD OR MATERIAL WORKED IN A MANNER ANALOGOUS TO PAPER -- **Glossary:** - Winding: forming two or more complete convolutions - Wrapping: forming one convolution possibly with an additional overlap
[B31C 1/00] Making tubes or pipes by feeding at right angles to the winding mandrel centre line -- The B31C 1/00 subclass covers processes for producing tubular or pipe-like articles from paper, cardboard or analogous sheet material by winding the strip onto a mandrel while the material is introduced at a right angle to the mandrel's centre line. This feeding direction creates a uniform wall thickness and enables rapid fabrication of wound tubes or pipes.
[B31C 1/02] Machines therefor having additional mandrels -- It covers machines used to produce wound paper tubes where a second mandrel assists the winding, typically by introducing material perpendicular to the primary mandrel axis. The additional mandrel guides or supports the web as it is wound, enabling production of tubes with specific cross-sections or reinforced walls.
[B31C 1/04] and forming a tube end into a container bottom -- B31C 1/04 covers the production of paper or similar wound tubes in which the wound material is fed at right angles to the mandrel's centre line, and the tube's open end is subsequently shaped to form a bottom for a container. It applies to processes that create tubular articles such as tubes or pipes and then convert the tube end into a sealed container base.
[B31C 1/06] and inserting into a tube end a bottom to form a container -- This subclass deals with methods of forming paper or similar wound tubes in which a bottom piece is fitted into the tube end to create a closed container, such as a paper tube with a sealed base. [B31C 1/08] Accessories of machines therefor not otherwise provided for -- B31C 1/08 concerns auxiliary parts for winding machines that produce paper, cardboard or analogous material tubes or pipes, specifically when the material is introduced at a right angle to the axis of the winding mandrel. [B31C 1/083] Winding mandrels -- B31C 1/083 covers winding mandrels, the rotating forms on which paper, cardboard or analogous material is wound to produce tubes or pipes, particularly when the material is fed at right angles to the mandrel centre line.
[B31C 1/086] expansibles -- The subclass B31C 1/086 covers processes for producing expandable tubular articles, such as paper or cardboard tubes, by winding a web around a mandrel while feeding the material at right angles to the mandrel's centre line, enabling the finished tube to be expanded in diameter after manufacturing.
[B31C 11/00] Machinery for winding combined with other machinery -- B31C 11/00 covers machines that combine a winding function with other processing steps such as cutting, printing, laminating or shaping, for producing wound articles of paper, cardboard or analogous materials. These integrated systems form tubes, rolls or other wound products more efficiently by performing winding together with additional operations.
[B31C 11/02] for additionally shaping the articles -- B31C 11/02 covers machines that combine a winding unit with additional processing steps to shape paper, cardboard or analogous materials while they are being formed into wound articles such as tubes. The classification applies to integrated equipment that performs winding together with actions such as embossing, cutting or coating.
[B31C 11/04] for applying impregnating by coating-substances during the winding -- B31C 11/04 covers machines that integrate winding of paper, cardboard or analogous sheet material with the simultaneous application of impregnating or coating substances. The apparatus combines a coating delivery system and a winding mechanism to ensure uniform impregnation as the material is formed into tubes or rolls.
[B31C 11/06] for drying the wound and impregnated articles -- B31C 11/06 relates to machinery used for winding paper, cardboard or similar materials that also incorporates means for drying the wound and impregnated articles, typically as part of systems that produce wound tubes or similar products.
[B31C 3/00] Making tubes or pipes by feeding obliquely to the winding mandrel centre line -- B31C 3/00 relates to the manufacture of paper, cardboard or similar wound tubes and pipes where the web is introduced to the winding mandrel at an angle offset from the centre line, allowing helical or skewed winding to produce tubes with specific cross-sectional or mechanical properties.
[B31C 3/02] and inserting into a tube end a bottom to form a container -- B31C 3/02 covers the process of producing wound paper or similar tubular articles by feeding the strip obliquely to the winding mandrel's centre line, then placing a bottom piece into one end of the tube to create a closed container.
[B31C 3/04] Seam processing -- B31C 3/04 covers techniques for treating the seam of a wound paper or analogous tube, such as sealing, bonding, trimming, reinforcing or otherwise finishing the junction where the material overlaps during winding. These processes aim to improve the tube's mechanical integrity, impermeability or handling characteristics.
[B31C 5/00] Making tubes or pipes without using mandrels -- B31C 5/00 covers processes for producing tubular or pipe-like structures from paper, cardboard, or similar fibrous materials without the use of a mandrel. The method typically involves winding, shaping, or compressing the material to form a hollow tube, often followed by bonding or curing steps.
[B31C 7/00] Making conical articles by winding -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Forming conical paper articles by winding, e.g. winding blanks
[B31C 7/02] Forming truncated cones -- B31C 7/02 covers the process of forming truncated cones by winding paper, cardboard or similar sheet-like materials. The method creates conical or frustoconical articles such as wound tubes, where the material is wrapped around a mandrel and trimmed to the desired shape. This subclass falls under making wound articles of paper-type materials.
[B31C 7/04] on two or more mandrels -- The subclass B31C 7/04 covers winding processes in which the paper, cardboard or analogous material is wound around two or more mandrels, enabling the formation of conical or other shaped articles such as wound tubes. It pertains to methods that employ multiple mandrels to achieve the desired geometry.
[B31C 7/06] and inserting into a cone end a bottom to form a container -- The CPC subclass B31C 7/06 covers processes for producing conical paper or similar-material objects by winding a sheet into a tube and then attaching a bottom to the narrow end to create a container, such as a paper cup or similar wound vessel.
[B31C 7/08] Forming pointed cones -- The CPC subclass B31C 7/08 covers the production of pointed cone-shaped items formed by winding paper, cardboard or similar sheet material, such as conical tubes or other wound articles. It falls under the broader group for making wound articles of paper and analogous materials.
[B31C 7/10] on two or more mandrels -- The code refers to processes for producing wound articles of paper, cardboard or similar materials where the wound structure is formed simultaneously on two or more mandrels, allowing creation of multi-tube or conical shapes. It covers techniques for winding, shaping and bonding the material while mounted on multiple cores.
[B31C 9/00] Simultaneous forming of cylindrical and conical shapes by winding separate webs, e.g. forming bottles -- This classification covers processes that simultaneously wind separate webs to create an article having both cylindrical and conical sections, such as a paper-based bottle formed from multiple layers in a single operation. The method produces a composite shape by winding the webs together.
[B31C 99/00] Subject matter not provided for in other groups of this subclass -- The B31C 99/00 group covers processes for producing wound articles such as wound tubes made from paper, cardboard or other materials treated like paper, when the specific subject matter does not fall within any of the other groups of this subclass. It serves as a catch-all for winding operations that are not otherwise classified.
[B31D] MAKING ARTICLES OF PAPER, CARDBOARD OR MATERIAL WORKED IN A MANNER ANALOGOUS TO PAPER, NOT PROVIDED FOR IN SUBCLASSES -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Making, otherwise than by winding, of articles other than boxes, cartons, envelopes, bags, and tubes from paper, other than from paper pulp.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Manufacture by dry processes of articles made from particles or fibres consisting of wood or other lignocellulosic or like organic material -> B27N - Making layered products not composed wholly of paper or cardboard -> B32B - Making articles from cellulosic fibrous suspensions, e.g. wood pulp -> D21J

[B31D 2205/0017] Providing stock material in a particular form -- The subclass covers steps in which a sheet, web, or other stock of paper, cardboard or analogous material is supplied in a defined shape or configuration before further processing into a three-dimensional article. [B31D 2205/0023] as web from a roll -- The entry covers a step in a multistage method where a continuous web is produced by unwinding material from a roll, forming the basis for three-dimensional paper, cardboard or analogous articles. [B31D 2205/0029] unwound from inside -- The B31D 2205/0029 subclass covers processes in which a sheet or web of paper-like material is unwound from the interior of a preformed mass or tube to form a three-dimensional article. It includes multiple-step operations where the material is extracted from within a solid or rolled form and then shaped, rather than being cut or peeled from the outside surface. This method is used for producing items such as hollow tubes, containers, or other structures that require internal unwinding of the substrate.
[B31D 2205/0035] as fan folded web -- This subclass covers processes in which a continuous web of paper, cardboard or analogous material is folded back-and-forth in a fan-like pattern to create a three-dimensional article. [B31D 2205/0047] Feeding, guiding or shaping the material -- B31D 2205/0047 covers methods and apparatuses that feed, guide, or shape paper-like material during a multi-step process for producing three-dimensional articles. [B31D 2205/0052] Perforating -- B31D 2205/0052 covers methods of perforating paper, cardboard or similar sheet materials, typically as a step within multi-stage processes for producing three-dimensional articles such as filters, packaging components or decorative panels.
[B31D 2205/0058] Cutting -- Cutting refers to the operation of separating or shaping a paper, cardboard or analogous material by removing portions with a tool or machine, forming the final geometry of a three-dimensional article. In multi-step processes it follows earlier forming or bonding steps and may involve shearing, slicing, or laser-ablation to achieve the required dimensions.
[B31D 2205/0064] Stabilizing the shape of the final product, e.g. by mechanical interlocking -- Code B31D 2205/0064 pertains to multi-step processes for producing three-dimensional paper, cardboard or analogous articles in which the shape of the completed item is maintained, for example by introducing mechanical interlocking features or other stabilizing structures that prevent deformation during handling or use.
[B31D 2205/007] Delivering -- B31D 2205/007 defines the delivering step in multi-stage processes for producing three-dimensional items from paper, cardboard or analogous materials. [B31D 2205/0076] involving particular machinery details -- The subclass B31D 2205/0076 covers multi-step methods for producing three-dimensional objects from paper, cardboard or analogous sheet materials, where the protection is defined by particular machinery details such as specific machine components, arrangements or operating conditions. [B31D 3/00] Making articles of cellular structure, e.g. insulating board -- B31D 3/00 covers processes for producing articles that have a cellular structure, such as insulating board and similar porous materials. [B31D 3/002] Methods for making cellular structures; Cellular structures  B31D3/005  takes precedence -- B31D 3/002 covers methods for producing cellular articles such as insulating boards and other porous materials made from paper, cardboard or analogous substances, where the specific technique is not included in more detailed subclasses. The focus is on forming a cellular structure, typically by shaping, bonding or curing processes that generate a network of voids within the material. This subclass captures inventive steps for creating such cellular products that fall outside the narrower, predefined categories.
[B31D 3/005] Making cellular structures from corrugated webs or sheets -- B31D 3/005 covers processes for forming cellular structures, such as insulated panels or honeycomb cores, by using corrugated webs or sheets as the base material. It includes methods where the belt functions as a supporting, transporting or shaping element during forming, laminating, pressing or finishing operations.
[B31D 5/006] including controlled deformation of flat material, e.g. pleating, corrugating or embossing  including crumpling flat material  B31D5/0043 -- B31D 5/006 covers controlled deformation steps applied to flat sheet-like material-such as pleating, corrugating, embossing or crumpling-to convert it into three-dimensional shapes. It is used in multi-step processes for producing paper, cardboard or analogous articles where the deformation is not covered by more specific subclasses.
[B31D 5/0065] including slitting and expanding flat material -- B31D 5/0065 covers processes that transform a flat sheet of paper, cardboard or a similar material into a three-dimensional article by means of slitting, cutting or shaping the sheet followed by expanding it, such as by folding, pleating, inflating or otherwise enlarging the cut sections. This subclass captures multi-step techniques not allocated to more specific categories.
[B31D 5/0069] including forming or transforming three-dimensional material, e.g. corrugated webs or material of cellular structure  making articles of cellular structure  B31D3/00 , corrugating paper or cardboard  B31F1/20 -- B31D 5/0069 covers multi-step processes for producing three-dimensional paper-like articles, such as corrugated webs or cellular-structure materials. It includes forming or transforming the material to create items with a cellular or corrugated architecture, falling under the broader class of making paper, cardboard, or analogous materials.
[B31D 5/0073] including pillow forming -- **Glossary:** - Pillow: refers to an inflated pouch or to an array of inflated pouches
[B31D 5/0078] and filling with a material other than air or gas -- Covers multi-step methods for producing three-dimensional paper, cardboard or analogous material objects that are subsequently filled with a non-gaseous substance such as a liquid, paste, resin or solid fill. The filling step follows the shaping of the 3D article and may involve impregnation, injection or insertion of the material.

It focuses on shaping these sheets into three-dimensional filter structures, including steps like folding, pleating, bonding or forming that result in functional filtration products.

It includes successive operations such as forming, shaping, joining, sealing and finishing that together create a hollow object, and it applies when the specific method is not otherwise classified in narrower subclasses.

[B31F 1/00] Mechanical deformation without removing material, e.g. in combination with laminating -- The B31F 1/00 subclass covers operations that mechanically deform paper, cardboard or similar sheet materials without cutting away any portion, often in conjunction with laminating steps. It includes processes such as bending, crushing, embossing, folding or otherwise reshaping the material while preserving its entire mass. This classification is used for patents describing such deformation techniques in the production of paper-based articles.

It specifically addresses equipment used to shape the ends of tubes or similar forms without removing material. This falls under the broader class of mechanical working of paper, cardboard or analogous materials.

[B31F 1/0038] Rim-rolling -- Rim-rolling is a mechanical deformation method in which a sheet of paper, cardboard or similar material is passed over a rolling element that bends the peripheral edge without removing any material, often used together with laminating to produce curved or reinforced rims.

It falls under the broader category of mechanical working of paper-type materials.

[B31F 2201/00] Mechanical deformation of paper or cardboard without removing material -- This CPC subclass covers processes that reshape paper, cardboard or analogous sheet materials by applying mechanical forces such as bending, folding, creasing, pleating or embossing, where no part of the material is cut away or removed. It includes operations that deform the substrate while preserving its full thickness and composition.
[B31F 2201/07] Embossing -- B31F 2201/07 covers embossing, which is the mechanical deformation of paper, cardboard or similar sheet material to produce raised or recessed patterns without removing any material. The process forms decorative or functional textures by pressing the sheet against a shaped die or roller.
[B31F 2201/0702] by tools working discontinuously -- This subclass concerns mechanical deformation of paper, cardboard or analogous sheet material performed with tools that act discontinuously-such as intermittent presses, rollers, punches or stamping elements-and does not involve removal of material.
[B31F 2201/0705] Hand operated -- The CPC subclass B31F 2201/0705 covers manual, hand-operated techniques for mechanically deforming paper, cardboard or similar sheet material without cutting or removing any material. It includes actions such as pressing, folding, crumpling or otherwise shaping the substrate solely by human force, distinguishing it from powered or material-removing processes.
[B31F 2201/0707] by tools working continuously -- The code B31F 2201/0707 covers continuous mechanical deformation of paper, cardboard or similar sheet materials where material is not removed, performed by tools that operate continuously, such as rollers or belts, to shape, stretch or compress the web during processing.
[B31F 2201/0715] The tools being rollers -- The entry B31F 2201/0715 covers rollers used as tools for mechanically deforming paper, cardboard or analogous materials without removing any material, such as applying pressure, bending, creasing or compressing the web during processing.
[B31F 2201/0717] Methods and means for forming the embossments -- This subclass addresses processes and apparatuses that produce embossed patterns on paper, cardboard or analogous sheet materials by mechanically deforming the surface without removing any material. It includes rollers, dies, stamps and related equipment that press or shape the web to create raised or recessed designs during manufacturing.
[B31F 2201/072] Laser engraving -- B31F 2201/072 covers laser engraving of paper, cardboard or similar sheet material, where a focused laser beam creates markings or surface relief by locally heating and deforming the substrate without removing any material. It falls under mechanical working or deformation of paper within the CPC hierarchy for performing operations on paper articles.
[B31F 2201/0723] Characteristics of the rollers -- This subclass concerns the physical and functional attributes of rollers used in machines that mechanically deform paper or cardboard, such as diameter, surface texture, material, hardness, temperature control and speed settings that affect the deformation process.
[B31F 2201/0725] Hardness -- The CPC class B31F 2201/0725 covers the hardness characteristic of paper, cardboard or similar sheet materials when they are mechanically deformed without material removal. It relates to methods and devices that assess or specify the resistance of the sheet to indentation, compression or other deformation during processing. The entry falls under performing operations for making paper articles.
[B31F 2201/0728] Material -- The entry refers to the substrate - paper, cardboard or similar sheet materials - that is mechanically deformed during manufacturing operations that shape or bend the material without removing any portion of it. It is used in the CPC subclass for mechanical working of paper and analogues.
[B31F 2201/073] Rollers having a multilayered structure -- The code covers rollers used in paper or cardboard processing where the roller is built from multiple layers, each possibly differing in material or hardness, to provide specific mechanical deformation characteristics without material removal. These rollers are employed in calendering, smoothing, or shaping operations within paper manufacturing.
[B31F 2201/0733] Pattern -- The CPC subclass B31F 2201/0733 covers techniques for mechanically deforming paper, cardboard or analogous materials to impart a pattern, such as embossing or creasing, without removing any material from the sheet.
[B31F 2201/0735] Pattern inclined with respect to the axis of the roller -- The classification covers a mechanical deformation of paper or cardboard in which a patterned surface is formed on the material while it is pressed between rollers, and the pattern is set at an angle to the roller's axis rather than being parallel. This inclined pattern is achieved without removing any material from the sheet.
[B31F 2201/0738] Cross sectional profile of the embossments -- The code B31F 2201/0738 covers the cross-sectional profile of embossments created when paper, cardboard or similar material is mechanically deformed without material removal. It specifies the shape of raised or indented patterns formed by embossing processes.
[B31F 2201/0741] Roller cooperating with a non-even counter roller -- This subclass covers devices where a roller works together with a counter-roller whose surface is not uniformly smooth, used to deform paper, cardboard or analogous material without cutting or removing any material. The non-even counter-roller can be ribbed, toothed or otherwise patterned to impart folds, creases or shaping during a continuous mechanical process.
[B31F 2201/0743] having a matching profile -- B31F 2201/0743 covers processes that mechanically deform paper, cardboard or analogous sheet material without removing any material, producing a shape that matches a predetermined profile.
[B31F 2201/0746] and having a self-centering profile -- B31F 2201/0746 relates to mechanical deformation of paper or cardboard where no material is removed, using a self-centering profile that automatically aligns the sheet during the operation. The feature ensures consistent deformation without manual positioning, fitting within the CPC hierarchy for making paper articles.
[B31F 2201/0748] having a dissimilar profile -- This subgroup covers processes that mechanically deform paper, cardboard or analogous sheet material so that the resulting cross-section has a shape different from the original, such as corrugating, embossing or pleating that produces a non-uniform profile.
[B31F 2201/0751] and having a self-centering profile -- This CPC subclass is part of the Performing Operations group, under Making Articles of Paper, Cardboard or Material Worked in a Manner Analogous to Paper, and specifically Mechanical Working or Deformation of Paper, Cardboard or Material Worked in a Manner Analogous to Paper. It covers mechanical deformation of paper or cardboard without removing material, using a tool or die that incorporates a self-centering profile to maintain consistent alignment during the process.
[B31F 2201/0753] Roller supporting, positioning, driving means -- The subclass B31F 2201/0753 covers devices that support, position, or drive rollers used in the mechanical deformation of paper, cardboard or analogous materials without removing material. These mechanisms ensure proper alignment and transmission of force during processes such as embossing, folding or compressing.
[B31F 2201/0754] The tools being other than rollers, e.g. belts or plates -- B31F 2201/0754 covers the mechanical deformation of paper, cardboard or analogous materials where material is not removed and the tooling employed is other than rollers, for example belts or plates.
[B31F 2201/0756] Characteristics of the incoming material, e.g. creped, embossed, corrugated -- B31F 2201/0756 addresses the properties of the paper, cardboard or analogous material supplied to a mechanical deformation step that does not remove material, such as its creped, embossed or corrugated structure. These material characteristics influence how the sheet behaves during subsequent shaping, folding or other non-cutting operations.
[B31F 2201/0758] Characteristics of the embossed product -- The subclass B31F 2201/0758 covers patents that describe the physical attributes of embossed paper or cardboard items, such as relief depth, pattern geometry, surface texture and overall shape resulting from mechanical deformation that does not remove material. It is used to classify inventions dealing with the characteristics of the embossed product itself.
[B31F 2201/0761] Multi-layered -- Covers methods for producing multi-layered paper, cardboard or analogous material by mechanically deforming the substrate without removing any material, such as lamination, folding or other deformation processes that create layered structures.
[B31F 2201/0764] the layers being nested -- B31F 2201/0764 covers processes where sheets of paper, cardboard or analogous material are mechanically deformed by nesting layers together without cutting or removing any part of the material. The technique is used to create composite structures or improve stiffness by interleaving the layers.
[B31F 2201/0766] the layers being superposed tip to tip -- This sub-group covers methods where sheets or layers of paper-like material are stacked tip-to-tip, creating a superposed tip arrangement without removing any material, typically in mechanical deformation operations such as folding, pleating or compressing.
[B31F 2201/0769] the layers being shifted -- This CPC subclass concerns mechanical deformation of paper, cardboard or analogous sheet materials by shifting their internal layers relative to each other, without cutting or removing any material. The method creates thickness variation, pleats or texture while preserving the sheet's overall mass.
[B31F 2201/0771] Other aspects of the embossing operations -- The subclass B31F 2201/0771 covers additional features of embossing processes applied to paper, cardboard or similar sheet material where the web is deformed without any material being removed. It includes the design of embossing patterns, tool configurations, pressure settings and other operational parameters that influence the raised or recessed relief created on the sheet.
[B31F 2201/0774] Multiple successive embossing operations -- An entry in the Cooperative Patent Classification for paper-working processes, specifically B31F 2201/0774, covers multiple successive embossing operations. It describes a method in which a sheet of paper or cardboard undergoes two or more sequential embossing steps, each mechanically deforming the material without removing any substance, to create complex patterns or improve physical properties. This falls under the broader categories of performing operations, making paper articles, and mechanical deformation of paper.
[B31F 2201/0776] Exchanging embossing tools -- B31F 2201/0776 covers the exchange of embossing tools in machines that mechanically deform paper, cardboard or analogous materials without removing material. It includes mechanisms or procedures for replacing, repositioning or switching embossing plates, rollers or other pattern-forming devices during embossing operations, allowing rapid pattern changes in the production of embossed sheets.
[B31F 2201/0779] Control -- B31F 2201/0779 pertains to control measures applied during mechanical deformation of paper, cardboard or similar materials where no material is removed. It covers the monitoring, regulation and feedback systems that ensure precise shaping, folding or embossing operations within the broader category of mechanical working of paper.
[B31F 2201/0782] Layout of the complete embossing machine, of the embossing line -- The entry B31F 2201/0782 concerns the overall arrangement and design of an embossing machine or complete embossing line used to mechanically deform paper, cardboard or similar sheet material without removing any material. It covers the spatial layout of the equipment, feed systems, rollers and supporting structures that together perform the embossing operation.
[B31F 2201/0784] Auxiliary operations -- The code B31F 2201/0784, titled Auxiliary operations, pertains to additional actions carried out while mechanically deforming paper, cardboard or similar sheet material, where no material is removed. It includes operations such as feeding, positioning, supporting or conditioning the sheet during processes like creasing, folding or embossing.
[B31F 2201/0787] Applying adhesive -- The subclass B31F 2201/0787 covers the step of applying an adhesive to paper, cardboard or analogous sheet material during a mechanical deformation operation that does not remove material. It includes methods where glue is used to join layers, reinforce surfaces or create composite structures while the substrate is being pressed, folded or otherwise shaped.
[B31F 2201/0789] Joining plies without adhesive -- B31F 2201/0789 covers techniques for bonding two or more plies of paper, cardboard or analogous sheet material without the use of adhesives, relying on mechanical deformation, pressure, heat or interlocking to create a permanent joint. It is situated in the CPC hierarchy under mechanical working or deformation of paper and cardboard.
[B31F 2201/0792] Printing -- B31F 2201/0792 refers to printing operations that modify the surface of paper, cardboard or analogous sheet material by mechanically deforming it without cutting or removing any portion. The method uses pressure or embossing to create images or text, falling under the CPC group for mechanical working of paper without material removal. It is part of the broader category of performing operations for making articles of paper.
[B31F 2201/0794] Cutting -- B31F 2201/0794 covers cutting operations applied to paper, cardboard or analogous sheet materials as part of mechanical working. It includes methods that use knives, shears, laser or other tools to separate or shape the sheet by removing material. The code falls under the hierarchy of performing operations, making articles of paper, and mechanical deformation without material removal, but specifically addresses the removal step.
[B31F 2201/0797] Perforating -- Perforating is the mechanical operation that creates a pattern of openings or holes in paper, cardboard or comparable sheet material, usually by punching, drilling or stamping. The process deforms the material to form the apertures without separating large sections, facilitating binding, ventilation, or decorative functions.
[B31F 5/00] Attaching together sheets, strips or webs -- This subclass deals with methods and apparatus for joining separate sheets, strips or webs of paper, cardboard or similar fibrous materials. It covers mechanical techniques such as stitching, stapling, welding, adhesive bonding, or interlocking of the sheets to produce a composite article, without altering the material's fundamental composition.
[B31F 5/001] by stapling or riveting -- The subclass B31F 5/001 covers methods for joining sheets, strips or webs of paper, cardboard or analogous materials by mechanically fastening them with staples or rivets, whereby the fastener penetrates the layers and locks them together. It is applied in the production of bonded paper products such as books, packaging, or composite panels.
[B31F 5/003] by stitching -- The CPC subclass B31F 5/003 pertains to the mechanical joining of sheets, strips or webs of paper, cardboard or analogous material by stitching, using thread, needle or similar means to interlace the pieces. This method falls under the broader category of mechanical working or deformation of paper-type materials.
[B31F 5/005] by folding  rim-rolling  B31F1/0041 -- B31F 5/005 pertains to the process of attaching paper or cardboard sheets, strips, or webs together through specific techniques such as folding and rim-rolling, which are detailed under B31F 1/0041. [B31F 5/006] using a strip, e.g. profiled  B31F5/06  takes precedence -- The subclass B31F 5/006 covers methods of joining sheets, strips or webs of paper, cardboard or analogous materials by applying a separate strip-often a profiled one-as the fastening element. [B31F 5/02] by crimping or slotting -- B31F 5/02 relates to the mechanical joining of sheets, strips or webs of paper, cardboard or analogous materials by forming crimps or slots that interlock the layers. The technique secures the parts without adhesives, staples or stitching, relying on deformation of the material to create a permanent connection.
[B31F 5/022] using a rotary tool -- B31F 5/022 covers the use of a rotary tool to join or fasten sheets, strips or webs of paper, cardboard or analogous materials. It is a specific method within the mechanical working of paper subclass, which itself falls under the broader category of making articles of paper.
[B31F 5/025] by slotting -- The subclass covers methods of joining sheets, strips or webs by forming slots in one or more of the materials so that complementary tongues, projections or other elements can be inserted to secure the parts together. It is a specific technique of mechanical working or deformation of paper, cardboard or analogous material used for attaching components.
[B31F 5/027] by perforating, e.g. by folding over the partially cut part -- This CPC subclass covers methods of joining paper, cardboard or analogous materials where the connection is formed by making perforations and then folding over the partially cut portion to secure the sheets. It falls under mechanical working and deformation of paper, specifically for attaching sheets, strips or webs.
[B31F 5/04] by exclusive use of adhesives -- This subclass covers processes that join sheets, strips or webs of paper, cardboard or analogous materials solely by applying adhesives, without any mechanical fasteners or deformation. It is a specific method within the broader category of mechanical working or deformation of paper for making articles of paper, cardboard or similar material.
[B31F 5/06] by adhesive tape -- The subclass B31F 5/06 covers methods of joining sheets, strips or webs by applying adhesive tape, typically in processes for making paper, cardboard or similar materials. It includes the use of tape to bond layers without mechanical fasteners, providing a simple means of attachment in mechanical working or deformation operations.
[B31F 5/08] for reinforcing edges -- B31F 5/08 deals with methods of reinforcing the edges of paper, cardboard or comparable sheet material when they are joined together as sheets, strips or webs. It includes edge sealing, binding or strengthening techniques to improve durability during mechanical working or deformation.
[B31F 5/085] combined with folding the strip around the edge, or applying an already folded strip on  folding edges  B31F1/0016 ,  B31F1/0029 -- This subclass covers methods that join sheets, strips or webs by folding a strip around an edge or by applying a pre-folded strip onto a folding edge, typically in the mechanical deformation of paper-like materials.
[B31F 7/00] Processes not otherwise provided for -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes for working paper not provided for in B31B50/00 , B31B70/00 , B31C1/00 - B31C99/00 , B31D1/00 - B31D5/00 , B31F1/00 - B31F5/00 .
[B31F 7/002] tubular articles, e.g. changing the cross-section -- This subclass covers processes for forming or reshaping tubular articles made from paper, cardboard or analogous materials, particularly operations that alter the cross-section of the tube and are not covered by more specific subclasses.

It includes forming, shaping and joining steps that result in a continuous or segmented tube.
[B31F 7/006] edges, e.g. sheet edges -- This subgroup deals with methods for forming, treating, or finishing edges of sheets of paper, cardboard or similar materials, such as trimming, rounding, reinforcing or otherwise shaping sheet edges. It includes operations not covered elsewhere in the mechanical working of paper.
[B31F 7/008] Repairing -- This subclass pertains to processes for repairing paper, cardboard or comparable sheet materials, employing mechanical working or deformation methods that are not otherwise specified. It includes techniques that restore strength, shape or functionality to damaged articles.
[B31F 7/02] Breaking coatings, e.g. on paper or cardboard -- B31F 7/02 covers processes for mechanically breaking or removing surface coatings from paper, cardboard or analogous sheet materials, such as peeling, scraping or cracking of varnishes, inks or laminates. The methods are applied when no more specific subclass is available, and they are classified under performing operations for making paper articles, specifically mechanical working or deformation of the material.
[B32] LAYERED PRODUCTS -- B32 groups patents concerning layered products such as laminates, composites and stratified structures, focusing on their manufacture, treatment and use. It covers processes for forming, bonding, coating or otherwise creating multilayered items and the resulting material characteristics. The class falls under the broader "Performing Operations" section of the CPC.
[B32B] LAYERED PRODUCTS, i.e. PRODUCTS BUILT-UP OF STRATA OF FLAT OR NON-FLAT, e.g. CELLULAR OR HONEYCOMB, FORM -- **Definition:** This place covers:  **Glossary:** - Adhesive: Substance applied in any state or in any manner that has bonding properties. - Coating: A coating in the sense of B32B is obtained by processes such as: (A) Brushing, flowing, spraying, dipping or doctor blading a solution or dispersion; (B) Sputtering, vapour/plasma/vacuum depositing; (C) Deposition of loose particles or fibres, e.g. by sprinkling, flocking, air laying; and (D) Deposition of fibres/pulp/particles in a wet slurry as in paper making (wet laying). Coatings are not considered defined B32B layers (see definition of Layer below). - Discontinuous layer: A layer formed of separate pieces of material having both a physical discontinuity and a continuous path through each of its major directions (e.g. x and y, or length and width). Examples include a grating, a honeycomb, a frame, or separate pieces of material that are juxtaposed side-by-side. Examples of discontinuous layers are as follows: - Embedded layer: A layer that is set, surrounded, enveloped, or enclosed in an impregnating material, mass of plastic or similar substance that penetrates and/or lies on side edges of the layer. - Fibrous layer: Random assembly of fibres or filaments, usually of limited length, e.g. felt or fleece, the fibres being interengaged or connected, e.g. by adhesive. - Filamentary layer: Layer of threads, filaments, tapes or ribbons of any substance (including wires) of more or less unlimited length secured together; it may be, e.g. woven, knitted, braided, netted, spunbonded, or formed of threads or filaments crossed or laid side by side and bonded together. - Film: Within B32B , a film that is formed by extrusion or moulding or that is formed as a self-supporting transfer coating is a layer. A film that is formed in-situ by coating is not considered to be a layer within the scope of B32B . - Impregnated layer: A layer that is at least partially filled by a material and has been obtained by permeating or saturating at least a part of the layer with a liquid substance, e.g. dispersions, uncured polymer, melted or molten polymer, glass, metals, settable compositions. - Juxtaposed side-by-side: In direct contact or with a bonding material, e.g. adhesive or mortar, in between. - Laminating: Laminating is the action of combining previously unconnected, but possibly laid up, layers to become one product whose layers will remain together. - Lay-up: Lay-up is the action of combining separate layers, one on top of the other, in order to form a half-product for entering the laminating process. - Layer: Sheet, strip or stratum having a small thickness relative to its other dimensions. It may be deformed out of the flat plane to form a three-dimensional shape; it may or may not be homogeneous or cohesive; it may be an assembly of fibres or pieces of material. It may be discontinuous, e.g. in the form of a grating or a honeycomb. It may or may not be in complete contact with the next layer, e.g. a corrugated layer against a flat layer. The layer has to have one of the following forms: (1) Preformed layer, i.e. taking the form of a layer at some stage before being brought into combination with another layer; (2) Layer formed in-situ, i.e. taking the form of a layer while or after being brought into combination with another layer. Additional explanations of (1) Preformed layer and (2) Layer formed in-situ are located following the Glossary of Terms. In B32B , with the exception of B32B15/01 - B32B15/018 and interlayers/composite interlayers proper for B32B17/10005 - B32B17/1099 , the following is excluded from the definition of a layer: A coating formed directly onto a substrate layer, which at the moment of its contact with the substrate does not have the form of a layer (unless the coating falls within the definition of (2) Layer formed in-situ as further explained below after the Glossary of Terms). - Layered product: Product comprising at least two superposed layers secured together; the term "secured" is to be interpreted broadly to include any method of uniting or securing the layers, e.g. needling, stitching, gluing, nailing, dovetailing, welding or the interposition of an adhesive or adhesive-impregnated support. Products wherein layers are obtained by co-extrusion or by simultaneous injection moulding of materials are included in this definition. It also encompasses two layers of ceramic powders that are pressed together in a press. It may also be an intermediate stage in the production of an article which is not layered in its final form, e.g. a panel with a protective layer that is stripped off when the panel is placed in its position of use. It is normally of substantially uniform thickness overall, i.e. ignoring local variations such as are produced by a corrugated face layer. The layered product may be in the form of an article, e.g. a container. - Next to: With no other layer being interposed. - Partial laminating: Partial laminating occurs (1) when one layer does not fully cover a surface of another layer, whereby the layer with the greater surface area is laminated on only part of its surface, or (2) when two coextensive layers are bonded on only part of their facing surfaces. - Particulate layer: Preformed layer of particles, e.g. chips, powder, granules, flakes, in which the particles are bonded together, e.g. sintered or by a binder. - Spaced fabric: A fabric that includes at least two outer fabrics joined together by connecting yarns that create an intermediate gap between the outer fabrics, to form a three-dimensional fabric. The spaced fabric can be a single layer or multiple layers. (1) A spaced fabric is considered a single layer for B32B when woven or knit fabrics are produced in a single step wherein the yarns simultaneously form a fabric that comprises outer plies with middle connecting (spacer) yarns. (2) A spaced fabric is considered to include multiple layers for B32B when the fabric is made from at least two preformed fabrics that are joined together with connecting yarns to create a laminate structure with a space between the outer fabrics.
