[B32B 11/00] Layered products comprising bituminous or tarry substances -- B32B 11/00 relates to the preparation and characteristics of multilayered articles that contain bituminous or tar-like materials, such as roofing felt, bitumen-impregnated board or laminated sheets. The classification covers processes for forming, treating and joining the layers and the resulting composite products.
[B32B 11/02] with fibres or particles -- B32B 11/02 relates to layered products made of bituminous or tar-like materials that incorporate fibers or particulate additives to reinforce the structure. The classification covers manufacturing methods and compositions where these reinforcements improve mechanical strength, durability, or functional performance of honeycomb, cellular or other stratified builds.
[B32B 11/04] comprising such substance as the main or only constituent of a layer, next to another layer of a -- B32B 11/04 covers layered products in which one stratum is formed principally or wholly from a bituminous or tarry material and is positioned next to another layer of a different composition, such as in roofing sheets, flooring panels or composite panels that combine a bitumen-rich layer with a structural or protective layer.
[B32B 11/042] of wood -- This classification entry pertains to layered products that include bituminous or tarry substances, specifically when one of the layers is made of wood. It falls under the broader category of performing operations and manufacturing processes for layered products with flat or non-flat structures.
[B32B 11/044] of natural rubber or synthetic rubber -- This subclass covers processes for producing layered products whose layers are made of natural rubber or synthetic rubber, including forming, laminating, shaping or treating the rubber into sheets, honeycomb or cellular structures. It is situated under the CPC group for layered products formed from bituminous or tarry substances.
[B32B 11/046] of synthetic resin -- B32B 11/046 covers layered products that are formed from synthetic resin, including those incorporating bituminous or tarry substances. It pertains to articles built up of flat or non-flat strata such as cellular or honeycomb structures where the binder or matrix is a synthetic polymer. These products are classified under the broader group of layered products within the performing operations section.
[B32B 11/048] of foam -- This classification entry pertains to layered products that include foam layers combined with bituminous or tarry substances, typically used in construction and insulation applications.
[B32B 11/06] of paper or cardboard -- A B32B 11/06 product is a layered construction in which paper or cardboard sheets are combined with or coated by bituminous or tarry substances, forming waterproof or protective boards. These may include tar-impregnated cardboard used for roofing, packaging, or insulation, where the flat or non-flat strata provide strength and the bituminous layer supplies moisture resistance.
[B32B 11/08] of metal -- B32B 11/08 pertains to layered products where one of the layers is made of metal and another layer comprises bituminous or tarry substances. This classification is used for materials that combine metallic components with bitumen or tar, often for applications requiring both structural integrity and waterproofing properties.
[B32B 11/10] next to a fibrous or filamentary layer -- The B32B 11/10 subclass covers layered products that contain bituminous or tarry substances positioned adjacent to a fibrous or filamentary layer, such as a fabric or non-woven mat, forming a composite structure where the polymeric or tar-based coating is applied directly onto the textile backing. This includes methods for bonding, curing or otherwise integrating the bituminous layer with the fibrous substrate.
[B32B 11/12] next to a particulate layer -- B32B 11/12 covers processes for producing layered products that contain bituminous or tarry substances where a particulate layer is applied adjacent to another layer. The invention relates to depositing, spreading or embedding a powder, granules or other discrete particles next to a continuous bituminous sheet to create a composite structure. Such methods are used in roofing, insulation or protective coatings.
[B32B 13/00] Layered products comprising a water-setting substance, e.g. concrete, plaster, asbestos cement, or like builders' material -- B32B 13/00 relates to layered building products that are formed from a water-setting binder such as concrete, plaster, asbestos cement or similar materials, where the final item consists of stacked strata that may be flat, cellular, honeycomb or other non-flat forms used in construction.
[B32B 13/02] with fibres or particles -- Subclass B32B 13/02 covers layered building materials such as concrete, plaster or asbestos-cement that set with water and are reinforced or filled with fibers, particles or other additives. It addresses the composition of the strata where the reinforcement is incorporated into the material to improve mechanical properties or other performance characteristics.
[B32B 13/04] comprising such substance as the main or only constituent of a layer, next to another layer of a -- This subclass covers layered products in which a water-setting material such as concrete, plaster, asbestos-cement or similar binder forms the main or sole constituent of one layer that is placed next to another layer of a different material, forming composite or sandwich structures used in construction and prefabricated building elements.
[B32B 13/042] of natural rubber or synthetic rubber -- B32B 13/042 covers layered building products that contain a water-setting binder such as concrete or plaster in which natural rubber or synthetic rubber is incorporated. The rubber component is used to impart flexibility, impact resistance or waterproofing to the stratified structure. This subclass falls under the broader group of layered products built from flat or non-flat strata.
[B32B 13/045] of foam -- This classification entry pertains to layered products that include a water-setting substance such as concrete or plaster, specifically focusing on those containing foam. It is part of the broader category of performing operations and layered products in the Cooperative Patent Classification system used by the EPO and USPTO.
[B32B 13/047] made of particles -- B32B 13/047 covers layered building products that are formed from a water-setting binder and consist essentially of discrete particles such as sand, gravel, or aggregates. The particles are incorporated into the fresh mixture and become locked in the hardened strata, producing concrete, plaster, or similar composites with a stratified structure. This subclass is used to classify processes and products where the particle-based composition is a defining feature.
[B32B 13/06] of metal -- This subclass concerns layered building products that use a water-setting binder such as concrete, plaster, asbestos cement or similar materials and incorporate metal within the layers, for example as reinforcement, facing or metallic inserts.
[B32B 13/08] of paper or cardboard -- B32B 13/08 covers layered building products that contain a water-setting binder (such as concrete, plaster or asbestos cement) and use paper or cardboard as one of the constituent layers, typically as facing, reinforcement or formwork material. The classification applies to constructions where the paper or cardboard contributes to the structural or protective performance of the composite.
[B32B 13/10] of wood
[B32B 13/12] of synthetic resin -- The subclass B32B 13/12 covers layered products in which a water-setting material such as concrete, plaster or asbestos-cement incorporates a synthetic resin as the binding agent, producing resin-based building composites. It includes methods and compositions for forming strata of flat or non-flat layers using these resin-modified materials.
[B32B 13/14] next to a fibrous or filamentary layer -- B32B 13/14 relates to methods for forming layered products in which a water-setting material such as concrete, plaster or similar is placed directly adjacent to a fibrous or filamentary layer, for example a reinforcement textile or fiber mat. The subclass covers the preparation, bonding and curing steps that create a composite structure combining the water-setting matrix with the fibrous layer.
[B32B 15/00] Layered products comprising metal -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Layered products characterised by having a continuous or discontinuous metal layer.
[B32B 15/01] all layers being exclusively metallic -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Layered products with all layers being metallic in the form of sheets/plates, distinct layers. They can be made by any possible method such as roll bonding, cladding, brazing, coating etc.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Making layered metal workpieces by pressure cladding -> B23K20/22 - Making coatings with a metallic material characterised by its composition -> C23C30/00
[B32B 15/011] all layers being formed of iron alloys or steels -- B32B 15/011 pertains to layered products whose layers are all formed from iron alloys or steels, such as metal honeycomb or cellular structures built entirely of these materials. It is classified under performing operations on layered products, specifically the subgroup for metal layered products.
[B32B 15/012] one layer being formed of an iron alloy or steel, another layer being formed of aluminium or an aluminium alloy -- The CPC subclass B32B 15/012 pertains to layered products built from alternating strata where at least one layer consists of an iron alloy or steel and another layer is made of aluminium or an aluminium alloy, covering metallic sandwich or composite structures.
[B32B 15/013] one layer being formed of an iron alloy or steel, another layer being formed of a metal other than iron or aluminium -- This CPC subclass covers metallic layered products in which at least one stratum is an iron alloy or steel while an adjoining stratum is a different metal, excluding aluminium. It applies to bimetallic or multimetal sheets, clads and sandwich structures produced for engineering and structural uses.
[B32B 15/015] the said other metal being copper or nickel or an alloy thereof -- B32B 15/015 concerns the production of layered metal products where the additional metal used is copper, nickel or an alloy of either, typically in honeycomb or cellular structures. It falls under the CPC heading for layered products comprising metal.
[B32B 15/016] all layers being formed of aluminium or aluminium alloys -- This CPC subclass covers layered metal products in which every stratum is made of aluminium or aluminium alloys, including flat or non-flat configurations such as honeycomb or cellular structures built from these materials.
[B32B 15/017] one layer being formed of aluminium or an aluminium alloy, another layer being formed of an alloy based on a non ferrous metal other than aluminium -- B32B 15/017 pertains to metal-based layered products in which one stratum consists of aluminium or an aluminium alloy while an adjacent stratum is made from a different non-ferrous metal alloy, excluding aluminium. This subclass falls under the broader grouping of layered products composed of metal.
[B32B 15/018] one layer being formed of a noble metal or a noble metal alloy -- The CPC entry B32B 15/018 covers layered metal products in which a single stratum is made of a noble metal or a noble-metal alloy such as gold, silver, platinum or their mixtures. This applies to honeycomb, cellular or other multi-layer structures where the noble-metal layer provides specific properties like corrosion resistance, conductivity or decorative appearance.
[B32B 15/02] Layer formed of wires, e.g. mesh -- This CPC subclass concerns metal layered products whose layer is a mesh made from interlaced wires. It is part of the performing operations group for layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures.
[B32B 15/04] comprising metal as the main or only constituent of a layer, next to another layer of a -- The subclass B32B 15/04 covers layered products in which a metal layer, forming the main or sole constituent of that stratum, is placed adjacent to another layer of a different material. It includes metal-based layers bonded to or combined with non-metal layers such as polymers, ceramics, or composites to create a stratified structure. This classification is used for processes and products where metal serves as a primary constituent in a multilayer composition.
[B32B 15/043] of metal  B32B15/01  takes precedence -- This classification entry pertains to layered products where at least one layer is made of metal. It specifies that when classifying such items, the code B32B 15/01 should be given priority if applicable.
[B32B 15/046] of foam -- B32B 15/046 pertains to layered products where one or more layers consist of metallic foam. This classification is part of the Cooperative Patent Classification system used by the European Patent Office and the United States Patent and Trademark Office for categorizing patent documents.
[B32B 15/06] of rubber -- B32B 15/06 pertains to metal-based layered products that include rubber, covering structures such as metal-rubber laminates, honeycomb cores or sandwich panels where rubber layers are bonded to metal strata. It falls under CPC section B for chemistry-metallurgy, subclass B32B for layered products, and the 15 group for those comprising metal, with 06 specifying the rubber component.
[B32B 15/08] of synthetic resin -- B32B 15/08 pertains to layered metal structures in which a synthetic resin is incorporated, such as metal honeycomb or cellular cores that are impregnated, coated or bonded with polymeric material to form composite panels, sandwich constructions or reinforced sheets. This subclass covers the manufacturing, treatment and use of such metal-resin layered products.
[B32B 15/082] comprising vinyl resins -- A B32B 15/082 layered product is a metal-based honeycomb, cellular or other stratified structure that incorporates vinyl-type resins as a binding or coating component. The vinyl resin may be used to improve adhesion, corrosion resistance or mechanical performance of the metal layers, enabling lightweight sandwich panels and similar composites.
[B32B 15/085] comprising polyolefins -- The CPC subclass B32B 15/085 covers metal-based layered products that incorporate polyolefin materials, such as honeycomb or cellular structures where polyolefin films, foils or powders are bonded to or sandwiched between metal strata. It pertains to the manufacture and design of such composite panels used in automotive, aerospace, or construction applications.
[B32B 15/088] comprising polyamides -- B32B 15/088 classifies metal-based layered products that include polyamide components, such as polyamide interlayers, coatings or laminates incorporated within the metal strata. It is a sub-category of layered products made of metal, covering manufacturing methods and structures where polyamides are combined with metal to achieve specific mechanical or protective properties.
[B32B 15/09] comprising polyesters -- B32B 15/09 covers metal-based layered products that incorporate polyester layers, such as metal-polyester laminates or sandwich structures where polyester films or resins are bonded to metal sheets. The entry pertains to preparation, bonding methods and characteristics of these composite metal products within the broader class of layered products.
[B32B 15/092] comprising epoxy resins -- The CPC entry B32B 15/092 covers metal-based layered products-such as honeycomb, cellular or other strata-formed structures-that incorporate epoxy resins within the layers. It pertains to the design, manufacture or use of these metal-epoxy composites for structural or functional purposes.
[B32B 15/095] comprising polyurethanes -- B32B 15/095 refers to layered products that combine metal with polyurethanes, such as sandwich panels, honeycomb or cellular structures where polyurethane layers are bonded to, impregnated in or fill metal sheets. The code covers both the manufacturing processes and the finished articles in which the polyurethane provides cushioning, insulation or structural reinforcement within the metal framework.
[B32B 15/098] comprising condensation resins of aldehydes, e.g. with phenols, ureas or melamines -- Layered metal products that include condensation resins derived from aldehydes, such as phenolic, urea or melamine based binders, are used to bond or coat the metal strata. These resins improve mechanical strength, thermal stability, or fire resistance of honeycomb or cellular metal structures.
[B32B 15/10] of wood
[B32B 15/12] of paper or cardboard -- B32B 15/12 covers the manufacture of metal-based layered products that incorporate paper or cardboard sheets, such as metal-clad paper, composite panels, or sandwich structures where a paper or cardboard core is bonded between metal layers. It includes processes for bonding, laminating, or otherwise joining these dissimilar materials to create flexible or rigid composites.
[B32B 15/14] next to a fibrous or filamentary layer -- This CPC subclass covers metal-based laminated structures where a metallic layer is bonded directly to a fibrous or filamentary layer, such as metal-reinforced fabrics, metal-plastic composites, or metal-paper laminates. It falls under layered products in the performing operations section of the CPC.
[B32B 15/16] next to a particulate layer -- B32B 15/16 covers methods for producing layered metal products where a solid metal layer is formed adjacent to a particulate layer, such as powders, granules or beads. It is applied to processes that create composite structures with alternating metal and particulate strata, including honeycomb, cellular or other non-flat configurations.
[B32B 15/18] comprising iron or steel -- The CPC subclass B32B 15/18 covers layered products, such as cellular or honeycomb structures, that are manufactured from iron or steel. It lies within the "layered products, comprising metal" branch of the Performing Operations section, specifying metal-based stratified forms.
[B32B 15/20] comprising aluminium or copper -- The CPC subclass B32B 15/20 covers layered metal products that are constructed from aluminium or copper, such as sandwich panels, honeycomb cores or cellular structures made of these metals. It pertains to the design and manufacture of flat or shaped stratified components using aluminium or copper as the constituent material.
[B32B 17/00] Layered products essentially comprising sheet glass, or glass, slag, or like fibres -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Layered products comprising:  **Glossary:** - Laminated safety glass or glazing, safety glazing, laminated glazing: Inorganic glass layer in sheet form bonded to another inorganic glass layer in sheet form or to a durable polymeric sheet or film via a resin interlayer, and wherein the interlayer keeps the laminated safety glass or glazing bonded even when struck or broken, preventing the glass from shattering. - Interlayer: An internal layer of thermoplastic polymer bonding the components of a laminated safety glass or glazing to one another. - Intermediate layer, intermediate film: An internal layer or film used as a barrier or as a carrier for functional layers and not having adhesive properties. - Plasticiser: Organic compound which reduces the glass transition temperature of the interlayer, usually an interlayer of PVB. - Glazing: A transparent closure of an opening such as the glass of a window. - Composite interlayer: A composite laminate that binds the inorganic glass layer to another inorganic glass layer or the durable polymeric sheet or film of the laminated safety glass or glazing. The composite interlayer comprises at least one interlayer and may also comprise an intermediate layer and/or a functional layer.
[B32B 17/02] in the form of fibres or filaments -- B32B 17/02 covers the manufacture of layered products such as glass, slag or similar fibre-based structures when they are produced as individual fibres or filaments. It pertains to processes that form flat or non-flat strata in filament form, typical for glass-fiber or honeycomb-type materials.
[B32B 17/04] bonded with or embedded in a plastic substance -- The subclass B32B 17/04 covers layered products such as glass, slag or fibre sheets that are bonded to or embedded in a plastic matrix, forming composite panels or structures. It addresses methods and materials for joining the strata with plastics to create reinforced, insulated or protective assemblies.
[B32B 17/06] comprising glass as the main or only constituent of a layer, next to another layer of a specific -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Layered products comprising an inorganic glass layer in sheet or film form next to another layer of generic material.  The layers need not be permanently secured, such as a releasable protective layer.
[B32B 17/061] of metal -- B32B 17/061 pertains to layered products that primarily consist of sheet glass or similar fibers, with a specific focus on those incorporating metal layers. This classification is part of the Cooperative Patent Classification system used by the European Patent Office and the United States Patent and Trademark Office.
[B32B 17/062] of wood -- The subclass B32B 17/062 covers the production of layered products in which the constituent strata are wood, such as plywood, laminated board or veneer assemblies. It includes manufacturing methods that bond, laminate or otherwise join flat or shaped wood layers to form a composite structure. This entry falls under the broader category of layered products built from flat or non-flat strata.
[B32B 17/063] of rubber -- B32B 17/063 designates methods for manufacturing layered articles where rubber forms the primary matrix, including sheet, honeycomb or cellular structures that may incorporate glass, slag or similar fibres. The classification applies to processes that produce multi-strata rubber products used in sealing, insulation or cushioning applications.
[B32B 17/065] of paper or cardboard -- B32B 17/065 classifies layered products whose constituent sheets are paper or cardboard, including sandwich panels, laminated boards and other multi-layer structures built from these fibrous sheets used in packaging, construction, etc. The subclass falls under the broader group for layered products made of glass, slag or similar fibres, and pertains to manufacturing processes that produce flat or non-flat stratified items from paper-based materials.
[B32B 17/066] of foam -- B32B 17/066 covers layered products that consist of a foam core or foam layers, such as honeycomb or cellular structures formed from foam materials, used in construction of composite sheets or panels. This subclass falls under the broader group of layered products built from sheets of glass, slag, fibres or similar, where the foam provides the internal stratum.
[B32B 17/067] of fibres or filaments -- B32B 17/067 covers layered products, such as honeycomb or cellular structures, that are formed primarily from fibers or filaments, including glass, slag or similar material strands. The classification addresses the manufacture and design of these stratified assemblies where the individual layers consist of fibrous or filamentous elements.
[B32B 17/068] of particles -- B32B 17/068 pertains to layered products that primarily consist of sheet glass or similar fibers, specifically focusing on those incorporating particles. This classification is part of the Cooperative Patent Classification system used by the European Patent Office and the United States Patent and Trademark Office.
[B32B 17/069] of intumescent material  B32B17/10311  takes precedence -- This classification entry pertains to layered products that primarily consist of sheet glass or similar fibers, specifically those incorporating an intumescent material layer. However, if the product also falls under the more specific category of having a cellular or honeycomb structure, it should be classified under B32B17/10311 instead.
[B32B 17/08] of cellulosic plastic substance -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Layered products comprising inorganic glass in sheet or film form next to a layer of a cellulose derivative or gelatin as polymeric substance.
[B32B 17/10] of synthetic resin -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Layered products comprising at least one inorganic glass layer in sheet or film form next to a layer of synthetic resin; the synthetic resin layer can be used as a glue layer to bond the glass layer with another glass layer or another material layer or can be used as a removable protective film.
[B32B 17/10005] laminated safety glass or glazing -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Layered products comprising at least one inorganic glass layer in sheet form next to a layer of synthetic resin; wherein the glass sheet is permanently bonded to at least one further glass layer in sheet form or a durable polymeric sheet or film via the layer of synthetic resin as a resin interlayer, and wherein the interlayer keeps the laminated safety glass or glazing bonded even when struck or broken, preventing the glass from shattering.  **Glossary:** - Laminated safety glass or glazing, safety glazing, laminated glazing: Inorganic glass layer in sheet form bonded to another inorganic glass layer in sheet form or to a durable polymeric sheet or film via a resin interlayer, and wherein the interlayer keeps the laminated safety glass or glazing bonded even when struck or broken, preventing the glass from shattering. - Interlayer: An internal layer of thermoplastic polymer bonding the components of a laminated safety glass or glazing to one another. - Intermediate layer, intermediate film: An internal layer or film used as a barrier or as a carrier for functional layers and not having adhesive properties. - Plasticiser: Organic compound which reduces the glass transition temperature of the interlayer, usually an interlayer of PVB. - Composite interlayer: A composite laminate that binds the inorganic glass layer to another inorganic glass layer or the durable polymeric sheet or film of the laminated safety glass or glazing. The composite interlayer comprises at least one interlayer and may also comprise an intermediate layer and/or a functional layer.
[B32B 17/10009] characterized by the number, the constitution or treatment of glass sheets -- This CPC subclass covers layered products where the defining feature is the number of glass sheets, their composition, or the way they are treated such as annealing, coating, or laminating. It applies to products built of flat or non-flat glass strata, including honeycomb or cellular structures.
[B32B 17/10018] comprising only one glass sheet -- This subgroup covers layered products that consist solely of a single glass sheet, without additional layers such as foams, honeycomb cores or other laminates. It applies to methods and devices that produce or use a product formed from one flat glass element.
[B32B 17/10027] the glass sheet not being an outer layer -- This CPC subclass covers layered products in which a glass sheet is used as an internal component rather than the outer surface, including multi-layer composites, sandwich panels, honeycomb or cellular structures where glass is embedded within other materials.
[B32B 17/10036] comprising two outer glass sheets -- B32B 17/10036 defines layered products that consist of two outer glass sheets bonded together, often with an intermediate core such as air, foam or another material. This subclass belongs to the CPC group for performing operations on sheet glass and similar laminated structures.
[B32B 17/10045] with at least one intermediate layer consisting of a glass sheet -- The subclass B32B 17/10045 covers layered products that incorporate at least one intermediate layer made of a glass sheet. It applies to composites such as laminated glass, honeycomb structures or sandwich panels where a glass sheet is positioned between other strata, typically of glass, slag, fibers or similar flat or non-flat materials. This entry falls under the broader category of layered products built from multiple strata.
[B32B 17/10055] with at least one intermediate air space -- B32B 17/10055 covers layered products such as sheet glass, glass fibre or slag that are built up from multiple strata and contain at least one internal air cavity. The classification applies to structures where the air space is incorporated between layers to provide reduced weight, insulation or structural benefits.
[B32B 17/10064] comprising at least two glass sheets, only one of which being an outer layer -- The CPC subclass B32B 17/10064 concerns layered glass constructions made from at least two glass sheets where only a single sheet forms the outer surface, such as laminated or protective glazing panels. It is located under performing operations for layered products built from flat or non-flat strata, specifically those comprising sheet glass or similar fibre materials.
[B32B 17/10073] comprising at least two glass sheets, neither of which being an outer layer -- B32B 17/10073 classifies layered products that consist of at least two glass sheets arranged as internal strata, with no sheet serving as the outer surface. The code falls under the CPC hierarchy of Performing Operations → Layered Products → Layered products, i.e. products built-up of flat or non-flat strata such as cellular or honeycomb forms, specifically covering constructions where the glass layers are wholly enclosed within the product.
[B32B 17/10082] Properties of the bulk of a glass sheet -- This subclass covers the measurement, analysis and description of intrinsic bulk characteristics of glass sheets, such as thickness, density, thermal conductivity, mechanical strength, optical transmission and chemical resistance, without reference to surface treatments or coatings. It applies to products built from flat or non-flat strata like honeycomb or cellular glass where the bulk properties determine performance.
[B32B 17/10091] thermally hardened -- B32B 17/10091 covers layered products such as sheet glass, glass-slag or fibre structures that undergo a thermal hardening step to improve strength or stability. It falls under performing operations for layered products built from flat or non-flat strata.
[B32B 17/101] having a predetermined coefficient of thermal expansion [CTE] -- This subclass covers layered glass or glass-like products that are manufactured so the overall coefficient of thermal expansion is set to a specified value. It includes methods such as material selection, compositional adjustment, or post-treatments to achieve a predetermined CTE, ensuring dimensional stability during temperature changes.
[B32B 17/1011] having predetermined tint or excitation purity -- This subclass addresses glass or similar sheet products that are manufactured with a specific colour tint or a defined excitation-purity level, ensuring consistent optical properties such as hue, transmission or fluorescence across the material.
[B32B 17/10119] having a composition deviating from the basic composition of soda-lime glass, e.g. borosilicate -- B32B 17/10119 covers layered glass products whose constituent glass differs from the usual soda-lime composition, such as borosilicate or other specialized glass formulations. The classification applies to multi-layer structures, including cellular or honeycomb forms, made from these modified glasses.
[B32B 17/10128] Treatment of at least one glass sheet -- B32B 17/10128 covers methods and apparatus for treating one or more glass sheets, such as cleaning, surface modification, coating, tempering or strengthening, that are used as layers in composite structures.
[B32B 17/10137] Chemical strengthening -- B32B 17/10137 covers the chemical strengthening of layered products, such as sheet glass, glass, slag or fibre-based composites, where the material is built from flat or non-flat strata and its strength is enhanced by chemical treatment.
[B32B 17/10146] Face treatment, e.g. etching, grinding or sand blasting -- This CPC subclass covers methods for treating the surface of layered products such as sheet glass, glass-fibre, slag or similar stratified materials. It includes operations like etching, grinding and sand-blasting applied to the face of these products, falling under performing operations on layered products.
[B32B 17/10155] Edge treatment or chamfering -- The subclass B32B 17/10155 covers methods for treating the edges of layered products such as sheet glass, slag or fibre-reinforced sheets, including honeycomb or cellular structures. It includes operations like chamfering, beveling, rounding or otherwise finishing edges to improve handling, assembly or performance.
[B32B 17/10165] Functional features of the laminated safety glass or glazing -- B32B 17/10165 classifies functional features of laminated safety glass or glazing, a type of layered product where sheets of glass are bonded with interlayers such as polymer films. The entry covers aspects that affect performance, including impact resistance, breakage behavior, acoustic damping, UV filtering and other safety-related properties of the laminated assembly.
[B32B 17/10174] Coatings of a metallic or dielectric material on a constituent layer of glass or polymer -- This subclass covers processes for applying metallic or dielectric coatings onto a specific layer within a laminated structure that includes glass or polymer sheets. It includes methods such as sputtering, chemical vapor deposition, or electroplating that form functional surfaces on the individual strata. Used for protective, decorative, or electrical purposes in layered products.
[B32B 17/10183] being not continuous, e.g. in edge regions -- This subclass deals with layered products such as sheet glass, glass fibre or slag that are intentionally non-continuous, typically in edge zones where the layers are broken, spaced or terminated. It includes designs where the stratified structure is interrupted to modify mechanical, optical or thermal properties.
[B32B 17/10192] patterned in the form of columns or grids -- The CPC code B32B 17/10192 covers layered products-such as sheet glass, glass-slag or fiber panels-that feature a surface pattern formed by columns or grid-like structures. This subclass specifies the arrangement of the material into regular, repeating columnar or grid patterns, typically used to impart aesthetic or functional properties to the layered sheet.
[B32B 17/10201] Dielectric coatings -- This subclass concerns dielectric coating layers applied to sheet glass, slag or fibrous sheets, forming insulating or protective films. It covers processes for depositing inorganic or organic insulating layers on flat-or-shaped substrates within the layered products group.
[B32B 17/10211] Doped dielectric layer, electrically conductive, e.g. SnO 2 :F -- B32B 17/10211 covers a doped dielectric layer that conducts electricity, exemplified by fluorine-doped tin-oxide coatings applied to glass, slag or fibrous sheets in layered structures such as honeycomb or cellular panels. The classification falls within CPC section B32B for layered products and specifies conductive oxide films that combine dielectric and conductive functions.
[B32B 17/1022] Metallic coatings -- B32B 17/1022 covers the application of metallic coatings to layered products, such as sheet glass, glass-based materials, slag, or fiber structures, where the product consists of stacked flat or non-flat strata. This falls under the broader categories of performing operations and layered products within the Cooperative Patent Classification system.
[B32B 17/10229] Metallic layers sandwiched by dielectric layers -- The entry B32B 17/10229 defines layered products that consist of alternating metallic sheets and dielectric (insulating) layers, forming a composite structure such as metal-dielectric laminates used in electronic, optical or protective applications. It covers the design, manufacture and properties of these metal-dielectric stacks.
[B32B 17/10238] in the form of particles -- The subclass B32B 17/10238 covers layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures that are produced from individual particles rather than continuous sheets. It includes materials like glass, slag or fiber particles that are assembled into a stratified form to create a bulk product with a layered internal geometry.
[B32B 17/10247] Laminated safety glass or glazing containing decorations or patterns for aesthetic reasons  containing metal wires for aesthetic reasons  B32B17/10422 -- This classification entry pertains to laminated safety glass or glazing that includes decorations or patterns for aesthetic purposes, specifically those containing metal wires for visual effect. It is part of a broader category dealing with layered products made from sheet glass or similar fibrous materials.
[B32B 17/10256] created by printing techniques -- B32B 17/10256 pertains to the manufacture of layered glass, slag or similar fibre sheets in which the stratified structure is produced by printing techniques, such as ink-jet, screen or digital printing, to deposit or pattern material layers and form the final laminated product.
[B32B 17/10266] on glass pane -- The classification refers to inventions concerning layered products where the primary component is a glass pane, such as laminated or composite glass structures, including processes for producing or treating such panes. It falls under layered products built of flat or non-flat strata, specifically those essentially comprising sheet glass or glass-based fibres.
[B32B 17/10275] on interlayer -- The code B32B 17/10275 classifies technologies related to interlayers used in layered products such as laminated glass, glass-fiber composites, or honeycomb structures. It covers the materials, adhesives, and methods for inserting or bonding an intermediate layer between sheets to improve strength, safety, or functional properties.
[B32B 17/10284] on intermediate layer -- B32B 17/10284 covers inventions that involve an intermediate layer within a layered product, such as a sheet of glass, glass-fiber, slag, or similar fibrous material, where the added layer provides distinct mechanical, thermal, or optical functions between the outer layers of the structure. This subclass falls under the broader group for layered products built from flat or non-flat strata.
[B32B 17/10293] Edge features, e.g. inserts or holes -- This classification covers edge features applied to layered products such as sheet glass, ceramic, or fiber sheets, including inserts, holes, or other modifications made at the periphery of the material. It pertains to manufacturing methods that create or attach these edge elements to improve handling, sealing, or functional performance.
[B32B 17/10302] Edge sealing -- B32B 17/10302 relates to methods and apparatus for sealing the edges of layered glass, slag or fibre sheets that form multi-strata products such as honeycomb or cellular panels. The edge sealing may involve adhesives, welding, bonding or other techniques to improve structural integrity, moisture resistance and fire protection.
[B32B 17/10311] Intumescent layers for fire protection -- The code B32B 17/10311 covers intumescent layers applied to layered products such as glass, slag or fibre sheets to provide fire-protective performance. The claim pertains to coatings or interlayers that swell when heated, forming an insulating barrier that slows heat transmission and protects the underlying structure.
[B32B 17/10321] Laminated safety glass or glazing containing liquid layers -- This class covers laminated safety glass or glazing in which one or more liquid interlayers, such as polymeric resins or silicone fluids, are bonded between glass sheets to improve impact resistance and retain fragments upon breakage. The liquid layers may be cured in place or remain fluid to provide additional sealing, acoustic damping, or thermal insulation.
[B32B 17/1033] Laminated safety glass or glazing containing temporary protective coatings or layers -- A laminated safety glass or glazing in which one or more temporary protective coatings or layers are incorporated between the glass sheets to shield the product during handling, transport, or installation, and which are intended to be removed or become inactive after the glass is in service. This entry covers such protective interlayers in glass structures built from flat or honeycomb-type strata.
[B32B 17/10339] Specific parts of the laminated safety glass or glazing being colored or tinted  tinted glass sheet  B32B17/1011 ; tinted interlayer  B32B17/10651 -- B32B 17/10339 pertains to laminated safety glass or glazing in which particular components are colored or tinted, such as a tinted glass sheet or a tinted interlayer. The entry falls under layered products made from glass, slag or similar fibers and covers the specific parts of the laminate that receive the coloration.
[B32B 17/10348] comprising an obscuration band -- B32B 17/10348 designates layered glass or similar sheet products that incorporate an obscuration band-a strip of material or treatment that reduces light transmission, providing privacy, shading, or decorative effect. The band may be integral to the laminate or applied as a distinct layer within the product's stratified structure.
[B32B 17/10357] comprising a tinted intermediate film -- The subclass covers layered products such as laminated glass, glass-slag composites or other sheet structures that contain an intermediate film which is tinted, colored or pigmented. It includes the use of a colored interlayer to provide aesthetic, UV-blocking or heat-absorbing properties within the composite.
[B32B 17/10366] Reinforcements of the laminated safety glass or glazing against impact or intrusion  containing metal wires for reinforcement  B32B17/10412 -- This CPC subclass concerns layered products, specifically laminated safety glass or glazing that incorporates metal-wire reinforcement to enhance resistance to impact or intrusion. It is recorded under code B32B 17/10366 within the broader category of layered products built from sheet glass, glass, slag or similar fibres.
[B32B 17/10376] Laminated safety glass or glazing containing metal wires -- The CPC subclass B32B 17/10376 covers laminated safety glass or glazing that incorporates metal wires within the layers. It includes products where one or more glass sheets are bonded together with an interlayer containing a wire mesh to improve strength and prevent shattering.
[B32B 17/10385] for ohmic resistance heating -- The CPC subclass B32B 17/10385 covers layered products such as sheet glass, glass-slag composites or similar fibre structures that are heated by passing an electric current directly through the material, i.e., using ohmic resistance heating. It pertains to processes where the product itself acts as the heating element during manufacture or treatment.
[B32B 17/10394] Alarm wires -- Alarm wires are conductive filaments integrated into laminated glass or similar layered panels, providing a built-in detection system that triggers an alarm when the glass is broken or stressed. The wires are typically embedded within the interlayer or between glass strata, allowing continuous monitoring without compromising the structural integrity of the product. This entry classifies such safety-enhanced layered products within the Cooperative Patent Classification system.
[B32B 17/10403] for radiation shielding -- In the Cooperative Patent Classification, code B32B 17/10403 is placed under performing operations, layered products. It covers layered constructions of sheet glass, glass-slag or similar fibre materials that are designed for radiation shielding.
[B32B 17/10412] for reinforcement -- The CPC subclass B32B 17/10412 covers layered glass or glass-like products that incorporate reinforcement to improve mechanical strength, stiffness or impact resistance. It includes the use of fibers, meshes, ribs or other strengthening elements within flat or non-flat strata such as honeycomb or cellular structures.
[B32B 17/10422] for aesthetic reasons -- B32B 17/10422 pertains to layered products made of glass, glass-slag, or similar fibres where the stratification is employed mainly for decorative or aesthetic purposes. It includes flat or non-flat structures such as honeycomb or cellular panels that are intended to enhance visual appearance.
[B32B 17/10431] Specific parts for the modulation of light incorporated into the laminated safety glass or glazing -- B32B 17/10431 covers components that are integrated into laminated safety glass or glazing to modulate light, such as filters, diffusion layers, or reflective films. These parts are designed for use in layered products built from flat or contoured glass, including honeycomb or cellular structures, and enable control of glare, privacy, or illumination in safety-glass applications.
[B32B 17/1044] Invariable transmission -- B32B 17/1044 addresses layered articles constructed from sheet glass, glass, slag or similar fibres in which the transmission of light or other radiation stays constant across the material. The term invariable transmission denotes products whose optical or radiative throughput does not vary with position or direction.
[B32B 17/10449] Wavelength selective transmission -- This subclass covers layered glass, slag, fiber or similar sheet products that are engineered to allow transmission of specific wavelengths of electromagnetic radiation while attenuating others, such as optical filters, dichroic glass and wavelength-selective panels.
[B32B 17/10458] Polarization selective transmission -- The CPC subclass B32B 17/10458 covers processes and structures for layered glass or similar sheet products that are designed to transmit light of a particular polarization while blocking other polarizations. It includes methods for incorporating polarising layers or coatings within laminated glass, honeycomb or cellular structures to achieve selective transmission.
[B32B 17/10467] Variable transmission -- This subclass concerns layered glass or similar sheet products whose light transmission can be varied on demand, including electro-chromic, thermochromic, photo-chromic, liquid-crystal, or mechanically adjustable glazing.
[B32B 17/10477] thermochromic -- Thermochromic layered products are structures made of stacked sheets of glass, slag, or similar fibers that change colour in response to temperature variations. The classification covers methods and devices that incorporate such temperature-responsive layers in honeycomb, cellular or other multilayer configurations.
[B32B 17/10486] photochromic -- This CPC subclass covers layered glass or glass-like sheet products that exhibit a photochromic effect, changing colour or light transmission when exposed to UV or visible light. It includes designs and methods for incorporating photochromic compounds into flat or structured glass panels, honeycomb cores, or similar fibre-reinforced layers.
[B32B 17/10495] optoelectronic, i.e. optical valve -- B32B 17/10495 covers layered products such as sheet glass, glass-fiber or slag composites that incorporate an optoelectronic function, specifically an optical valve for controlling light transmission. The classification falls under the Performing Operations > Layered Products hierarchy and is used to index inventions where a laminated structure includes a device that modulates light in electronic circuits.
[B32B 17/10504] Liquid crystal layer -- B32B 17/10504 covers the incorporation of a liquid-crystal layer within a structured, multi-strata product such as glass, slag or fiber-based panels. It pertains to the preparation, orientation, sealing or encapsulation of liquid crystals in layered sheets, honeycomb cores or other flat or non-flat composites used in displays or smart-material applications.
[B32B 17/10513] Electrochromic layer -- B32B 17/10513 covers electrochromic layers incorporated in multilayered products such as glass, slag or fiber sheets. These layers are thin films that alter their optical properties, typically colour or transmittance, in response to an electrical stimulus, enabling applications like smart windows, dimmable mirrors and low-power displays.
[B32B 17/10522] Electrophoretic layer -- The B32B 17/10522 subclass concerns electrophoretic layers incorporated into laminated structures such as sheet glass, glass-based composites, slag or fiber-reinforced panels. It covers the formation, composition and application of electrically charged particle layers that provide visual, filtering or functional properties within these layered products.
[B32B 17/10532] Suspended particle layer -- Suspended particle layer refers to a sheet-like structure in which solid particles are held apart by a binder or air, forming a layer that can be glass, slag, silica or similar fibres and is used in honeycomb, cellular or laminated components.
[B32B 17/10541] comprising a light source or a light guide -- The CPC subclass B32B 17/10541 covers layered products such as glass, glass-slag, or fibre laminates that incorporate a light source or a light-guiding element within the strata. It includes transparent or translucent panels, glazing, or honeycomb structures designed to emit, transmit or distribute illumination through the layered material.
[B32B 17/1055] characterized by the resin layer, i.e. interlayer -- B32B 17/1055 covers layered products such as laminated glass or other sheet materials that are defined by a resin or polymer interlayer bonding the individual layers together. The interlayer provides adhesion, impact resistance, and can affect optical, acoustic or safety properties of the composite product. This subclass includes applications where the resin layer is the principal distinguishing feature of the multilayer structure.
[B32B 17/10559] Shape of the cross-section -- The code B32B 17/10559 refers to patents that define or modify the cross-sectional shape of layered products such as sheet glass, glass-slag composites or fibrous panels. It falls under the CPC group for performing operations on layered products and covers any geometric configuration of the material's profile.
[B32B 17/10568] varying in thickness -- B32B 17/10568 covers layered products whose individual strata are not uniform in thickness, such as glass, slag or fiber sheets where the layer depth changes across the material. The classification is used for inventions that intentionally vary thickness to achieve specific mechanical, thermal or optical properties.
[B32B 17/10577] Surface roughness -- This subgroup concerns the measurement, specification and control of surface roughness on layered products such as laminated glass, fibre-reinforced plates or honey-comb structures. It covers methods for grading texture, setting roughness criteria and applying surface-finishing techniques that affect the external face.
[B32B 17/10587] created by embossing -- The CPC subclass B32B 17/10587 covers processes for producing layered products such as sheet glass, glass-ceramics, slag or fibre sheets by embossing the material. It falls under performing operations on layered products, specifically methods that shape flat or non-flat strata into a textured surface.
[B32B 17/10596] created by melt fracture -- This CPC entry covers the formation of layered sheet products such as glass, slag or fiber sheets by using melt fracture, where the molten material fractures during extrusion to create a cellular or honeycomb structure. It relates to processes that generate strata of flat or non-flat layers through this fracture mechanism.
[B32B 17/10605] Type of plasticiser
[B32B 17/10614] comprising particles for purposes other than dyeing -- B32B 17/10614 classifies layered products such as glass, slag or fiber sheets that incorporate added particles whose function is not coloration. The particles may serve reinforcement, insulation, flame-retardancy or other performance-enhancing roles. This subclass falls under the broader group for layered products built from flat or non-flat strata.
[B32B 17/10623] Whitening agents reflecting visible light -- B32B 17/10623 pertains to whitening agents that reflect visible light and are applied to layered products such as sheet glass, glass-based composites, slag or fiber-reinforced structures. These agents are used to enhance the brightness or apparent whiteness of the surface by scattering and reflecting the visible spectrum.
[B32B 17/10633] Infrared radiation absorbing or reflecting agents -- This CPC subclass covers additives incorporated into sheet glass, glass-fiber, slag-fiber or similar layered materials that absorb or reflect infrared radiation, providing thermal-insulating or heat-reflecting properties. It includes the composition, preparation and use of these infrared-active agents in construction, automotive, aerospace and related applications.
[B32B 17/10642] Thermally conductive agents -- The CPC subclass B32B 17/10642 covers additives and thermally conductive agents incorporated into layered products such as sheet glass, glass-based laminates, slag or fibre-based honeycomb and cellular structures. It addresses materials that improve heat-transfer properties of these stratified assemblies, typically used in applications where efficient thermal conduction through the layered substrate is required.
[B32B 17/10651] comprising colorants, e.g. dyes or pigments -- B32B 17/10651 pertains to layered products made of sheet glass, glass, slag or similar fibres in which colourants such as dyes or pigments are incorporated, covering both the manufacturing methods and the resulting coloured structures.
[B32B 17/1066] imparting a tint in certain regions only, i.e. shade band -- This CPC subclass covers processes for producing layered glass, slag, fibre or similar sheet products in which a tint is applied selectively to defined zones, creating shade bands. It relates to methods of imparting color or shading in specific regions of flat or non-flat layered structures.
[B32B 17/10669] Luminescent agents -- B32B 17/10669 covers the incorporation of luminescent agents into layered products such as sheet glass, glass, slag or fiber-based structures, where the product consists of stacked flat or non-flat strata. The classification applies to technologies that embed light-emitting compounds within these layered materials.
[B32B 17/10678] comprising UV absorbers or stabilizers, e.g. antioxidants -- B32B 17/10678 covers layered glass or similar fibrous products that incorporate ultraviolet absorbers or stabilizers such as antioxidants. The classification applies to laminated, honeycomb or cellular sheet materials where UV-protective additives are integrated into the structure to improve durability and resistance to degradation.
[B32B 17/10688] Adjustment of the adherence to the glass layers -- The CPC subclass B32B 17/10688 covers techniques for adjusting the adhesion between glass layers in laminated or cellular products such as sheet glass, glass-fiber, slag or similar fibrous strata. It includes methods, treatments or additives used to modify bonding strength, improve interfacial contact or control delamination in layered structures. This subclass falls under the broader categories of Performing Operations on Layered Products.
[B32B 17/10697] being cross-linked -- The subgroup B32B 17/10697 concerns layered products-such as sheet glass, glass-slag or fibre structures-where the individual layers are chemically cross-linked, improving the material's strength, stiffness, or thermal stability, for example in cross-linked glass-fiber honeycomb or cellular panels.
[B32B 17/10706] being photo-polymerized -- The subgroup B32B 17/10706 relates to the manufacture of layered products such as sheet glass, glass-fiber, slag-fiber or similar strata in which the layers are joined or formed by photo-polymerization. It covers processes that use light-activated polymerizable resins or coatings to cure and bond the individual sheets, creating honeycomb, cellular or other multilayer structures.
[B32B 17/10715] containing polyether -- B32B 17/10715 covers layered products-such as sheet glass, glass-slag composites or similar fiber structures-that incorporate a polyether component. The classification applies to methods and resulting articles where the polyether acts as a binder, filler or additive within the stratified material, influencing properties like flexibility, impact resistance or thermal performance. It falls under the CPC group for layered products built from flat or non-flat strata.
[B32B 17/10724] containing polyamide -- The subclass B32B 17/10724 covers layered glass-type products, such as sheets, panels or honeycomb structures, in which polyamide material is incorporated as an interlayer, coating or reinforcement, affecting the mechanical or barrier properties of the composite. This entry falls under the hierarchy of performing operations for layered products built from flat or non-flat strata.
[B32B 17/10733] containing epoxy -- The CPC subclass B32B 17/10733 pertains to layered products-laminated glass, cellular or honey-comb structures, etc.-that incorporate epoxy resin as a bonding or matrix material within the strata.
[B32B 17/10743] containing acrylate (co)polymers or salts thereof -- This subgroup relates to layered products - such as glass, slag or fibre sheets - that incorporate acrylate (co)polymers or their salts, typically as binders, adhesives or reinforcement agents. The polymers may be used to improve mechanical strength, flexibility or chemical resistance of the stratified structure.
[B32B 17/10752] containing polycarbonate -- B32B 17/10752 covers layered products-such as glass, slag or similar fibre structures-that incorporate polycarbonate as a constituent material, either as a separate layer or blended within the strata. The classification applies to composites where polycarbonate contributes to the mechanical, optical or thermal properties of the multi-layered article.
[B32B 17/10761] containing vinyl acetal -- The CPC subclass B32B 17/10761 covers layered products such as sheet glass, glass-slag composites or similar fibre structures that incorporate vinyl acetal as a component, typically to improve chemical resistance or mechanical properties. It applies to honeycomb, cellular or other stratified forms where the vinyl acetal is present in the material or the bonding layers.
[B32B 17/1077] containing polyurethane -- B32B 17/1077 covers layered products - for example glass sheets, glass-fiber mats, slag or similar fibre structures - that incorporate polyurethane, typically as a binder or matrix material within the strata, providing resilience, adhesion or insulation to the composite.
[B32B 17/10779] containing polyester -- This CPC subclass pertains to layered products such as sheets of glass, slag or fibre panels that incorporate polyester within the structure, usually as a matrix, binder or coating to improve mechanical or thermal performance, and includes the related manufacturing steps and compositions.
[B32B 17/10788] containing ethylene vinylacetate -- B32B 17/10788 falls under the layered products group for sheet-glass, slag or fibre structures and specifies that the product incorporates ethylene-vinylacetate. The entry covers compositions where this copolymer is added to the layers to modify properties such as flexibility, impact resistance or adhesion. It is a niche sub-class within the broader performing-operations hierarchy for multilayered material designs.
[B32B 17/10798] containing silicone -- B32B 17/10798 classifies layered products such as sheet glass, glass-slag composites or similar fibre structures that incorporate silicone, typically as a coating, binder or additive to improve flexibility, durability or thermal resistance. The entry covers processes for preparing these silicone-containing layered materials and their resulting forms.
[B32B 17/10807] Making laminated safety glass or glazing; Apparatus therefor -- The CPC entry B32B 17/10807 covers processes for producing laminated safety glass or glazing, including the steps of assembling and bonding layers of glass with interlayers such as plastic or resin, and the machinery used to carry out these operations. It falls under the layered-products group dealing with sheet-glass constructions.
[B32B 17/10816] by pressing -- This sub-class covers processes for forming layered structures such as glass, slag or fibre sheets by applying pressure to bond the layers together.
[B32B 17/10825] Isostatic pressing, i.e. using non rigid pressure-exerting members against rigid parts -- B32B 17/10825 covers the use of isostatic pressing, where flexible pressure-applying members are employed against rigid components to compact layered products such as sheet glass, glass-slag composites, or fiber mats, creating uniform density throughout the strata.
[B32B 17/10834] using a fluid -- B32B 17/10834 covers processes for layered products such as sheet glass, slag or fibre laminates in which a fluid is employed, for example to impregnate, coat, or bond the layers during manufacture. It falls within the CPC hierarchy of Performing Operations → Layered Products, focusing on the use of liquids, gases or vapour in the production of flat or non-flat stratified structures.
[B32B 17/10844] using a membrane between the layered product and the fluid -- B32B 17/10844 relates to processes in which a membrane or barrier layer is positioned between a layered product - such as sheet glass, glass-fiber, slag, honeycomb or cellular structures - and the contacting fluid. The membrane controls fluid ingress, protects the layers, or facilitates selective transport during manufacture or use.
[B32B 17/10853] the membrane being bag-shaped -- Refers to layered products where the functional membrane is formed as a bag-shaped structure, typically using flat or non-flat sheets such as glass, glass fibre, slag fibre or similar materials. The subclass addresses fabrication methods and designs specific to this three-dimensional membrane geometry.
[B32B 17/10862] using pressing-rolls -- The subclass covers methods where layered glass, slag, fibre sheets and similar materials are produced by passing the material through a pair of pressing rolls that shape and consolidate the strata. It includes continuous or intermittent rolling operations that generate flat or shaped panels.
[B32B 17/10871] in combination with particular heat treatment -- B32B 17/10871 covers layered products - including sheet glass, glass-fiber, slag or similar fibrous sheets - where the layers are subjected to a particular heat-treatment step such as annealing, tempering or controlled cooling to alter mechanical or optical characteristics.
[B32B 17/1088] by superposing a plurality of layered products -- B32B 17/1088 relates to the manufacture of a composite by superposing several layered products, for example sheets of glass, slag or fibrous materials, to create a multi-strata structure such as honeycomb or cellular panels. This entry falls under the CPC section for performing operations on layered products.
[B32B 17/10889] shaping the sheets, e.g. by using a mould  B32B17/10816  takes precedence -- B32B 17/10889 covers methods for shaping sheet-like layered products-such as glass, slag or fibre sheets-by means of moulds or similar forming tools. It falls under the broader class of layered products built from flat or non-flat strata, including honeycomb and cellular structures. The subclass B32B 17/10816 is the preceding entry that takes priority.
[B32B 17/10899] by introducing interlayers of synthetic resin -- B32B 17/10899 covers the manufacture of layered products such as sheet glass, glass-slag or similar fibre sheets in which one or more synthetic-resin interlayers are introduced between the strata. The interlayer may be applied as a film, coating or impregnated sheet to improve adhesion, impact resistance or other functional properties of the composite panel. This falls under the Performing Operations → Layered Products hierarchy of the CPC.
[B32B 17/10908] in liquid form -- The CPC entry B32B 17/10908 refers to layered products-such as glass, slag, or fibre sheets and honeycomb structures-when they are in a liquid state, typically describing the handling, shaping or forming of these materials while molten before solidification. It falls under the hierarchy of performing operations on layered products.
[B32B 17/10917] between two pre-positioned glass layers -- This CPC subclass covers processes in which an additional material-such as a film, coating, filler or adhesive-is introduced or bonded between two pre-positioned glass sheets, typically during the manufacture of laminated or honeycomb-type glass structures. It pertains to methods that modify the interlayer while the outer glass layers remain in place.
[B32B 17/10926] by spraying -- This CPC subclass covers processes for forming layered structures-such as cellular or honey-comb panels built from sheet glass, glass fibres, slag or similar materials-where the layers are created by spraying a liquid or molten material onto a substrate.
[B32B 17/10935] as a preformed layer, e.g. formed by extrusion -- B32B 17/10935 refers to layered products that incorporate a pre-formed layer, such as one produced by extrusion, within a composite structure. The classification covers items built from strata of flat or shaped sheets, including glass, slag or fiber layers, where the extruded layer is inserted as a discrete element rather than being formed in-situ. This entry falls under the broader CPC group for layered products and sheet-glass-type materials.
[B32B 17/10944] in powder form -- B32B 17/10944 covers processes for producing layered products such as glass, slag or fibre sheets from powder materials. The classification addresses forming stratified structures by using powders as the raw feedstock, enabling the creation of honeycomb, cellular or other multi-layered components.
[B32B 17/10954] by using an aligning laminating device -- B32B 17/10954 covers layered products-such as sheet glass, glass-slag composites, or similar fibre structures-where the layers are aligned and bonded using a laminating device that positions each sheet before lamination. This sub-group falls under the broader class of performing operations on layered products, specifically the preparation of strata of flat or non-flat materials.
[B32B 17/10963] specially adapted for repairing the layered products -- B32B 17/10963 covers techniques, devices or materials specially adapted for repairing layered products such as sheet glass, glass, slag or fibre-based panels. The entry falls under performing operations on layered products, focusing on the restoration or fixing of strata-built structures.
[B32B 17/10972] Degassing during the lamination  B32B17/10816  takes precedence -- This classification code pertains to the process of degassing during the lamination of layered products that primarily consist of sheet glass or similar fibrous materials, with a specific note that another code (B32B17/10816) takes precedence in certain contexts.
[B32B 17/10981] Pre-treatment of the layers -- B32B 17/10981 covers methods for preparing the individual strata of a layered product before assembly, such as cleaning, chemically modifying, or applying surface-active treatments to sheets of glass, slag or fiber-based materials to improve bonding, durability or functional performance.
[B32B 17/1099] After-treatment of the layered product, e.g. cooling -- B32B 17/1099 covers processes that apply post-manufacturing treatments to layered products such as sheet glass, glass-fiber, slag or honeycomb structures, for example cooling, annealing or surface conditioning to improve properties. The classification is part of the CPC group for performing operations on layered materials.
[B32B 18/00] Layered products essentially comprising ceramics, e.g. refractory products -- **Definition:** This place covers:  At least two pre-shaped green ceramic, ceramic pre-form (e.g. a ceramic fiber pre-form) or sintered ceramic layers are joined together, where the emphasis is not on the joining method. It also encompasses two layers of ceramic powders that are pressed together in a press. If after joining the two ceramic layers other type of layers, e.g. metallic or plastic layers are joined to the initial ceramic laminate, classification under other main groups of B32B will be necessary as well, but classification in B32B18/00 remains. If in between the two ceramic layers there is a thin, non-essential layer of another material, e.g. a metallic electrode, it is still classified in B32B18/00 , but classification in other groups of B32B should be considered. B32B18/00 is normally not used for laminates containing identical ceramic layers, such as in multilayer capacitors.  B32B18/00 also contains cold bonding of ceramic substrates.
[B32B 19/00] Layered products comprising natural mineral fibres or particles, e.g. asbestos, mica -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Layered products characterised by having a layer made of naturally occurring mineral fibres or particles.
[B32B 19/02] embedded in a plastic substance -- B32B 19/02 covers layered composite products in which natural mineral fibres or particles such as asbestos, mica or similar materials are incorporated into a plastic matrix, forming strata that may be flat, cellular or honey-comb. The classification pertains to the manufacture of such reinforced plastic structures.
[B32B 19/04] next to another layer of a -- B32B 19/04 covers layered products that incorporate a stratum of natural mineral fibres or particles such as asbestos or mica placed next to another layer of a different material, including honeycomb or cellular structures. It pertains to the design or manufacturing of such composite laminates where the mineral-based layer is adjacent to a contrasting layer.

[B32B 19/048] made of particles -- This CPC subclass concerns layered products whose structure is formed from natural mineral fibers or particles, such as asbestos or mica, arranged in flat or non-flat strata like cellular or honeycomb forms.
