[B32B 19/06] next to a fibrous or filamentary layer -- This subclass deals with layered products that incorporate a fibrous or filamentary stratum-in particular natural mineral fibres such as asbestos or mica-adjacent to another layer of material. It covers the design and manufacture of composite structures where the fiber layer is bonded or otherwise joined to a second layer, for purposes such as reinforcement, insulation, or aesthetic effect.
[B32B 19/08] comprising asbestos -- B32B 19/08 covers the manufacture of layered structures such as honeycomb or cellular panels that incorporate natural mineral fibres like asbestos. It applies to products built from strata of flat or non-flat material where asbestos is used as a reinforcing or functional component.
[B32B 2037/0061] the apparatus being an office laminator -- B32B 2037/0061 covers laminating machines designed for office use, where the apparatus applies a protective film to flat documents or thin sheets. The subclass specifies compact, low-pressure devices intended for small-scale, on-demand lamination rather than industrial continuous-feed systems.
[B32B 2037/0069] the apparatus being originally designed for another function, e.g. printer, photocopier -- B32B 2037/0069 covers apparatus that was originally created for a different primary function but is employed for another purpose, such as using a printer or photocopier to perform tasks beyond its initial design. This classification captures repurposed or dual-use equipment where the original design intent differs from the current application.
[B32B 2037/0092] in which absence of adhesives is explicitly presented as an advantage -- B32B 2037/0092 refers to coating or film technologies where the absence of adhesives is specifically presented as an advantage, covering methods and products that rely on inherent adhesion, mechanical interlocking or surface treatment rather than glue. The subclass is used to classify inventions that emphasize adhesive-free bonding for reasons such as reduced material cost, environmental impact or improved durability.
[B32B 2037/1063] using an electrostatic force -- B32B 2037/1063 covers methods and apparatus that employ electrostatic forces to manipulate or deposit materials on glass, ceramic or related substrates, such as electrostatic spraying, printing or particle-attraction techniques used in shaping, coating or treating those surfaces.
[B32B 2037/1072] using a fluid jet -- B32B 2037/1072 covers processes that use a fluid jet to shape, cut, or otherwise treat solid materials during manufacturing, including water-jet cutting, high-pressure spray forming and jet machining of metals, ceramics, polymers and composites. It applies to any method where a high-velocity fluid stream performs material removal or deformation.
[B32B 2037/1081] using a magnetic force -- The subclass B32B 2037/1081 covers processes for shaping, treating or forming polymeric or composite materials in which a magnetic force is applied to influence or manipulate the material, such as aligning magnetic particles, moving molten polymer, or assisting curing through magnetic fields. This includes the use of static or varying magnetic fields during extrusion, molding, coating or other manufacturing steps.
[B32B 2037/109] using a squeegee -- B32B 2037/109 relates to the use of a squeegee to spread, remove or level fluids on a substrate, typically in coating, printing or cleaning processes. It covers devices that move a flexible blade across a surface to control the distribution of liquids.
[B32B 2037/1215] Hot-melt adhesive -- B32B 2037/1215 covers the use of hot-melt adhesives-thermoplastic or thermosetting polymers applied in a molten state that solidify on cooling-for bonding layers in laminated or sandwich structures, including methods of preparation, application and the specific formulations employed in such multilayer products.
[B32B 2037/1223] film-shaped -- The CPC class B32B 2037/1223 relates to processes for producing film-shaped glass, ceramic or mineral products, including methods of forming thin, continuous sheets, coatings or layered structures. It covers techniques such as casting, rolling, extrusion, or deposition that yield flexible or planar film forms for optical, electronic or protective applications.
[B32B 2037/123] net-shaped -- The CPC subclass B32B 2037/123 concerns the manufacture of net-shaped metal articles, such as meshes, grids, perforated sheets or lattice structures. It covers processes and apparatus for forming, shaping, joining or sintering metal into open-work, net-like configurations, including related surface-treatment steps.
[B32B 2037/1238] in the form of powder -- B32B 2037/1238 designates inventions that involve a material being handled, processed or employed in the form of a powder. The subclass covers methods for producing, modifying, shaping, or using powders, granules, agglomerates or other particulate forms, along with related apparatuses and treatment steps specific to that powder state.
[B32B 2037/1253] curable adhesive -- B32B 2037/1253 covers curable adhesives applied to glass articles or during glass manufacturing, including adhesives that harden by polymerization, heat, radiation or chemical reaction to bond glass to glass or other materials.
[B32B 2037/1261] moisture curable -- B32B 2037/1261 relates to moisture-curable coating compositions and the methods for applying them, covering formulations that harden when exposed to moisture and are used for protective or decorative films such as paints, inks and sealants.
[B32B 2037/1269] multi-component adhesive -- The CPC B32B 2037/1269 entry covers multi-component adhesive systems in which two or more separate parts are combined to form the final adhesive, including the composition of each component, the method of mixing or activation, and related applications such as sealants, bonding agents, or encapsulants.
[B32B 2037/1276] water-based adhesive -- B32B 2037/1276 is a CPC subclass covering adhesives that use water as the principal carrier or solvent. It includes formulations where polymeric or inorganic components are dispersed in an aqueous medium to provide bonding properties.
[B32B 2037/148] whereby layers material is selected in order to facilitate recycling of the laminate -- The CPC subclass B32B 2037/148 covers laminates in which the individual layers are chosen specifically to enable the laminate's recycling. It addresses material selection and layer design that facilitate separation, recovery, or reuse of components, improving the overall recyclability of the composite structure.
[B32B 2037/243] Coating -- B32B 2037/243 covers methods and apparatus for applying protective, decorative or functional coatings to substrates, including techniques such as spraying, dipping, brushing or printing, as well as the composition of coating materials used in these processes. The subclass focuses on the coating step itself rather than the substrate preparation.
[B32B 2037/246] Vapour deposition -- B32B covers processes for applying protective or functional layers to surfaces, including coating and surface-finishing techniques. Sub-group 2037/246 specifically relates to vapour deposition methods, where material is transferred in gaseous form and condensed onto a substrate to form a thin film. This includes physical or chemical vapour deposition processes used in microelectronics, optics, and similar fields.
[B32B 2037/262] Partition plates or sheets for separating several laminates pressed simultaneously -- B32B 2037/262 covers partition plates or sheets that are placed between multiple laminates during a simultaneous pressing operation to keep them separated and ensure uniform pressure distribution. These accessories are used in the manufacture of stacked composite panels, printed circuit boards, or other multilayer structures where independent curing or bonding of each layer is required.
[B32B 2037/264] Pressure equalizing layers -- The CPC subclass B32B 2037/264 covers technologies that incorporate pressure-equalizing layers in the production of ceramic or glass articles. It includes designs where a supplementary layer is applied to balance internal and external pressures during shaping, forming, or sintering, improving dimensional stability and reducing defects such as warping or cracking.
[B32B 2037/266] Cushioning layers -- B32B 2037/266 relates to the design and manufacture of cushioning layers within multilayer articles, covering materials and structures that provide shock-absorbing or compressible properties for protective or comfort functions such as padding, footwear soles, or impact-resistant panels. It includes the preparation, bonding, and integration of foam, elastomeric, or cellular layers intended to absorb energy and distribute loads. This subclass focuses on the technical features that give the layer its cushioning effect.
[B32B 2037/268] Release layers -- Release layers are intermediate coating layers applied to a substrate that can be selectively removed to separate or transfer a subsequent or overlying film, often acting as sacrificial layers to enable clean detachment, patterning or transfer processes in metal coating and micro-fabrication.
[B32B 2038/0016] Abrading -- The code covers processes in which a workpiece is subjected to abrasion, i.e., material removal by rubbing an abrasive medium such as grinding wheels, belts, sandpapers, or particles in a slurry, to shape, finish or deburr surfaces. It includes apparatus and parameters for abrasive action.
[B32B 2038/002] Sandblasting -- B32B 2038/002 relates to the mechanical preparation of surfaces by abrasive impact, commonly known as sandblasting. It covers methods and apparatus that accelerate abrasive particles against a workpiece to clean, roughen or shape its surface before coating or other processing.
[B32B 2038/0024] Crushing -- B32B 2038/0024 covers methods and equipment for crushing metal material or metal powder to reduce particle size, typically as a preparatory step in powder-metallurgy or cermet production. It includes mechanical actions such as impact, compression or shearing that break larger pieces into smaller particles for subsequent shaping or sintering.
[B32B 2038/0028] Stretching, elongating -- B32B 2038/0028 covers processes that stretch or elongate polymeric sheets, films or other plastic articles, including uniaxial and biaxial drawing, orientation and thinning techniques used to modify mechanical, optical or barrier properties. This subgroup is part of the broader class for shaping and treating plastics by methods such as molding, casting, and forming.
[B32B 2038/0044] for creating local stresses -- B32B 2038/0044 pertains to techniques within thin-film deposition that deliberately generate localized mechanical stresses in a coating or substrate, such as stress-inducing ion implantation, thermal gradients, or patterned substrate deformation, to modify film properties, improve adhesion or enable micro-structuring.
[B32B 2038/0048] Annealing, relaxing -- The CPC subclass B32B 2038/0048 covers annealing or relaxation processes applied to glass, ceramic or similar materials after shaping. It includes heat-treatment steps that reduce internal stresses, improve dimensional stability and modify mechanical or optical properties of the finished article.
[B32B 2038/0052] Other operations not otherwise provided for -- B32B 2038/0052 covers miscellaneous glass-working steps that are not specifically listed in other B32B subclasses, including auxiliary or unconventional treatments applied during the production or finishing of glass articles.
[B32B 2038/0056] Moistening -- B32B 2038/0056 covers the moistening step in the manufacture of laminated or composite glass, where a liquid-typically water, a solvent or an aqueous solution-is applied to one or more glass surfaces to improve adhesion, cleaning or subsequent processing. The classification is used for methods that deliberately wet the glass before bonding, coating or other treatment operations.
[B32B 2038/006] Relieving internal or residual stresses -- The B32B 2038/006 subclass covers methods and processes that reduce or eliminate internal or residual stresses in metal parts, such as heat treatment, mechanical deformation, vibration, or other stress-relief techniques applied after forming, machining or joining. It is used to classify patents describing how these treatments improve dimensional stability, mechanical performance or fatigue resistance of the treated material.
[B32B 2038/0064] Smoothing, polishing, making a glossy surface -- This subclass covers techniques and devices that remove surface irregularities, applying abrasive or chemical actions to produce a smooth, mirror-like finish on solid materials, including polishing pads, lapping machines, chemical-mechanical polishing, and related steps in semiconductor or optical component fabrication.
[B32B 2038/0068] Changing crystal orientation -- B32B 2038/0068 relates to methods for altering the orientation of crystals in a solid material, including techniques such as deformation, annealing, or applying external fields to re-orient the crystal lattice. The entry covers processes that intentionally change crystal direction to achieve desired physical or mechanical properties.
[B32B 2038/0072] Orienting fibers -- The subclass B32B 2038/0072 covers methods for orienting fibers within a sheet, web or composite, using mechanical, magnetic, electric or fluid-flow techniques to align the fibers in a preferred direction. It includes equipment and procedural steps that control fiber orientation to enhance strength, stiffness, permeability or other functional properties of the material.
[B32B 2038/0076] Curing, vulcanising, cross-linking -- The code B32B 2038/0076 covers processes that chemically or thermally cure, vulcanise or cross-link polymeric or rubbery materials to form three-dimensional networks, improving elasticity, strength and stability. It includes methods using heat, radiation, catalysts or additives to achieve the desired degree of cross-linking, as well as related equipment and control steps.
[B32B 2038/008] Sewing, stitching -- B32B 2038/008 relates to methods of joining textile materials by sewing or stitching. It includes the use of needle and thread, yarn or other filament, and covers variations such as lockstitch, chain stitch, and specialized stitching for composite fabrics.
[B32B 2038/0084] Foaming -- The CPC subclass B32B 2038/0084 covers coating processes in which a foaming step is employed to create a cellular or porous structure in the applied layer. It includes methods that generate gas bubbles by chemical reaction, physical expansion, or use of blowing agents during the formation of films, paints, or other surface coatings.
[B32B 2038/0088] Expanding, swelling -- The code B32B 2038/0088 covers techniques for expanding or swelling metal workpieces, such as hydraulic or pneumatic bulging, internal-pressure expansion of tubes, and other methods that increase thickness or diameter without removing material. It includes apparatus and processes that produce a controlled swell or radial expansion in sheet, plate, or strip during mechanical forming operations.
[B32B 2038/0092] Metallizing -- The CPC subclass B32B 2038/0092 covers metallizing processes, i.e., methods for depositing a metal layer onto a substrate. It includes techniques such as vapor deposition, sputtering, electro-plating and spray-coating applied for functional or decorative purposes. This classification is used for inventions that produce or modify metallic coatings on various materials.
[B32B 2038/0096] Riveting -- B32B 2038/0096 relates to the joining of sheet metal or similar materials by riveting, covering the preparation, shaping and setting of rivets as well as the tools and machines used to produce and install them. The subclass includes methods for forming, inserting and securing rivets in assemblies and the apparatus for controlling the riveting process.
[B32B 2038/042] Punching -- B32B 2038/042 concerns punching processes used to create openings in metal or other sheet materials. It includes the design of punches, dies, tooling arrangements, and methods for removing material by shearing or forming holes in workpieces.
[B32B 2038/045] Slitting -- B32B 2038/045 pertains to the slitting of sheet or strip materials, describing methods and apparatus for dividing a continuous sheet into narrower strips by cutting, tearing, or other separation techniques. The classification includes mechanical, thermal, or laser slitting processes and devices such as knives, rollers, and cutting heads used in metal, plastic, or composite sheet processing.
[B32B 2038/047] Perforating -- B32B 2038/047 falls under the sheet-metal working section of the Cooperative Patent Classification and covers processes and tools for perforating materials. It includes methods of creating regular or irregular openings in metal sheets, films, or similar substrates for purposes such as ventilation, filtration, decor or weight reduction, as well as the corresponding apparatus that performs the punching, drilling or laser-based perforation.
[B32B 2038/166] Removing moisture -- The code B32B 2038/166 designates processes for removing moisture from sheets, films, paper or similar substrates, typically as part of a coating operation. It includes drying techniques such as heating, air-stream, vacuum or other means applied before, during or after the application of a coating.
[B32B 2038/168] Removing solvent -- B32B 2038/168 covers methods for removing a solvent from a coated material, such as drying, evaporation, heating, vacuum or solvent extraction, to solidify or cure the coating or film after application.
[B32B 2038/1891] Using a robot for handling the layers -- The code B32B 2038/1891 refers to methods in which a robotic system is employed to manipulate or transport individual layers of sheet material during manufacturing. It covers robots that pick up, position, align, stack, or transfer layers for processes such as printing, coating, laminating, or assembly, allowing automated handling of thin or flexible substrates.
[B32B 2041/04] Detecting wrong registration, misalignment, deviation, failure -- B32B 2041/04 relates to sheet-metal forming processes and covers methods or apparatus for detecting registration errors, misalignment, deviation or failure during the operation, such as monitoring the correct positioning of parts, identifying improper feed or alignment, and signalling corrective action to prevent defective products.
[B32B 2041/06] Starting the lamination machine or method -- The code B32B 2041/06 relates to the initiation of laminating equipment, covering methods and apparatus features used to start a lamination machine. It includes procedures for pre-heating, feeding sheets, and energising the drive system so that continuous laminating can commence. This classification is part of the broader B32B group for laminating processes.
[B32B 21/00] Layered products comprising wood, e.g. wood board, veneer, wood particle board -- This subclass covers layered wood products such as boards, veneers and wood particle board, formed by bonding flat or shaped wood layers or particles into composite structures.
[B32B 21/02] of fibres, chips, or particles -- B32B 21/02 concerns methods for making layered wood products-boards, veneers or particle board-using fibrous, chip or particulate wood material. It addresses the formation, bonding and shaping of these wood strands into flat or non-flat panels, including cellular or honeycomb structures.
[B32B 21/04] comprising wood as the main or only constituent of a layer, next to another layer of a -- B32B 21/04 covers layered products in which a wood layer forms the primary or sole material of one stratum, positioned adjacent to another layer of a different material. This includes wood boards, veneers, particle board or honeycomb structures where wood constitutes a distinct layer within a composite.
[B32B 21/042] of wood  B32B21/13  takes precedence -- The Cooperative Patent Classification (CPC) entry B32B 21/042 pertains to layered products comprising wood, such as wood boards, veneer, or wood particle board. This classification is specific to products where the layer of wood takes precedence over other materials in the structure.
[B32B 21/045] of natural rubber or synthetic rubber -- B32B 21/045 covers layered wood products such as boards, veneers or particle boards that are combined with natural rubber or synthetic rubber, either as a bonding agent or as an integral material in the structure. It pertains to the manufacture of these composite panels where rubber provides flexibility, water resistance or adhesive properties within the wood layers.
[B32B 21/047] of foam -- This subclass covers layered wood products that incorporate foam as a core or inserted layer, such as wood-foam sandwich panels, veneer bonded to foam, or particle board with foam inclusions. It relates to the design and manufacture of wood-based laminated structures where foam provides lightweight or insulating characteristics.
[B32B 21/06] of paper or cardboard -- B32B 21/06 covers the manufacture or processing of layered products formed from paper or cardboard, for example corrugated sheets, sandwich panels and composite boards. The subclass falls under layered products built from flat or non-flat strata and is a child of the wood-based layered products group.
[B32B 21/08] of synthetic resin
[B32B 21/10] Next to a fibrous or filamentary layer -- This CPC subclass relates to layered wood products such as boards, veneers and particle board where a wood layer is positioned next to a fibrous or filamentary layer, often forming composite panels or sandwich structures. It covers the arrangement, bonding or processing of the wood layer adjacent to the non-wood fibrous layer.
[B32B 21/12] next to a particulate layer -- This subclass deals with methods or structures in which a particulate layer such as wood particles, fibers or granules is placed adjacent to another layer in a wood-based laminated product. It includes the formation of boards, veneers or particle boards where the particulate component is positioned next to a solid or honeycomb layer to achieve desired mechanical or aesthetic properties.
[B32B 21/13] all layers being exclusively wood -- B32B 21/13 classifies layered products whose entire structure consists solely of wood, such as wood boards, veneers, or wood particle boards built from flat or non-flat wooden strata, including honeycomb or cellular forms where every layer is wood.
[B32B 21/14] comprising wood board or veneer -- B32B 21/14 relates to layered products that incorporate wood board, veneer or similar wood-based sheets as constituent strata. It covers structures such as plywood, particle board, or honeycomb panels where at least one layer consists of wood board or veneer, fitting within the broader class of layered products in the Performing Operations section.
[B32B 2250/00] Layer arrangements -- B32B 2250/00 covers the arrangement of layers in multilayered or cellular products, such as honeycomb, foam or other structured sheets. It includes the order, orientation, spacing and bonding of individual strata to achieve a desired overall form or mechanical performance. The code is used for patents concerning the design and assembly of such layered structures.
[B32B 2250/02] 2 layers -- This subclass covers products built from exactly two stacked layers, whether flat or shaped, such as sandwich panels, laminates, or honeycomb structures with a pair of distinct strata. It addresses the arrangement, bonding and functional interaction of the two layers.
[B32B 2250/03] 3 layers -- The CPC subclass B32B 2250/03 covers methods for forming layered products that are built up with exactly three distinct strata. It relates to arranging three flat or non-flat layers-such as in honeycomb, cellular or sandwich structures-during the manufacturing process. This entry is part of the broader category of performing operations on layered products.
[B32B 2250/04] 4 layers -- This CPC subclass covers products built up of exactly four distinct layers of material, whether flat, curved, cellular or honey-comb, with the layers arranged in a defined sequence as part of the final layered product.
[B32B 2250/05] 5 or more layers -- B32B 2250/05 designates layered products that consist of five or more strata, including flat or non-flat configurations such as cellular or honeycomb structures. It falls under the CPC section for performing operations on layered products, focusing on layer arrangements.
[B32B 2250/20] All layers being fibrous or filamentary -- This CPC subclass of layered products (B32B 2250/20) covers items whose each stratum is made of fibrous or filamentary material, such as fabrics, non-woven mats, paper or fiber-reinforced sheets, assembled into multi-layer structures. It includes methods for producing and employing such layered constructions where all layers share a fibrous character.
[B32B 2250/22] All layers being foamed -- B32B 2250/22 covers layered products in which every layer is formed by a foaming process, such as foamed plastics, metal or ceramic foams, creating a composite structure of multiple foam strata. It applies to manufacturing methods and finished articles where each stratum results from expansion of a material, often to achieve lightweight, insulated or absorptive characteristics.
[B32B 2250/24] All layers being polymeric -- This CPC subclass concerns layered products in which each stratum is formed from a polymer. It covers the design, creation and arrangement of polymeric layers in composites, cellular or honeycomb structures, and similar multi-layer configurations. The focus is on the use of polymer materials for all layers.
[B32B 2250/242] All polymers belonging to those covered by group -- B32B 2250/242 covers the use of any polymer that belongs to the groups defined in the preceding subclass for creating layered products, such as cellular or honeycomb structures, by specifying the arrangement of the layers. It falls under the CPC hierarchy Performing Operations → Layered Products → Layered Products, i.e., products built up of flat or non-flat strata.
[B32B 2250/244] All polymers belonging to those covered by group -- This CPC subclass B32B 2250/244 covers layered products that incorporate any polymer belonging to the groups defined in the preceding class, such as polymeric honeycomb or cellular structures. It pertains to the use of these polymers in manufacturing flat or non-flat strata that form composite panels, cores, or similar multi-layered components.
[B32B 2250/246] All polymers belonging to those covered by groups -- B32B 2250/246 classifies layered products built from polymeric strata, such as honeycomb or cellular structures, where the polymers used belong to the groups defined in the preceding subclasses. It addresses the arrangement of flat or non-flat layers and applies to any polymer that falls within those referenced groups.
[B32B 2250/248] All polymers belonging to those covered by group -- B32B 2250/248 designates layered products-such as foams, honeycombs or other strati-structured items-where the constituent material is any polymer included in the referenced polymer group, without limiting the description to a particular polymer type or formulation. It covers all such polymers used to build up flat or non-flat strata.
[B32B 2250/26] All layers being made of paper or paperboard -- This CPC group covers layered products where every layer is formed from paper or paperboard, such as multi-layered boards, cartons, or honeycomb structures made solely of paper material. It applies to manufacturing processes and designs of such paper-based stratified items.
[B32B 2250/40] Symmetrical or sandwich layers, e.g. ABA, ABCBA, ABCCBA -- The code B32B 2250/40 covers layered products that are built from repeating or mirrored sequences of layers, such as ABA, ABCBA or ABCCBA arrangements. It applies to structures where the layer order is symmetrical, often used for sandwich or honeycomb-type materials that benefit from balanced mechanical or thermal properties.
[B32B 2250/42] Alternating layers, e.g. ABAB(C), AABBAABB(C) -- B32B 2250/42 classifies layered products whose strata are arranged in repeating alternating sequences, such as ABAB, AABBAABB or similar patterns, often used in cellular, honeycomb or other flat and non-flat constructions. The entry covers the design and manufacture of these specific layer arrangements within the broader group of performing operations for layered materials.
[B32B 2250/44] Number of layers variable across the laminate -- B32B 2250/44 covers laminates whose layer count varies across the sheet or component, such as variable-thickness honeycomb or cellular structures. It relates to the production of layered products where the number of strata is not uniform.
[B32B 2255/00] Coating on the layer surface -- This group is for classification of coatings on a layered product. Specific details of coatings or processes thereof can be found in C08J7/00 , B05D , C09D , C09J , C23C or D06M .
[B32B 2255/02] on fibrous or filamentary layer -- B32B 2255/02 covers applying a coating to a fibrous or filamentary layer that is part of a multi-layered product, such as fabric, non-woven mats or rope, where the coating alters surface properties, adds protection, or provides additional functionality. It resides in the CPC hierarchy under performing operations on layered products, specifically coatings on the layer surface.
[B32B 2255/04] on a particulate layer -- B32B 2255/04 covers methods of applying a coating to a particulate layer, i.e., a surface formed from a stratum of loose or bound particles such as powders, granules or beads. It falls within the layered-products subclass of performing operations, addressing how coatings are deposited onto these particle-based strata for functional or protective purposes.
[B32B 2255/06] on metal layer -- The code B32B 2255/06 covers methods for applying a coating specifically onto a metal layer that forms part of a layered product such as cellular, honeycomb or other stratified structures. It pertains to the surface treatment of the metal stratum during the fabrication of multilayered components.
[B32B 2255/062] metal layer being a foamed layer -- This CPC subclass concerns the application of a metal coating that itself is a foamed structure, i.e. a metal layer containing a cellular or honey-comb framework. It is used to produce layered products where the metal layer provides structural, thermal or acoustic benefits while retaining a lightweight, porous architecture.
[B32B 2255/08] on wood layer -- The CPC subclass B32B 2255/08 concerns layered products that incorporate a wood layer and the application of a coating on the surface of that wood layer. It covers processes, materials and treatments used to protect, decorate or add functionality to wood strata in panels, honeycomb cores or other multi-stratified structures.
[B32B 2255/10] on synthetic resin layer or on natural or synthetic rubber layer -- The classification B32B 2255/10 refers to coating operations performed on a synthetic resin layer or on a natural or synthetic rubber layer that form part of a multilayered product such as cellular or honeycomb structures. It is situated in the CPC hierarchy under Performing Operations, Layered Products and the sub-category Coating on the layer surface.
[B32B 2255/102] synthetic resin or rubber layer being a foamed layer -- This subclass covers layered products where a synthetic resin or rubber layer is formed as a foam and applied as a coating to the surface of another layer, such as cellular, honeycomb, or other structured substrates. It addresses the creation of foamed polymer or elastomer skins that bond to underlying strata in composite structures.
[B32B 2255/12] on paper layer -- B32B 2255/12 classifies processes for applying a coating to a paper layer that forms part of a multilayered product such as a cellular, honeycomb or other stratified structure. The entry covers techniques for treating the surface of the paper layer to achieve desired functional or protective properties within the overall laminated assembly.
[B32B 2255/20] Inorganic coating -- B32B 2255/20 refers to the application of inorganic coatings on the surface of layered products, such as cellular, honeycomb or other stratified structures. It covers processes that deposit non-organic films onto flat or non-flat layers to provide protection, functional properties or aesthetic effects.
[B32B 2255/205] Metallic coating -- The B32B 2255/205 subclass concerns applying a metallic coating to the surface of a layered product, such as a cellular, honeycomb, or other striated structure, whether flat or non-flat. It covers methods and compositions for depositing metal layers onto the layers to impart properties like conductivity, corrosion resistance, or visual finish.
[B32B 2255/24] Organic non-macromolecular coating -- B32B 2255/24 pertains to organic non-macromolecular coatings applied to the surfaces of layered products, including flat, cellular or honeycomb structures. It falls within the CPC hierarchy under Performing Operations → Layered Products → Coating on the layer surface, describing processes for depositing thin organic films that are not polymeric.
[B32B 2255/26] Polymeric coating -- B32B 2255/26 covers the application of polymeric coatings to the surfaces of layered structures such as honeycomb or cellular panels. It pertains to methods for depositing or curing polymer films that protect, seal, or modify the functional properties of each stratum. The classification is used for patents involving coating processes on non-flat layered products.
[B32B 2255/28] Multiple coating on one surface -- B32B 2255/28 covers processes or products in which more than one coating is applied to the same surface of a layered product, for example sequential paint, polymer, or metal layers on a honeycomb or cellular substrate. The classification is used for inventions that deposit multiple functional or protective films on a single face of a stratified structure.
[B32B 2260/00] Layered product comprising an impregnated, embedded, or bonded layer wherein the layer comprises an impregnation, embedding, or binder material -- B32B 2260/00 pertains to layered products in which one or more layers are impregnated, embedded, or bonded with a filler, binder, or other material, creating a composite stratum that may be flat or shaped like cellular or honeycomb structures. The classification addresses the manufacturing of such multi-layered assemblies where the functional layer is integrated by impregnation or bonding techniques.
[B32B 2260/02] Composition of the impregnated, bonded or embedded layer -- The subclass B32B 2260/02 concerns the specific materials and formulations used to impregnate, embed or bond a layer within a layered product such as honeycomb, cellular or other stratified structures. It covers compositions of resins, adhesives, polymers, metals, ceramics or similar binders that give the layer mechanical strength, adhesion or other functional properties.
[B32B 2260/021] Fibrous or filamentary layer -- It relates to layered products where one of the layers is made of fibrous or filamentary material, typically used as reinforcement or support, which may be impregnated with resin, embedded, or bonded to other layers to form composite structures such as honeycomb, cellular, or sandwich panels.
[B32B 2260/023] Two or more layers -- B32B 2260/023 covers layered products that consist of two or more strata in which at least one layer is impregnated, embedded or bonded to another material, forming a composite structure such as cellular, honeycomb or other non-flat configurations. The classification pertains to the manufacture of such multi-layered articles where the layers are integral through a binder, impregnant or embedding medium.
[B32B 2260/025] Particulate layer -- B32B 2260/025 covers layered products that include a particulate layer formed by impregnation, embedding or bonding of particles with a binder or matrix material, such as honeycomb or cellular structures where the layer is integrated into the overall product. This subclass falls under performing operations for layered products and concerns the construction of strata that incorporate particulate reinforcement or filling.
[B32B 2260/026] Wood layer -- The CPC subclass B32B 2260/026 covers layered products in which a wood layer is incorporated, possibly impregnated, embedded or bonded to adjoining strata. It falls under the broader category of layered products built from flat or non-flat strata such as honeycomb or cellular structures.
[B32B 2260/028] Paper layer -- The CPC class B32B 2260/028 covers paper layers that constitute an impregnated, embedded or bonded stratum within a layered product. It applies to composite structures built from multiple strata, such as cellular or honeycomb forms, where the paper provides reinforcement or functional properties through impregnation or bonding.
[B32B 2260/04] Impregnation, embedding, or binder material -- The subclass B32B 2260/04 covers layered products whose layers are treated with an impregnation, embedding or binder substance, such as resins, adhesives, polymers or other consolidating agents, to reinforce, seal or modify the structure. It applies to configurations like cellular, honey-comb or other striated builds where the added material penetrates or bonds the individual strata, improving mechanical strength, durability or functional performance.
[B32B 2260/042] Bituminous or tarry substance -- The subclass B32B 2260/042 concerns layered products whose impregnated, embedded or bonded layer uses a bituminous or tarry substance as the binder. It applies to items such as panels, roofing sheets or composites where bitumen or tar fills pores, adheres layers together or provides waterproofing within the stratified structure.
[B32B 2260/044] Water-setting substance, e.g. concrete, plaster -- It covers compositions that set by reacting with water, such as concrete and plaster, employed as the impregnating, embedding or binder layer in a multilayered structure. These substances form the solid matrix that holds together the strata of flat or non-flat layers in products like honeycomb or cellular panels.
[B32B 2260/046] Synthetic resin -- B32B 2260/046 covers synthetic resin employed as the impregnation, embedding or binder material in layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures. The resin forms an impregnated or bonded layer that gives strength and stability to the strati of flat or non-flat panels.
[B32B 2260/048] Natural or synthetic rubber -- The code B32B 2260/048 identifies layered products in which a layer of natural or synthetic rubber is impregnated, embedded or bonded to a substrate, forming a stratum within cellular, honeycomb or other flat or non-flat structures. This subclass covers the use of rubber as the impregnation, embedding or binder material that provides strength, flexibility or sealing in such multi-layered constructions.
[B32B 2262/00] Composition or structural features of fibres which form a fibrous or filamentary layer or are present as additives -- This CPC subclass B32B 2262/00 covers compositions and structural features of fibres that form a fibrous or filamentary layer or are employed as additives in layered products such as cellular or honey-comb structures. It is situated under Performing Operations → Layered Products in the hierarchy.
[B32B 2262/02] Synthetic macromolecular fibres -- B32B 2262/02 classifies synthetic macromolecular fibres based on their composition or structural characteristics when they form a fibrous or filamentary layer or act as additives in layered products such as cellular, honeycomb or other stratified structures. The entry covers polymeric fibre formulations, cross-linking, surface treatments and incorporated modifiers that affect the performance of these layered materials.
[B32B 2262/0207] Elastomeric fibres -- B32B 2262/0207 pertains to elastomeric fibres used in layered products such as cellular, honeycomb or other stratified structures. It falls under the CPC hierarchy of Performing Operations → Layered Products → Composition or structural features of fibres, covering materials that provide elastic or rubber-like characteristics within the individual layers.
[B32B 2262/0215] Thermoplastic elastomer fibers -- B32B 2262/0215 covers thermoplastic elastomer fibers that form or reinforce fibrous or filamentary layers in structured products such as cellular, honey-comb or other layered assemblies. The classification addresses the composition and structural characteristics of these elastomeric fibers, whether they constitute the primary layer or are incorporated as additives to modify mechanical or functional properties.
[B32B 2262/0223] Vinyl resin fibres -- B32B 2262/0223 relates to vinyl-resin fibers used as components of layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures. The classification covers the composition of the fibers and any structural features, including additives, that influence the formation of flat or non-flat fibrous layers.
[B32B 2262/023] Aromatic vinyl resin, e.g. styrenic (co)polymers -- B32B 2262/023 covers aromatic vinyl resins, including styrenic copolymers, that are employed in layered products such as cellular or honey-comb structures. The subclass focuses on the composition and structural features of fibres forming or added to these flat or non-flat strata.
[B32B 2262/0238] Vinyl halide, e.g. PVC, PVDC, PVF, PVDF -- The CPC entry B32B 2262/0238 covers layered products whose fibrous or filamentary layers are made from vinyl-halide polymers such as PVC, PVDC, PVF or PVDF, focusing on the composition and structural characteristics of these fibers or their use as additives within the strata. [B32B 2262/0246] Acrylic resin fibres -- The code B32B 2262/0246 pertains to acrylic resin fibres that form the fibrous layer or serve as additives in layered products such as cellular or honey-comb structures. [B32B 2262/0253] Polyolefin fibres -- B32B 2262/0253 covers polyolefin fibres used in layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures. It relates to the composition and structural features of fibres that form a fibrous layer or act as additives in those constructions.
[B32B 2262/0261] Polyamide fibres -- The CPC entry B32B 2262/0261 addresses polyamide fibres used in layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures, focusing on their composition and structural characteristics when forming fibrous or filamentary layers or serving as additives. It is classified under Performing Operations → Layered Products → Composition or structural features of fibres.
[B32B 2262/0269] Aromatic polyamide fibres -- The CPC entry B32B 2262/0269 refers to fibres produced from aromatic polyamide polymers, such as aramids, characterised by rigid, heat-resistant backbones and high tensile strength. These fibres are used in layered products like composites, protective textiles and honeycomb structures, where their unique structural features and additive compositions are critical.
[B32B 2262/0276] Polyester fibres -- The B32B 2262/0276 subgroup addresses polyester fibres employed in layered or cellular products such as honeycomb, cellular panels and other stratified structures. It covers the composition, morphology and any additives of the fibres that influence the formation, strength or other functional properties of the fibrous layers within these multi-strata constructions.
[B32B 2262/0284] Polyethylene terephthalate [PET] or polybutylene terephthalate [PBT] -- The CPC subclass B32B 2262/0284 concerns layered products made from polyethylene terephthalate (PET) or polybutylene terephthalate (PBT), addressing the composition and structural features of fibres that form a fibrous or filamentary layer or act as additives in flat or non-flat strata such as cellular or honeycomb forms.
[B32B 2262/0292] Polyurethane fibres -- The CPC subclass B32B 2262/0292 covers polyurethane fibres used as structural or additive components in layered products such as foams, honeycombs or other cellular materials. It includes the composition, preparation and structural characteristics of these polymeric filaments when incorporated into flat or non-flat strata. This classification is applied to patents dealing with the manufacture or modification of polyurethane fibre layers.
[B32B 2262/04] Cellulosic plastic fibres, e.g. rayon -- This CPC subgroup pertains to layered products that incorporate cellulosic plastic fibres such as rayon, focusing on the composition and structural characteristics of the fibres when they form a fibrous or filamentary layer or act as additives.
[B32B 2262/06] Vegetal fibres -- B32B 2262/06 concerns vegetable-derived fibres that are incorporated into or form the fibrous or filamentary layers of layered products such as honeycomb, cellular or other stratified structures, describing their composition and structural characteristics when used as primary layers or additives.
[B32B 2262/062] Cellulose fibres, e.g. cotton -- This subclass covers layered products that incorporate cellulose fibres such as cotton, focusing on the composition and structural characteristics of the fibres when they form a fibrous or filamentary layer or serve as additives in the material.

It pertains to the design, manufacture or modification of stratified materials that incorporate these plant-based fibres for reinforcement, texture or functional properties.
[B32B 2262/067] Wood fibres -- B32B 2262/067 concerns wood fibres used in layered products such as cellular or honey-comb structures. It addresses the composition, structural characteristics and the role of wood fibres as a fibrous or filamentary layer or as additives that modify the properties of the product.

It is nested under Performing Operations → Layered Products → Composition or structural features of fibres.
[B32B 2262/10] Inorganic fibres -- B32B 2262/10 covers inorganic fibres used in layered products, addressing the composition and structural characteristics of fibrous or filamentary layers and any fibre additives. This classification applies to products built from flat or non-flat strata such as cellular or honeycomb forms.
[B32B 2262/101] Glass fibres -- B32B 2262/101 covers glass fibres used in or added to layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures. [B32B 2262/103] Metal fibres -- B32B 2262/103 covers metal fibres that are incorporated as structural or additive elements in layered products such as honeycomb or cellular structures. The code addresses the composition, geometry and arrangement of metallic filaments that form a fibrous layer within the product.
[B32B 2262/105] Ceramic fibres -- Ceramic fibres are classified under B32B 2262/105. This code falls under layered products with fibrous or filamentary layers. It involves composition or structural features of fibres.
[B32B 2262/106] Carbon fibres, e.g. graphite fibres -- This subgroup covers carbon or graphite fibers used as reinforcing elements in layered products such as honeycomb, cellular or other stratified structures. It relates to the composition and structural features of these fibers when forming a fibrous layer or acting as additives in the material.
[B32B 2262/108] Rockwool fibres -- Rockwool fibres are inorganic mineral-wool filaments produced by spinning molten rock or basalt into a fibrous web that is then bonded into a non-woven mat. Their high thermal resistance, fire-retardancy and acoustic absorption make them a common component of layered products such as insulation panels, acoustic boards and honeycomb structures.
[B32B 2262/12] Conjugate fibres, e.g. core/sheath or side-by-side -- Conjugate fibres are composite filaments in which two or more distinct polymer components are combined in a single strand, typically as a core-sheath or side-by-side arrangement, to impart complementary mechanical, thermal or functional properties. The classification covers their composition and structural features within layered products such as honeycomb or cellular structures.
[B32B 2262/124] Non-woven fabric -- The CPC subclass B32B 2262/124 covers non-woven fabrics, focusing on the composition and structural characteristics of the fibres that create a fibrous or filamentary layer or act as additives. It is placed under layered products, specifically those built from strata of flat or non-flat forms such as cellular or honeycomb structures. This subclass details the material makeup and arrangement of fibres in non-woven textile products.
[B32B 2262/128] Woven fabric -- The CPC subclass B32B 2262/128 covers woven fabric as a layered product where fibres are interlaced to form a textile sheet. It addresses the composition and structural features of the fibres that make up the woven layer or serve as additives, and is relevant to manufacturing processes that create flat or shaped laminates.
[B32B 2262/132] Knitted fabric -- The subclass B32B 2262/132 concerns knitted fabrics in which yarns are interlooped to create a continuous fibrous layer, covering plain, rib, jersey and other knit structures. [B32B 2262/136] Net structure -- The code covers net structures formed by interlaced fibres or filaments that make up a layer in composite, cellular or honeycomb products, addressing their geometry, bonding methods and any additive components. It falls within the CPC hierarchy for layered products under performing operations.

[B32B 2266/0214] Materials belonging to -- The Cooperative Patent Classification entry B32B 2266/0214 pertains to the composition of foam materials used in layered products, specifically addressing the types of materials that constitute these foams. This classification is part of a broader hierarchy dealing with performing operations and layered products.
[B32B 2266/0221] Vinyl resin -- The B32B 2266/0221 entry covers the use of vinyl-based resin in foam compositions for layered products such as cellular, honeycomb or other strati­fied structures. It pertains to formulations where a vinyl polymer acts as the matrix or binder in the creation of flat or non-flat layered foam items.
[B32B 2266/0228] Aromatic vinyl resin, e.g. styrenic (co)polymers -- Aromatic vinyl resins such as styrenic homopolymers or copolymers are polymeric materials based on aromatic vinyl monomers that can be formulated into foam compositions. They are used to create layered products whose structure consists of flat or non-flat strata, including cellular or honeycomb forms.
[B32B 2266/0235] Vinyl halide, e.g. PVC, PVDC, PVF, PVDF -- B32B 2266/0235 covers the preparation of foam structures made from vinyl-halide polymers such as poly(vinyl chloride), poly(vinylidene chloride), poly(vinyl fluoride) and poly(vinylidene fluoride). It is applied to layered products, including cellular or honeycomb forms, where the foam constitutes the primary material. The entry falls under performing operations for layered products.
[B32B 2266/0242] Acrylic resin -- B32B 2266/0242 covers the use of acrylic resin as a material in the manufacture of layered products, particularly foams and other cellular or honey-comb structures. The entry falls under performing operations for layered products and specifies the composition of foam incorporating acrylic resin.
[B32B 2266/025] Polyolefin -- The CPC subclass B32B 2266/025 covers foamed structures made from polyolefin polymers, such as polyethylene or polypropylene, used as layered products like honeycomb, cellular or other stratified forms. It pertains to the composition of the foam material rather than the manufacturing process, focusing on the polyolefin matrix that provides the desired mechanical or thermal properties.
[B32B 2266/0257] Polyamide -- B32B 2266/0257 covers foamed compositions in which the polymer matrix is a polyamide, such as nylon, forming a layered structure that may be flat, cellular or honey-comb. It includes the preparation and shaping of polyamide foam products, detailing the material's formulation, foaming agents and processing conditions.
[B32B 2266/0264] Polyester -- B32B 2266/0264 defines polyester as a material used in the composition of foam within layered products, such as cellular or honeycomb structures. It falls under the hierarchy performing operations → layered products → layered products, i.e. products built-up of strata of flat or non-flat form.
[B32B 2266/0271] Epoxy resin -- This subclass covers the use of epoxy resin in the manufacture of layered foamed structures such as cellular or honeycomb panels. It concerns the composition of foam where epoxy resin acts as the matrix material, enabling the formation of flat or non-flat strata. The classification falls under performing operations for layered products.
[B32B 2266/0278] Polyurethane -- The CPC class B32B 2266/0278 refers to the production of polyurethane foam as a layered product, covering processes that create flat or non-flat strata such as cellular or honeycomb structures. It falls under Performing Operations → Layered Products, specifically the composition of foam, and includes methods for forming, shaping and treating polyurethane layers.
[B32B 2266/0285] Condensation resins of aldehydes, e.g. with phenols, ureas, melamines -- The CPC entry B32B 2266/0285 relates to foam compositions formed by condensation of aldehydes with compounds such as phenols, ureas or melamines. It covers the preparation and use of these polymeric foams in layered products, including flat or non-flat structures like cellular, honeycomb or other stratified materials. This subclass falls under the broader categories of performing operations and layered products.
[B32B 2266/0292] Thermoplastic elastomer -- The CPC entry B32B 2266/0292 covers the composition of foam made from thermoplastic elastomers, focusing on processes that produce layered structures such as flat, cellular or honeycomb strata. It falls under the performing-operations group for layered products, describing how these elastomeric foams are formulated and manufactured.
[B32B 2266/031] Bituminous or tarry material -- The CPC class B32B 2266/031 covers layered products in which the foam matrix or cellular structure is formed from bituminous or tarry material. It applies to compositions where bitumen, tar or similar viscous substances serve as the primary binder or filler in the creation of foamed, honey-comb or other stratified forms.
[B32B 2266/04] Inorganic -- B32B 2266/04 concerns foamed products whose matrix is formed from inorganic materials such as metals, ceramics, glass or mineral compounds. It includes processes and compositions for producing cellular or honey-comb structures where the foam is built up of flat or non-flat strata, covering the preparation of inorganic foams and their resulting layered forms.
[B32B 2266/045] Metal -- This CPC entry covers the preparation, shaping and treatment of metal foams and other layered metal structures such as honeycomb, focusing on compositions where metal forms the primary material in cellular or stratified products.
[B32B 2266/049] Water-setting material, e.g. concrete, plaster or asbestos cement -- A water-setting material such as concrete, plaster or asbestos cement is classified under CPC B32B 2266/049, placed in the layered-products branch of performing-operations. These materials form a solid matrix by setting with water and are considered as layered or cellular structures, often related to foam compositions.
[B32B 2266/053] Mineral element, e.g. asbestos or mica -- The Cooperative Patent Classification code B32B 2266/053 pertains to the composition of foam in layered products, specifically focusing on the inclusion of mineral elements such as asbestos or mica. This classification is used by the European Patent Office and the United States Patent and Trademark Office for patent documentation.
[B32B 2266/057] Silicon-containing material, e.g. glass -- B32B 2266/057 pertains to foamed layered products that incorporate silicon-containing materials such as glass. It covers processes for forming cellular or honeycomb structures where glass or similar silicon-based substances are used as a component of the foam composition.
[B32B 2266/06] Open cell foam -- Open cell foam is a porous cellular material whose cells are interconnected, allowing air or liquids to pass through the structure. It is produced as a layered product and is used for cushioning, sound absorption, thermal insulation, filtration and similar applications where breathability and shock-absorption are required.
[B32B 2266/08] Closed cell foam -- B32B 2266/08 pertains to closed-cell foam, a layered material in which the individual cells are sealed and filled with gas or air, giving the foam a rigid, non-permeable structure. It falls under the broader categories of performing operations and layered products, specifically dealing with the composition of foam.
[B32B 2266/10] characterised by the foam pores -- A CPC subclass for layered products, focusing on foams whose internal structure is defined by the shape, size or arrangement of the pores. It covers compositions where the porous foam itself provides the distinguishing feature of the product.
[B32B 2266/102] Nanopores, i.e. with average diameter smaller than 0.1 µm -- The code B32B 2266/102 designates nanopores-pores whose average diameter is under 0.1 µm-incorporated in foam or other layered products built of flat or non-flat strata such as cellular or honeycomb structures. It covers the composition and manufacturing of such fine-scale porous materials.
[B32B 2266/104] Micropores, i.e. with average diameter in the range from 0.1 µm to 0.1 mm -- B32B 2266/104 covers the creation of micropores-tiny voids whose average diameter ranges from 0.1 µm up to 0.1 mm-within foam or other layered structures. The code is used for processes that generate or control such pores to achieve specific mechanical, thermal or acoustic properties in cellular, honeycomb or similar materials.
[B32B 2266/106] Unimodal pore distribution -- The B32B 2266/106 subclass covers foams whose pores are distributed according to a single, most-frequent size range, i.e., a unimodal pore-size distribution. It applies to layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures where the pore geometry follows one predominant diameter rather than multiple distinct peaks.
[B32B 2266/108] Bimodal pore distribution -- B32B 2266/108 pertains to foam compositions engineered with two distinct pore-size ranges, creating a bimodal pore distribution that can enhance mechanical strength, thermal insulation or other functional properties. The classification applies to layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures where the pore architecture is deliberately controlled during manufacture.
[B32B 2266/12] Gel -- A gel is a semi-solid, cross-linked polymer network that retains a large amount of liquid within its structure, giving it a jelly-like consistency. In the context of layered products, it is treated as a type of foam composition where the dispersed phase forms continuous, often cellular, strata.
[B32B 2266/122] Hydrogel, i.e. a gel containing an aqueous composition -- B32B 2266/122 covers hydrogels, which are gelled materials that contain an aqueous composition and are used as a type of foam or layered product formed from water-based polymers. The classification falls under performing operations for layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures.
[B32B 2266/124] Organogel, i.e. a gel containing an organic composition -- The CPC entry B32B 2266/124 refers to organogels, which are gels whose continuous phase consists of an organic liquid rather than water. These materials form a three-dimensional network that immobilises the organic phase, giving a semi-solid consistency useful in areas such as pharmaceuticals, cosmetics, and food technology. It falls under the hierarchy of Performing Operations → Layered Products → Composition of foam.
[B32B 2266/126] Aerogel, i.e. a supercritically dried gel -- Aerogels are ultra-light, porous solids obtained by supercritical drying of a gel, creating a network of interconnected pores that retain the shape of the original gel while dramatically reducing density. The CPC subclass B32B 2266/126 classifies these materials as layered products because their internal structure consists of a continuous matrix of flat or non-flat striated cells, such as honeycomb or foam. They are widely used for thermal insulation, acoustic damping, and lightweight structural applications.
[B32B 2266/128] Xerogel, i.e. an air dried gel -- Xerogel, an air-dried gel, is classified under CPC B32B 2266/128, which falls within the performing-operations branch for layered products such as foams, cellular or honeycomb structures. This code covers the preparation and composition of xerogels, emphasizing their formation from gel precursors that are removed of liquid by drying. It is used to catalogue methods of producing solid, porous materials with retained structural integrity.
[B32B 2266/14] Adhesive foam -- The B32B 2266/14 entry covers adhesive foams, which are foam compositions that incorporate a binding agent to enable the material to stick to surfaces during or after curing. These foams are used in layered products such as honeycomb, cellular or other stratified structures where the adhesive component provides structural integrity and attachment.
[B32B 2270/00] Resin or rubber layer containing a blend of at least two different polymers -- The Cooperative Patent Classification code B32B 2270/00 pertains to layered products with a resin or rubber layer that contains a blend of at least two different polymers, focusing on the composition and structure of these specific layers within multi-layered materials.
[B32B 2272/00] Resin or rubber layer comprising scrap, waste or recycling material -- B32B 2272/00 covers the production of laminated products in which a layer of resin or rubber incorporates scrap, waste or recycled material. It falls under the layered products subclass of performing operations, dealing with flat or non-flat strata such as honeycomb or cellular structures. The code is used by the EPO and USPTO to classify such environmentally-focused manufacturing processes.
[B32B 2274/00] Thermoplastic elastomer material -- B32B 2274/00 designates thermoplastic elastomer material, a polymer that can be processed like a thermoplastic while retaining elastomeric elasticity, intended for use in layered products such as cellular, honey-comb or other stratified structures. It falls under the Performing Operations → Layered Products hierarchy, describing flexible, recoverable components built from flat or non-flat strata.
[B32B 23/00] Layered products comprising cellulosic plastic substances -- B32B 23/00 covers the manufacture of layered structures that incorporate cellulosic plastic materials, such as composites formed from paper, pulp or cellulose derivatives combined with polymer matrices. These products are built up as flat or non-flat strata, including honeycomb or cellular configurations, and are used where strength, lightness or barrier properties are required.
[B32B 23/02] in the form of fibres or filaments -- B32B 23/02 relates to layered products composed of cellulosic plastic substances that are manufactured as fibres or filaments, such as cellulose-based filamentary materials having a cellular, honeycomb or other stratified structure.
[B32B 23/04] comprising such substance as the main or only constituent of a layer, next to another layer of a -- The Cooperative Patent Classification entry B32B 23/04 pertains to layered products where cellulosic plastic substances are used as the primary or sole component of a layer, adjacent to another distinct layer. This classification is part of a broader hierarchy that deals with performing operations and layered products in general.
[B32B 23/042] of metal -- B32B 23/042 pertains to layered products where one or more layers are composed of cellulosic plastic substances, and at least one layer is made of metal. This classification is part of the Cooperative Patent Classification system used by the European Patent Office and the United States Patent and Trademark Office.
[B32B 23/044] of wood -- The CPC subclass B32B 23/044 covers layered products that incorporate wood as a cellulosic-plastic material. It pertains to structures built from flat or non-flat strata, such as honeycomb or cellular forms, where wood serves as the primary component of the layered assembly.
[B32B 23/046] of natural rubber or synthetic rubber -- This subclass covers layered products built from strata of cellulosic plastic substances where the layers are made of natural rubber or synthetic rubber, such as honeycomb, foam or cellular structures using rubber as the matrix material. It is used to classify patents describing rubber-based layered composites.
[B32B 23/048] of foam -- The code B32B 23/048 covers foamed layered products that are made from cellulosic plastic substances, such as cellulose-based polymers expanded into a cellular structure. These foams are used as lightweight, insulating or cushioning layers in composite panels and similar constructions.
[B32B 2305/00] Condition, form, state or properties of the layers or laminate -- B32B 2305/00 relates to the condition, form, state or physical properties of the individual layers or laminates in a layered product. It classifies inventions that define, modify or control how each stratum behaves, is shaped or is treated within composite structures such as honeycomb, cellular or other multi-layered materials.
[B32B 2305/02] Cellular or porous -- This subclass covers layered products built from a network of cells or pores, such as honeycomb, foam or other cellular structures, where the layers are defined by the void geometry. It relates to the condition, form, state or properties of those cellular or porous laminates within the Performing Operations → Layered Products hierarchy.
[B32B 2305/022] Foam -- B32B 2305/022 covers foams, which are layered products formed by a network of gas-filled cells in a solid matrix, including both flat and three-dimensional cellular structures such as honeycomb, cellular plastics and other aerated materials. The class addresses the condition, form, state or properties of these layered or laminated foams used in various applications.
[B32B 2305/024] Honeycomb -- The B32B 2305/024 subclass covers honeycomb structures, a type of layered product formed from a regular array of cells that may be flat, curved or cellular in shape. It classifies the condition, form, state or physical properties of these honeycomb laminates, including the geometry of the cells, the material of the walls, and any surface treatments applied.
[B32B 2305/026] Porous -- B32B 2305/026 concerns layered or laminated products whose layers are porous, including cellular, honeycomb or other open-cell structures, and relates to the condition, form, state or properties of such porous layers.
[B32B 2305/028] Hollow fillers -- Hollow fillers are lightweight, void-containing particles incorporated into laminates or layered structures to reduce weight, improve insulation, or modify mechanical properties. They include cellular, honeycomb, or foamed inserts made of plastics, metals, ceramics or composites, and are used in sandwich panel cores or as discrete void-forming elements.
[B32B 2305/07] Parts immersed or impregnated in a matrix -- The CPC subclass B32B 2305/07 covers components that are placed in or saturated with a surrounding matrix material, such as fillers, reinforcements or inserts that become embedded during the formation of a layered product. It applies to parts that are immersed in liquids, resins or other binders and subsequently solidified to form a composite laminate, including honey-comb or cellular structures.
[B32B 2305/073] partially -- The CPC subclass B32B 2305/073 deals with operations on layered products where only part of the laminate is treated-such as partial curing, partial consolidation, partial polymerisation or other incomplete setting of the layers-so that some layers retain a different condition, form or state than the rest.
[B32B 2305/076] Prepregs -- The code B32B 2305/076 designates preparatory impregnated fiber materials, or prepregs, employed to build layered composites such as laminates, honeycomb or cellular structures, focusing on the condition, form, state and properties of the layers or laminate during manufacture.
[B32B 2305/08] Reinforcements -- B32B 2305/08 - Reinforcements refers to the condition, form, state or properties of layers or laminates in layered products such as cellular, honeycomb or non-flat structures. It covers any measures that strengthen or stiffen the strata, including added fibers, ribs, cores or other supportive elements.
[B32B 2305/10] Fibres of continuous length -- The CPC subgroup B32B 2305/10 pertains to layered or laminate products that incorporate fibres of continuous length, meaning the reinforcing fibres run uninterrupted through the structure. It addresses the condition, form, state or properties of such continuous fibres within cellular, honey-comb or other stratified materials.
[B32B 2305/18] Fabrics, textiles -- B32B 2305/18 classifies fabrics and textiles as layered products, concentrating on the condition, form, state or properties of their individual layers or laminates, such as flat, cellular or honeycomb structures, and how these characteristics affect the performance of the material.
[B32B 2305/182] knitted -- B32B 2305/182 classifies knitted configurations of layered products, including textiles, cellular or honeycomb structures, focusing on the condition, form, state or properties of the individual layers or the overall laminate.
[B32B 2305/184] Braided fabrics -- B32B 2305/184 classifies braided fabrics as a specific form of layered product in which individual filaments or yarns are interlaced to create a textile structure. It addresses the condition, shape, state and other properties of the resulting laminate, covering manufacturing techniques and functional characteristics of the braid. [B32B 2305/186] Knitted fabrics -- B32B 2305/186 classifies knitted fabrics as a type of layered product, emphasizing their condition, form, state or other properties. It pertains to textiles constructed from interlocking yarn loops that create a stratified structure, covering variations in thickness, surface texture, flexibility and other characteristics of the laminate.
[B32B 2305/188] Woven fabrics -- B32B 2305/188 covers woven fabrics as a type of layered product, focusing on the condition, form, state or properties of the individual layers or the laminate as a whole. [B32B 2305/20] in the form of a non-woven mat -- B32B 2305/20 covers layered products whose condition, form or state is a non-woven mat. [B32B 2305/22] Fibres of short length -- B32B 2305/22 covers short-length fibres used in the production of layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures, addressing the condition, form, state or properties of the layers or laminate.
[B32B 2305/24] Whiskers -- The B32B 2305/24 entry, titled Whiskers, covers the presence, formation or control of fine hair-like protrusions on the surface of layered products such as honeycomb or cellular structures. It addresses the condition, form or state of these whiskers, including methods to produce, modify or suppress them in laminates.
[B32B 2305/28] in the form of a mat -- This CPC subclass covers layered products that are manufactured, treated or used as a mat, a continuous flexible sheet formed from intersecting strands or fibers. It includes methods for forming, conditioning, or finishing such mats, which may serve as precursors or components of cellular, honey-comb or other non-flat laminates.
[B32B 2305/30] Fillers, e.g. particles, powders, beads, flakes, spheres, chips -- B32B 2305/30 covers the use of fillers-particles, powders, beads, flakes, spheres or chips-in layered products, specifying how such additives are incorporated to affect the condition, form, state or properties of the laminate, such as strength, weight, thermal or acoustic performance.
[B32B 2305/34] Inserts -- The CPC subclass B32B 2305/34 covers inserts that are placed within layered or laminated products, such as honeycomb, cellular or other multi-strata structures, to modify their condition, form, state or properties. It includes components positioned in voids or between layers for reinforcement, sealing, joining or functional enhancement of the laminate. This classification applies to the design and use of such inserts in composite panels and similar constructions.
[B32B 2305/342] Chips -- B32B 2305/342 covers chips, which are small separated fragments or cut pieces produced from layered or laminated products such as cellular, honeycomb or flat strata, focusing on their condition, shape, state or material properties within the laminate. It addresses how these chips are generated, characterized or employed in processes involving layered structures.
[B32B 2305/345] Heating elements -- The B32B 2305/345 subclass covers heating elements incorporated into layered products such as laminates, cellular or honeycomb structures. It addresses the design, placement and integration of thermal components that provide heat to or through the layers, affecting the condition, form or state of the composite material.
[B32B 2305/347] Security elements -- B32B 2305/347 relates to security elements incorporated into layered products such as laminated, cellular or honeycomb structures. It addresses the condition, form, state or properties of the layers that provide anti-counterfeiting, tamper-evident or protective functions, including embedded RFID tags, holograms, seals or similar protective features.
[B32B 2305/38] Meshes, lattices or nets -- The CPC subclass B32B 2305/38 concerns the condition, form, state or properties of meshes, lattices or nets that constitute layered products, such as structures built from flat or non-flat strata like cellular or honey-comb materials. It falls under performing operations for layered products and deals specifically with the geometry and characteristics of these interlaced or perforated layers.
[B32B 2305/54] Filled microcapsules -- This subclass covers layered or laminate products that incorporate microcapsules whose interior is filled with a functional material such as a liquid, gas or solid. The classification is applied to composites, foams, honeycomb or cellular structures where the filled capsules contribute to the mechanical, thermal or release properties of the material.
[B32B 2305/55] Liquid crystals -- B32B 2305/55 covers liquid-crystal materials as they relate to layered products, focusing on the condition, form, state or properties of the layers or laminates. [B32B 2305/70] Scrap or recycled material -- B32B 2305/70 concerns the use of scrap or recycled material in the manufacture of layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures, addressing the condition, form, state or properties of the layers or laminate.
[B32B 2305/72] Cured, e.g. vulcanised, cross-linked -- This subclass covers the curing or cross-linked treatment of layered or cellular products, such as vulcanising rubber sheets within a laminate. It includes methods that transform the layers into a chemically bonded, hardened state to improve strength, elasticity or heat resistance.
[B32B 2305/74] Partially cured -- B32B 2305/74 covers layered products whose individual layers have been only partially cured, meaning the polymerization or hardening reaction is incomplete. It pertains to the condition, form, state or properties of such partially cured strata in honeycomb, cellular or other laminate structures.
[B32B 2305/77] Uncured, e.g. green -- This subclass covers layered or laminate products that remain in an uncured or green state, meaning the constituent layers have not undergone the curing or hardening process. [B32B 2305/80] Sintered -- B32B 2305/80 classifies layered or laminated articles whose layers are formed, consolidated or finished by sintering, including cellular, honey-comb or foam structures made from powdered material.
