[B32B 2307/4026] within the layer by addition of a colorant, e.g. pigments, dyes -- B32B 2307/4026 relates to processes for introducing a colorant-such as pigments or dyes-into the interior of a layer of a laminated or cellular product, e.g., honeycomb, foam or other stratified structures, during or after the layer's formation.
[B32B 2307/404] Multi-coloured -- The sub-class B32B 2307/404 relates to layered products where the individual strata are coloured differently, covering multi-coloured laminates such as flat, cellular or honey-comb structures. It includes the characteristics of the coloured layers and methods for producing or applying such multi-coloured laminates.
[B32B 2307/406] Bright, glossy, shiny surface -- B32B 2307/406 covers layered products whose outer surface is bright, glossy or shiny, indicating a high-reflectance finish achieved by polishing, coating or inherent material properties. It applies to laminates, honeycomb or cellular structures where the surface appearance is a defining characteristic.
[B32B 2307/408] Matt, dull surface -- The CPC subclass B32B 2307/408 covers layered products that are designed to have a matt, non-reflective or dull surface finish. It falls under the hierarchy of performing operations → layered products → properties of the layers or laminate and is used for patents describing the manufacture or treatment of laminates where a matte appearance is a key characteristic.
[B32B 2307/409] Iridescent, pearlescent surface -- B32B 2307/409 covers layered products whose outer layers produce an iridescent or pearlescent appearance, achieved by optical effects such as interference, diffraction or scattering within the laminate structure. It applies to laminates, films or composites designed to display changing colours or a lustrous sheen when viewed from different angles.
[B32B 2307/41] Opaque -- B32B 2307/41 designates layered or laminate structures whose individual strata are opaque, meaning they do not allow light to pass through. This subclass pertains to the material and surface characteristics of non-transparent layers in honeycomb, cellular or other flat or non-flat composites.
[B32B 2307/412] Transparent -- The CPC subclass B32B 2307/412 covers layered or laminated products whose layers are designed to be transparent. It includes any process or material that provides optical clarity to flat, honeycomb, cellular or other striated structures, enabling light transmission through the laminate. This subclass falls under properties of layers within the broader category of layered products.
[B32B 2307/414] Translucent -- B32B 2307/414 concerns layered products that are translucent, meaning the structure of flat or non-flat strata, such as cellular or honeycomb laminates, permits light to pass through while maintaining structural integrity. The entry addresses the optical properties of the layers or laminates that give the material its partial transparency.
[B32B 2307/416] Reflective -- B32B 2307/416 covers layered products whose individual strata are designed to reflect electromagnetic radiation, such as light, by using reflective coatings, metallic films or surfaces with specular or diffuse reflectivity. It includes specifications of the reflective characteristics of each layer in laminates, honeycombs or cellular structures.
[B32B 2307/418] Refractive -- The subclass B32B 2307/418 covers the refractive characteristics of layered products such as laminates, honeycomb or cellular structures, focusing on how the layers affect light transmission, refraction or optical index. It includes methods for adjusting or measuring these optical properties in flat or non-flat stratified materials.
[B32B 2307/42] Polarizing, birefringent, filtering -- This subclass covers layered or laminated structures whose constituent sheets provide optical functions such as polarization, birefringence or selective filtering. It includes products like polarizing films, birefringent laminates and filter plates used in displays, lenses and optical equipment.
[B32B 2307/422] Luminescent, fluorescent, phosphorescent -- This subclass deals with layered products whose individual strata show luminescent, fluorescent or phosphorescent behaviour, meaning they emit visible light when excited by an energy source or retain light after exposure. It includes coatings, films, honeycomb, cellular structures and other laminates specifically designed to glow, fluoresce, or display after-glow characteristics.
[B32B 2307/50] having particular mechanical properties -- B32B 2307/50 covers layered or laminated products whose individual strata are characterised by specific mechanical properties such as strength, stiffness, impact resistance or elasticity. The code is applied when the performance of the laminate is defined by these mechanical attributes, rather than by its geometry, composition or manufacturing method, and sits within the CPC hierarchy under performing operations for layered products.
[B32B 2307/51] Elastic -- B32B 2307/51 covers the elastic characteristics of layered or laminated products, such as cellular, honeycomb or other stratified structures, describing how the layers deform under load and recover their shape. It pertains to the mechanical behavior of the strata that gives the overall product its flexibility or resilience.
[B32B 2307/514] Oriented -- B32B 2307/514 covers layered products whose individual strata are deliberately oriented to give the material specific directional characteristics, such as aligned fibers, cells or honeycomb structures that affect strength, stiffness or thermal behavior. The classification applies to processes and designs where the orientation of each layer is a defining property of the final laminate.
[B32B 2307/516] mono-axially -- B32B 2307/516 covers layered or laminate products whose individual layers are oriented or stressed in a single axial direction. The code applies to designs such as honeycomb or cellular panels where the mechanical or physical properties are defined primarily along one axis. It is used to classify inventions that exploit mono-axial characteristics for strength, stiffness or thermal behavior.
[B32B 2307/518] bi-axially -- B32B 2307/518 covers layered or laminate products whose layers are oriented or treated in two perpendicular directions, i.e., bi-axially. It relates to the properties that result from this dual-axis arrangement, such as strength, stiffness or thermal behavior, in structures like honeycomb, cellular or other flat and non-flat built-up panels.
[B32B 2307/52] multi-axially -- This CPC subclass covers layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures in which the individual strata are arranged in more than one axial direction, giving the material multi-axial reinforcement or functionality. It applies to methods and designs where layers are oriented at varying angles to achieve specific mechanical or physical properties.
[B32B 2307/536] Hardness -- The CPC subclass B32B 2307/536 concerns the hardness of layered products such as cellular, honeycomb or flat laminates. It covers methods for measuring, specifying and reporting hardness values of individual layers or the entire laminate, including related test procedures and the influence of layer properties on overall hardness.
[B32B 2307/538] Roughness -- The CPC subclass B32B 2307/538 covers the roughness characteristic of layers or laminates, describing surface texture, irregularities and tactile quality of flat or non-flat stratified products such as cellular or honeycomb structures. It addresses how the roughness of each stratum influences overall performance, handling, adhesion, wear resistance or aesthetic appearance of the finished composite.
[B32B 2307/54] Yield strength -- The CPC subclass B32B 2307/54 covers the measurement, specification or evaluation of the yield strength of layered products, such as laminates, honeycomb structures or cellular materials. It relates to the mechanical property at which the material begins to deform plastically under load, focusing on the behavior of the individual layers or the composite laminate as a whole.
[B32B 2307/542] Shear strength -- B32B 2307/542 pertains to the evaluation of shear strength of layered or laminate products such as honeycomb or cellular structures. It includes methods for measuring resistance to shear forces between layers and characterising the mechanical performance of the composite. The code is used for patents concerning testing procedures, apparatus or data related to shear strength of such stratified materials.
[B32B 2307/544] Torsion strength -- B32B 2307/544 relates to the determination of torsion strength for layered products, including honeycomb, cellular and other flat or non-flat laminates. It covers methods and apparatus used to assess the resistance of these strata-built structures to twisting forces.
[B32B 2307/546] Flexural strength -- B32B 2307/546 covers the determination or specification of flexural strength for layered products such as laminates, cellular, honeycomb or other stratified structures. It relates to assessing how much bending load a composite can sustain before failure, which is a key property for structural performance. This subclass falls under the broader group of properties of the layers or laminate.
[B32B 2307/548] Creep -- B32B 2307/548 pertains to methods for assessing or controlling creep deformation in layered products such as honeycomb, cellular or other stratified structures, including testing, measurement and treatment procedures aimed at evaluating long-term dimensional changes under sustained load.
[B32B 2307/552] Fatigue strength -- B32B 2307/552 addresses the fatigue strength of layered products such as flat or non-flat laminates, cellular panels and honeycomb structures. It covers methods for determining how repeated loading affects the durability of the individual layers and the composite as a whole.
[B32B 2307/554] Wear resistance -- B32B 2307/554 pertains to the wear resistance of layered products, including flat or non-flat laminates, cellular and honeycomb structures. The code classifies the properties of the layers that give the material durability against abrasion and mechanical wear.
[B32B 2307/558] Impact strength, toughness -- B32B 2307/558 relates to the measurement or evaluation of impact strength and toughness of layered products such as honeycomb, cellular or other multi-strata structures. It covers methods, apparatuses or criteria for determining how these laminates resist sudden loads or fractures, and the resulting performance characteristics of the material's layers.
[B32B 2307/56] Damping, energy absorption -- The CPC subclass B32B 2307/56 concerns layered products-such as cellular or honeycomb structures-designed to provide damping or energy-absorption functions. It covers materials and constructions whose laminate or stratified architecture is intended to reduce vibration, shock or impact by dissipating mechanical energy.
[B32B 2307/58] Cuttability -- B32B 2307/58 covers the cuttability of layered products, such as honeycomb, cellular or other laminated structures, describing how easily the material can be sliced, torn or separated along its layers. The classification applies to properties of the individual strata or the laminate as a whole that affect cutting performance, including resistance to fracture and the quality of the cut surface.
[B32B 2307/581] Resistant to cut -- B32B 2307/581 covers layered or laminated products whose constituent layers are engineered to be resistant to cutting, such as cut-resistant fabrics, honeycomb structures or other composites that retain integrity under sharp forces. The subclass falls under the CPC hierarchy for properties of layers within performing operations on layered products.
[B32B 2307/582] Tearability -- The B32B 2307/582 entry covers the tearability of layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures, focusing on how the properties of individual layers or laminates affect the ability of the whole product to be torn. It is used to classify patents dealing with design, material selection, or testing methods that influence tear resistance or intentional tearability in multi-layered components.
[B32B 2307/5825] Tear resistant -- B32B 2307/5825 relates to layered products-such as honeycomb, cellular or other flat and non-flat laminates-where the focus is on the tear-resistance of the layers or the laminate as a whole. It covers the design, composition or treatment of the strata that provide resistance to tearing, ensuring durability in applications where mechanical stresses are common.
[B32B 2307/584] Scratch resistance -- The subclass B32B 2307/584 pertains to the scratch-resistance of layered products, such as honeycomb, cellular or other multilayer structures. It includes methods, materials, surface treatments, and testing procedures that improve or assess how well the layers or laminates withstand surface damage from scratching.
[B32B 2307/70] Other properties -- B32B 2307/70 covers the study and specification of any additional or miscellaneous characteristics of layered products such as cellular, honey-comb or other strati-formed materials, beyond the primary mechanical, thermal or chemical properties already defined elsewhere. It includes ancillary traits that affect performance, appearance or handling.
[B32B 2307/702] Amorphous -- The B32B 2307/702 subclass concerns amorphous layers within laminated or cellular products, covering the characteristics, treatment and performance of non-crystalline strata in such composites. [B32B 2307/704] Crystalline -- The CPC subclass B32B 2307/704 covers the crystalline nature or crystalline characteristics of the individual layers or laminates in products built from stacked strata, such as honeycomb, cellular or other layered structures. It pertains to how the crystal structure influences the performance, strength, thermal or optical properties of the laminate.
[B32B 2307/706] Anisotropic -- The code B32B 2307/706 covers layered or laminate products whose individual layers exhibit anisotropic behaviour, meaning their physical or mechanical properties differ with direction within the layer. It applies to materials such as honeycomb, cellular or other strata where orientation-dependent characteristics are engineered for specific performance. This subclass falls under the broader categories of performing operations on layered products and the properties of the layers or laminates.
[B32B 2307/708] Isotropic -- Isotropic refers to materials whose properties are identical in all directions, applicable to layered or laminated products where each layer exhibits uniform mechanical, thermal, or optical behavior regardless of orientation. In CPC this subclass covers isotropic layers or laminates, their preparation and characterization.
[B32B 2307/71] Resistive to light or to UV -- B32B 2307/71 covers layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures that are designed to resist light or ultraviolet radiation. The classification applies to materials and laminates whose layers provide protection against illumination or UV exposure, often used in outdoor or high-temperature applications.
[B32B 2307/712] Weather resistant -- A B32B 2307/712 classification covers layered or laminated products where the focus is on resistance to weather effects such as moisture, sunlight, temperature changes, and atmospheric exposure, addressing how the individual strata or the overall laminate maintain performance and durability under such conditions.
[B32B 2307/714] Inert, i.e. inert to chemical degradation, corrosion -- B32B 2307/714 pertains to layered or laminated products whose individual strata are chemically inert, meaning they resist degradation, corrosion or other chemical attack. [B32B 2307/7145] Rot proof, resistant to bacteria, mildew, mould, fungi -- The subclass B32B 2307/7145 pertains to layered or laminated products-such as cellular, honeycomb, or flat-stratified materials-whose layers are specifically engineered to be rot-proof and resistant to bacteria, mildew, mould and fungi. It falls under the CPC hierarchy for properties of the layers or laminate within performing operations on layered products.
[B32B 2307/716] Degradable -- This CPC subclass concerns layered products such as foams, honeycombs or other structures built from flat or non-flat strata whose layers are designed to degrade by chemical, biological or environmental action. [B32B 2307/7163] Biodegradable -- B32B 2307/7163 covers layered or laminate products whose constituent layers are biodegradable, including cellular, honeycomb or flat structures that break down naturally after use. [B32B 2307/7166] Water-soluble, water-dispersible -- It is a CPC entry under B32B 2307/7166 for layered products, covering water-soluble or water-dispersible materials used in laminates such as cellular or honeycomb structures, indicating that the layers can dissolve or disperse in water during manufacture or service.
[B32B 2307/718] Weight, e.g. weight per square meter -- The CPC subclass B32B 2307/718 covers the determination or specification of the weight of layered or laminated products, such as honey-comb, cellular or other strata-built panels, expressed as weight per unit area (for example grams per square metre). This information is used to assess material performance and handling characteristics of the layers.
[B32B 2307/72] Density -- B32B 2307/72 covers the measurement, specification or control of the density of layered products such as cellular, honeycomb or other flat or non-flat laminates. [B32B 2307/722] Non-uniform density -- This subclass covers layered products whose individual strata have differing densities, providing gradients of mechanical or thermal properties. [B32B 2307/724] Permeability to gases, adsorption -- This subclass concerns the gas-permeability and adsorption behaviour of layered or laminated products such as honeycomb, cellular, or flat strata, covering methods, apparatus and material properties that determine how gases pass through or are adsorbed by the layers.

[B32B 2307/7265] Non-permeable -- The CPC subclass B32B 2307/7265, titled Non-permeable, pertains to layered or laminated products whose structure is designed to prevent the passage of gases, liquids or other substances through the material. [B32B 2307/732] Dimensional properties -- The entry B32B 2307/732 concerns the dimensional characteristics of layered or laminated products such as thickness, cell size, shape, spacing and overall geometry. [B32B 2307/734] Dimensional stability -- B32B 2307/734 covers the dimensional stability of layered products such as honeycomb, cellular or other laminated structures. [B32B 2307/746] Slipping, anti-blocking, low friction -- B32B 2307/746 classifies layered products whose surface or inter-layer characteristics are designed to slip easily, resist blocking and exhibit low friction, such as honeycomb or cellular structures where the layers are treated or configured to minimise adhesion and improve smooth movement. [B32B 2307/752] Corrosion inhibitor -- B32B 2307/752 covers the use of corrosion inhibitors in layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures, focusing on how the protective additives affect the properties of the layers or laminates. [B32B 2307/754] Self-cleaning -- The CPC subclass B32B 2307/754 covers self-cleaning features of layered products, such as coatings, films, honeycomb or cellular structures, where the cleaning effect arises from the intrinsic properties of the layers or laminate rather than external mechanisms. It addresses designs that enable surfaces to repel contaminants, break down stains, or recover cleanliness through material composition, texture, or inherent chemical activity.
[B32B 2307/756] Refurbishable, i.e. marks or scratches can be removed -- B32B 2307/756 covers layered or laminate products whose surface properties allow refurbishment, meaning marks, scratches or other damage can be removed to restore the original appearance. [B32B 2307/764] Insect repellent -- B32B 2307/764 covers the incorporation of insect-repellent agents into layered products such as foams, honeycomb structures or other laminate forms. [B32B 23/08] of synthetic resin -- B32B 23/08 pertains to layered products where at least one layer is made of a cellulosic plastic substance, specifically when this layer is composed of synthetic resin. [B32B 2309/06] Angles -- The B32B 2309/06 entry concerns operations for forming layered products in which the angle between successive strata or cell walls is defined or adjusted, such as setting the inclination of walls in honey-comb or cellular structures to achieve a specific geometry or performance. [B32B 2309/16] Tension -- The subclass B32B 2309/16 covers processes where a layered or cellular product is placed under tensile forces during manufacturing or post-treatment, such as stretching or pulling a honeycomb or cellular core to control its shape, density, or mechanical properties. It includes methods for applying, regulating or releasing tension in these stratified structures.
[B32B 2309/60] In a particular environment -- B32B 2309/60 pertains to procedures for producing layered products where the manufacturing takes place in a specified environment, such as controlled temperature, pressure, gas atmosphere or vacuum. [B32B 2309/62] Inert -- B32B 2309/62 (Inert) covers operating procedures for producing layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures that are chemically non-reactive. [B32B 2309/64] Sterile -- The CPC entry B32B 2309/64 "Sterile" covers procedures for producing or treating layered products-such as cellular, honeycomb or other flat and non-flat strata-so that they are free from viable microorganisms. [B32B 2309/65] Dust free, e.g. clean room -- The code B32B 2309/65 covers operating procedures that create or maintain a dust-free environment, such as clean-room techniques, for the production or handling of layered products built from flat or non-flat strata like cellular or honeycomb structures. [B32B 2309/66] Fluid other than air -- B32B 2309/66 covers processes for handling fluids other than air when producing layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures. [B32B 2309/68] Vacuum -- B32B 2309/68 covers the use of vacuum techniques in the manufacture of layered products such as cellular, honey-comb or other stratified structures. It includes operations where a vacuum is applied to shape, consolidate, bond or cure the layers during production, and is classified under Performing Operations → Layered Products → Operating procedures.
[B32B 2309/70] Automated, e.g. using a computer or microcomputer -- The B32B 2309/70 subclass relates to automated operating procedures for manufacturing layered products such as honeycomb or cellular structures, wherein computers, microcomputers or other digital control systems direct the formation, stacking, bonding or shaping of the strata. It covers process steps that are performed by programmed equipment rather than manually, including computer-controlled positioning, timing and quality monitoring.
[B32B 2309/72] For measuring or regulating, e.g. systems with feedback loops -- The B32B 2309/72 subclass covers devices or processes that measure or regulate the formation of layered structures such as honeycomb or cellular panels, typically using feedback loops to adjust manufacturing parameters in real time.

The code covers treatments like heating, irradiation, plasma or chemical exposure used to alter, cure, or functionalise the layers.

[B32B 25/00] Layered products comprising natural or synthetic rubber -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Layered products characterised by a layer of thermosetting synthetic rubber.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Layered products characterised by having a fibrous or filamentary layer made of a natural or synthetic rubber -> B32B5/02 - Layered products characterised by having a particulate layer made of a natural or synthetic rubber -> B32B5/16 - Layered products characterised by having a foamed layer made of a natural or synthetic rubber -> B32B5/18  **Glossary:** - Thermosetting Rubber: Vulcanized rubber that cannot be re-melted or remolded without destroying its original characteristics. - Vulcanization: An irreversible process during which a rubber compound through a change in its chemical structure (for example, cross-linking) becomes less plastic and more resistant to swelling by organic liquids and elastic properties are conferred, improved, or extended over a greater range of temperature.
[B32B 25/02] with fibres or particles -- B32B 25/02 covers layered products made of natural or synthetic rubber that incorporate reinforcing fibres or particulate fillers. These materials are formed as strata, such as cellular, honeycomb or other multi-layer structures, and are used where added strength, stiffness or specific functional properties are required.

This subclass covers composites like rubber-laminated sheets, hoses, belts and sandwich structures where rubber is the main or sole constituent of one stratum.

It includes rubbers used as core, skin or filler material in laminated or foam-type constructions.

[B32B 33/00] Layered products characterised by particular properties or particular surface features, e.g. particular surface coatings -- The B32B 33/00 subclass covers layered products-such as cellular, honeycomb or other multi-strata structures-designed or treated to exhibit particular functional properties or distinct surface characteristics, including specialized coatings, patterns, or textures that impart unique mechanical, optical, thermal or chemical performance.
[B32B 37/00] Methods or apparatus for making layered products -- The CPC subclass B32B 37/00 covers techniques and equipment used to produce layered products, where the material is built up in successive strata of flat or non-flat sections such as cellular, honeycomb or other structured forms. It includes manufacturing processes that create these multilayered structures and the apparatus designed to carry out those processes.
[B32B 37/0007] involving treatment or provisions in order to avoid deformation or air inclusion, e.g. to improve surface quality -- B32B 37/0007 covers techniques applied during the production of layered materials - such as foams, honeycomb or cellular structures - to prevent distortion or trapped air, thereby enhancing surface finish and dimensional stability. The provision may include pre- or post-process treatments, tooling adjustments or environmental controls aimed at maintaining the integrity of each stratum.
[B32B 37/0015] to avoid warp or curl -- The subclass B32B 37/0015 covers methods and apparatus that prevent or correct warping and curling of layered products such as laminates, honeycomb or cellular structures during their manufacture. It includes controls of moisture, temperature, curing rates, tooling pressure and other process parameters designed to keep each stratum flat and dimensionally stable.
[B32B 37/0023] around holes, apertures or channels present in at least one layer -- B32B 37/0023 covers methods and equipment for producing layered structures-such as cellular, honeycomb or other stratified products-where at least one layer includes holes, apertures or channels. The classification applies to processes that create or shape these openings during the fabrication of the multilayered item.
[B32B 37/003] to avoid air inclusion -- The B32B 37/003 subclass covers methods and apparatuses used in the manufacture of layered products-such as honeycomb, cellular or other stratified structures-to prevent the entrapment of air within the layers, ensuring a void-free configuration and improving material performance.
[B32B 37/0038] involving application of liquid to the layers prior to lamination, e.g. wet laminating  B32B37/12  takes precedence -- The code B32B 37/0038 covers processes or equipment that apply a liquid to the component layers before they are laminated together, a technique known as wet laminating. This subclass falls under the broader category B32B 37/12, which deals with lamination methods in general.
[B32B 37/0046] characterised by constructional aspects of the apparatus -- This CPC subgroup covers inventions that emphasize the structural design of apparatuses for producing layered products, describing features such as the arrangement, geometry or specific components of the equipment that influence layer formation. It focuses on constructional aspects of frames, rollers, molds or other mechanical elements rather than the processing steps themselves.
[B32B 37/0053] Constructional details of laminating machines comprising rollers; Constructional features of the rollers -- The subclass B32B 37/0053 deals with the constructional aspects of laminating machines, specifically the design and features of the rollers used in the process. It covers roller geometry, drive and support arrangements, surface treatments, heating or cooling integration and other mechanical details that influence the bonding of layered products.
[B32B 37/0076] characterised in that the layers are not bonded on the totality of their surfaces -- The code B32B 37/0076 covers methods or devices for producing layered products in which the individual layers are only partially bonded, meaning the bonding does not extend over the entire contacting surface but occurs at discrete areas, spots or along selected lines. This subclass deals with partial or selective attachment of flat or non-flat strata such as cellular, honeycomb or other multi-layer structures.
[B32B 37/0084] Point bonding -- Point bonding refers to the technique of joining individual layers of a sheet-like or cellular material at distinct, localized spots rather than across the entire surface. This method creates a mechanical or adhesive bond at discrete points, providing structural integrity while preserving flexibility, and is commonly applied to honeycomb, cellular, or other multilayered products.Point bonding refers to the technique of joining individual layers of a sheet-like or cellular material at distinct, localized spots rather than across the entire surface. This method creates a mechanical or adhesive bond at discrete points, providing structural integrity while preserving flexibility, and is commonly applied to honeycomb, cellular, or other multilayered products.
[B32B 37/02] characterised by a sequence of laminating steps, e.g. by adding new layers at consecutive laminating stations -- This subclass covers processes for producing layered products where the layers are built up sequentially through multiple laminating stations, each adding a new layer. It includes methods that use a series of laminating steps to create a multi-layer structure, such as honeycomb or cellular panels.
[B32B 37/025] Transfer laminating -- Transfer laminating involves bonding a pre-formed polymeric or composite sheet to a substrate by applying heat and pressure, creating a multilayer structure without directly molding the layers together. The classification covers methods and apparatus that position, align, and transfer the laminating film, often using rollers or belts, to produce layered products such as sheets, films, or panels.
[B32B 37/04] characterised by the partial melting of at least one layer -- The CPC class B32B 37/04 covers methods or apparatus for producing layered products where at least one layer is partially melted to bond or shape the structure, such as honeycomb or cellular panels.
[B32B 37/06] characterised by the heating method -- Subclass B32B 37/06 covers methods and apparatus for producing layered products that are distinguished by the heating technique employed, such as thermal curing, sintering, or heat-assisted lamination, used to bond, shape or solidify the strata of the final structure. This includes processes where heat is applied during the formation of foams, honeycomb or other multi-layered forms.
[B32B 37/065] resulting in the laminate being partially bonded  B32B37/0076  takes precedence -- B32B 37/065 covers processes or equipment that produce layered products in which the individual layers are only partially bonded together, creating a composite where some regions remain unjoined. This subclass follows the more general B32B 37/0076, which deals with fully bonded laminates, and is used for techniques such as selective adhesive application, localized heat or pressure bonding, and patterned curing.
[B32B 37/08] characterised by the cooling method -- The sub-group B32B 37/08 includes processes and apparatus for producing layered products where the distinguishing feature is the cooling method used to solidify each layer, such as chilled plates, gas, water or other means of heat removal. The cooling technique affects layer adhesion, thickness control and material properties during manufacture.
[B32B 37/085] Quenching -- B32B 37/085 relates to quenching processes used in the manufacture of layered products such as cellular, honey-comb or other stratified structures. It covers methods and apparatus that rapidly cool or otherwise treat the layers after formation to achieve desired material properties, dimensions or performance.
[B32B 37/10] characterised by the pressing technique, e.g. using action of vacuum or fluid pressure -- B32B 37/10 covers methods or apparatus for producing layered products in which the layers are joined by a pressing technique, such as applying vacuum or fluid pressure, to consolidate the strata into a solid structure. This includes processes used to form honeycomb, cellular or other multi-layered materials.
[B32B 37/1009] using vacuum and fluid pressure -- The B32B 37/1009 subclass covers methods or apparatus that form layered products by applying a vacuum to remove air and a fluid pressure to push or shape material into the desired stratum, enabling the creation of honeycomb, cellular or other multilayer structures. It is a subcategory of "methods or apparatus for making layered products."
[B32B 37/1018] using only vacuum -- B32B 37/1018 relates to methods or apparatus for producing layered products, such as cellular or honeycomb structures, that employ only vacuum to form the strata, without using pressure or other assisting forces.
[B32B 37/1027] Pressing using at least one press band -- B32B 37/1027 covers methods or apparatus for forming layered structures in which the layers are consolidated by a pressing step that uses at least one press band. The press band, typically a continuous belt or flexible element, contacts the workpiece to apply pressure while moving relative to the material, enabling production of cellular, honeycomb or other striated products.
[B32B 37/1036] Pressing between one press band and a cylinder -- It covers methods or apparatus where a material is pressed using a single press band against a rotating cylinder to form layered structures such as honeycomb or cellular panels. The technique creates successive strata by applying pressure while the material passes between the band and cylinder. Classified under CPC B32B 37/1036, it falls within the performing-operations group for layered-product manufacture.
[B32B 37/1045] Intermittent pressing, e.g. by oscillating or reciprocating motion of the pressing means  B32B37/0076  takes precedence -- Intermittent pressing refers to a technique where the pressing tool moves in an oscillating or reciprocating manner, applying pressure to successive layers of material to form a composite structure such as honeycomb or cellular panels. The method can be used in processes that build up flat or shaped layered products, allowing control over layer thickness and density.
[B32B 37/1054] Regulating the dimensions of the laminate, e.g. by adjusting the nip or platen gap -- This CPC subclass deals with methods and apparatus that control the size or thickness of a laminate while it is being formed, for example by varying the nip pressure or the gap between platens. It is part of the B32B 37 group covering processes for making layered products and focuses on dimensional regulation to achieve uniformity and desired performance.
[B32B 37/12] characterised by using adhesives -- This CPC subclass deals with processes and equipment for producing layered products-such as honeycomb, cellular or other stratified structures-where the layers are bonded by adhesives. It covers methods of applying, curing or otherwise using adhesive agents to join the strata during manufacture, distinguishing these techniques from mechanical fastening or other bonding means.
[B32B 37/1207] Heat-activated adhesive  B32B37/04  takes precedence -- This classification code pertains to methods and apparatus for creating layered products using heat-activated adhesives, with a specific note that the broader category B32B37/04 has precedence in the hierarchy.
[B32B 37/1284] Application of adhesive -- B32B 37/1284 concerns the application of adhesives in the manufacture of layered products such as cellular, honeycomb or other stratified structures, covering methods, apparatus and steps used to bond the individual strata together.
[B32B 37/1292] selectively, e.g. in stripes, in patterns  B32B37/0076  takes precedence -- This classification code pertains to methods or apparatus for creating layered products with selective application, such as in stripes or patterns, but it is noted that the code B32B37/0076 has precedence over this entry.
[B32B 37/14] characterised by the properties of the layers -- B32B 37/14 covers methods, apparatuses and products in which the distinguishing feature of a layered material is the specific property of its individual layers, such as thickness, density, elasticity or thermal conductivity. The classification is used for honeycomb, cellular or other multi-strata structures where performance is derived from the characteristics of each layer rather than the overall geometry.
[B32B 37/142] Laminating of sheets, panels or inserts, e.g. stiffeners, by wrapping in at least one outer layer, or inserting into a preformed pocket -- B32B 37/142 covers methods and apparatus for laminating sheets, panels or inserts such as stiffeners by wrapping them in at least one outer layer or by placing them into a pre-formed pocket, forming a bonded layered structure. It falls under the broader category of producing layered products built from flat or non-flat strata.
[B32B 37/144] using layers with different mechanical or chemical conditions or properties, e.g. layers with different thermal shrinkage, layers under tension during bonding  constructional features for tensioning  B32B38/1825 -- The subclass B32B 37/144 covers processes for manufacturing layered products in which the individual layers are intentionally given distinct mechanical or chemical characteristics, such as differing thermal-shrink behavior or pre-tension during bonding, and includes specific constructional features employed to impose tension on the layers.
[B32B 37/146] whereby one or more of the layers is a honeycomb structure -- The CPC subclass B32B 37/146 concerns methods or apparatus for manufacturing layered products in which one or more of the layers is formed as a honeycomb structure, typically used to create lightweight, high-strength panels by arranging flat or non-flat strata such as cellular or honeycomb cores.
[B32B 37/15] with at least one layer being manufactured and immediately laminated before reaching its stable state, e.g. in which a layer is extruded and laminated while in semi-molten state -- This subclass covers methods where a layer is produced and laminated before it solidifies, such as extruding a semi-molten sheet and bonding it immediately to another layer. The approach ensures the layer is still in a fluid or semi-molten state when lamination occurs, enabling strong adhesion and integrated structure in layered products.
[B32B 37/153] at least one layer is extruded and immediately laminated while in semi-molten state -- The CPC entry B32B 37/153 covers processes for producing layered products in which at least one layer is extruded and then laminated to another layer while still semi-molten, forming a bond before solidification. This technique is used to create composites such as honeycomb, cellular or other multi-stratum structures in a continuous manufacturing step. It falls under the broader class of methods for making layered products.
[B32B 37/156] at least one layer is calendered and immediately laminated -- B32B 37/156 covers manufacturing methods for layered products in which a sheet or other layer is first passed through calender rollers to smooth or compress it and then, without interruption, is bonded to an adjacent layer by lamination. The classification applies to processes that combine calendaring and immediate lamination in a single production step for items such as honeycomb, cellular or other structured panels.
[B32B 37/16] with all layers existing as coherent layers before laminating -- B32B 37/16 relates to processes and equipment for producing layered products where each constituent sheet is already formed as a coherent layer before the laminating step, covering the preparation of such pre-formed layers and their subsequent bonding into a composite structure.
[B32B 37/18] involving the assembly of discrete sheets or panels only -- **Glossary:** - Discrete sheets or panels: Dimension of sheets or panels is determined at the instant when sheets or panels come into contact.
[B32B 37/182] one or more of the layers being plastic -- B32B 37/182 pertains to methods or apparatus for producing layered products in which at least one of the strata is composed of plastic, including structures such as cellular or honeycomb forms. It falls under the Performing Operations class for layered products.
[B32B 37/185] Laminating sheets, panels or inserts between two discrete plastic layers -- The CPC subclass B32B 37/185 covers processes that bond a sheet, panel or insert to a plastic layer by placing it between two separate plastic sheets and laminating them together. It includes methods that use heat, pressure, adhesives or radiation to create a unified layered product while retaining the discrete nature of each outer layer.
[B32B 37/187] the layers being placed in a carrier before going through the lamination process -- B32B 37/187 covers processes in which individual layers of a sheet-like material are first positioned or assembled within a carrier or support before the assembly undergoes lamination to create a multilayer product. The carrier holds the layers in place during handling and alignment, facilitating the production of honeycomb, cellular or other structured composites.
[B32B 37/20] involving the assembly of continuous webs only -- **Glossary:** - Continuous webs: Dimension of webs or layers is determined at the instant when webs or layers come into contact.
[B32B 37/203] One or more of the layers being plastic -- B32B 37/203 pertains to processes or equipment for producing layered structures in which at least one layer consists of a plastic material. The classification addresses the formation of composite sheets, honeycomb or cellular forms that combine plastic with other strata.
[B32B 37/206] Laminating a continuous layer between two continuous plastic layers -- The code B32B 37/206 covers methods and apparatus for laminating a continuous sheet of material between two continuous plastic sheets, forming a layered product. It pertains to the production of flat or shaped structures such as honeycomb, cellular or other strati­fied panels by joining the layers together in a continuous process.
[B32B 37/22] involving the assembly of both discrete and continuous layers -- **Glossary:** - Discrete and continuous layers: Dimension of layers is determined at the instant when layers come into contact.
[B32B 37/223] One or more of the layers being plastic -- B32B 37/223 relates to processes or equipment for producing layered structures in which at least one of the strata consists of a plastic material, such as plastic sheets, films or foams, typically combined with other materials like metal or paper.
[B32B 37/226] Laminating sheets, panels or inserts between two continuous plastic layers -- The code B32B 37/226 covers processes and equipment for inserting sheets, panels or other inserts between two continuously formed plastic layers, then bonding them to create a single laminated product. It includes techniques such as feeding, aligning and fusing the intermediate material while the surrounding plastics are still molten or under pressure.
[B32B 37/24] with at least one layer not being coherent before laminating, e.g. made up from granular material sprinkled onto a substrate -- B32B 37/24 covers processes and equipment for producing layered products in which at least one of the layers is initially non-coherent, such as a granular or powdered material that is deposited onto a substrate before being laminated. The classification applies to methods that create a solid, integral structure from otherwise loose or unbonded layers.
[B32B 37/26] with at least one layer which influences the bonding during the lamination process, e.g. release layers or pressure equalising layers -- B32B 37/26 classifies methods and apparatus for producing layered products in which at least one layer is designed to affect the bonding during lamination, for example by acting as a release layer or a pressure-equalising layer that controls adhesion and pressure distribution between strata. This sub-group falls under the broader categories of performing operations on layered products, specifically addressing functional layers that modify the lamination process.
[B32B 37/28] involving assembly of non-flat intermediate products which are flattened at a later step, e.g. tubes -- This CPC subclass concerns methods or apparatuses that assemble three-dimensional intermediate components, such as tubes, which are subsequently flattened to form layered structures. It falls under the broader category of layered products and covers processes where non-flat elements are joined before being converted into flat or honey-comb forms.
[B32B 37/30] Partial laminating -- Partial laminating covers processes and equipment that apply adhesive layers to only selected zones of a sheet or core material, creating composite structures such as honeycomb or cellular panels where the lamination does not extend over the entire surface. It is used to reinforce or bond specific regions while preserving other areas for weight-saving or functional reasons.
[B32B 38/00] Ancillary operations in connection with laminating processes -- In this group, the following expression is used with the meaning indicated: "in connection with laminating processes" means ancillary operations are carried out either as steps of the lamination processes, or in line with the lamination processes, just before or immediately after.
[B32B 38/0004] Cutting, tearing or severing, e.g. bursting; Cutter details  cutting in general  B26D ; laminating combined with punching or perforating  B32B38/04 ; removing all or part of the layers  B32B38/10 ; cutting in combination with laying up and registration  B32B38/185  takes precedence -- B32B 38/0004 covers ancillary operations in laminating processes, such as cutting, tearing or severing of layered products, including bursting and cutter details defined in B26D. It also includes laminating combined with punching or perforating, removal of all or part of the layers, and cutting performed together with lay-up and registration.
[B32B 38/0008] Electrical discharge treatment, e.g. corona, plasma treatment; wave energy or particle radiation  heat treatment  B32B38/0036 -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Heat treatment -> B32B38/0036
[B32B 38/0012] Mechanical treatment, e.g. roughening, deforming, stretching -- This subclass covers mechanical operations applied to layered products during or after laminating, such as roughening, deforming or stretching the layers to modify surface texture or shape. It falls under CPC B32B for layered products and ancillary laminating processes.
[B32B 38/0032] increasing porosity  B32B38/04  takes precedence -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Punching, slitting or perforating -> B32B38/04
[B32B 38/0036] Heat treatment  for heating or cooling of layers during lamination  B32B37/06 ,  B32B37/08 -- The code B32B 38/0036 covers ancillary operations in lamination that involve heat treatment, i.e., the controlled heating or cooling of individual layers or the entire laminate during the bonding process. It relates to the sub-classes B32B 37/06 and B32B 37/08, which address the thermal conditioning of layers to influence curing, adhesion, or material properties.
[B32B 38/004] by physically contacting the layers, e.g. by the use of heated platens or rollers -- The subclass B32B 38/004 pertains to ancillary steps in lamination where the layers are bonded by direct physical contact, such as applying pressure with heated platens or rollers to fuse the strata.
[B32B 38/04] Punching, slitting or perforating -- A CPC subclass for ancillary steps in laminating that involve cutting actions such as punching, slitting or perforating layered structures like honeycomb or cellular panels. It covers methods and equipment used to create openings or separate strips in these built-up products during the manufacturing process.
[B32B 38/06] Embossing -- Embossing is an ancillary operation applied during laminating of layered products, where the stacked strata are deformed to produce raised patterns or textures. It is carried out with dies, rollers or other tools to impart decorative or functional surface relief on flat or non-flat composites such as honeycomb or cellular structures.
[B32B 38/08] Impregnating -- The CPC subclass B32B 38/08 concerns the ancillary step of impregnating a layer or a complete laminate with liquids such as resins, adhesives, or fluids to enhance bonding, fill voids, or modify properties during laminating of layered products, including flat, cellular or honey-comb structures.
[B32B 38/10] Removing layers, or parts of layers, mechanically or chemically -- It covers methods for removing layers or parts of layers from laminated or other layered products, employing mechanical or chemical means as ancillary operations in lamination processes.
[B32B 38/105] on edges -- This CPC subclass covers operations performed on the edges of layered products during laminating processes, such as trimming, sealing, or reinforcing the periphery after the layers are bonded. It falls under ancillary operations within the B32B class for manufacturing laminated sheets, honeycomb, and other stratified structures.
[B32B 38/12] Deep-drawing -- The code B32B 38/12 covers deep-drawing techniques applied to laminated or sandwich products, where a flat multilayer sheet is drawn into a deep cavity to form shaped components while preserving the layered structure. It falls under ancillary operations linked to laminating processes in the CPC hierarchy.
[B32B 38/14] Printing or colouring -- B32B 38/14 covers ancillary operations performed during laminating, specifically the printing or colouring of layered products such as flat, cellular or honey-comb structures. It relates to applying pigments, inks or dyes to the surface or interior strata of the laminate as part of the manufacturing process.
[B32B 38/145] Printing -- B32B 38/145 relates to printing as an ancillary operation in laminating layered products, such as honeycomb or cellular structures. It covers the application of inks, markings or graphics onto one or more layers before, during, or after the bonding step.
[B32B 38/16] Drying -- B32B 38/16 covers drying operations performed as part of laminating processes for layered products such as honeycomb, cellular or other multi-strata structures. It includes techniques for removing moisture from impregnated layers or adhesive-bonded sheets to achieve the desired material properties.
[B32B 38/162] Cleaning -- The subclass B32B 38/162 covers cleaning operations that are carried out as ancillary steps in laminating processes for layered products such as honeycomb, cellular or other stratified structures. It includes methods and equipment for removing dust, residues, or other contaminants from the surfaces before, during or after the lamination.
[B32B 38/164] Drying -- B32B 38/164 addresses drying as an ancillary operation in laminating processes for layered products such as cellular, honeycomb or other multi-strata structures. The code covers methods for removing moisture from the laminate during manufacture to improve bond strength and dimensional stability. It is part of the broader category concerning performing operations on layered products.
[B32B 38/18] Handling of layers or the laminate -- B32B 38/18 pertains to the handling of layers or the laminate, covering ancillary operations such as positioning, aligning, feeding, moving or otherwise manipulating individual sheets, honeycomb or cellular structures during a laminating process.
[B32B 38/1808] characterised by the laying up of the layers -- This subclass covers ancillary operations in laminating processes that involve the sequential laying up of individual sheets, foils, cores or other flat or non-flat elements to form a layered product. It includes methods for arranging, aligning or depositing the layers before they are bonded into a composite structure.
[B32B 38/1816] Cross feeding of one or more of the layers -- The B32B 38/1816 subclass covers ancillary operations that involve cross feeding one or more separate layers during a laminating process, such as introducing additional sheets or plies into the material stream to form layered products like honeycomb or cellular structures. This operation aids in building up multi-layered constructions.
[B32B 38/1825] characterised by the control or constructional features of devices for tensioning, stretching or registration -- B32B 38/1825 is a CPC subclass within Performing Operations → Layered Products → Ancillary Operations in connection with laminating processes. It pertains to devices whose control or structural design provides tensioning, stretching or registration functions for handling or aligning sheets during lamination.
[B32B 38/1833] Positioning, e.g. registration or centering -- The subclass B32B 38/1833 covers techniques for positioning, such as registration or centering, of individual layers during laminating operations. It addresses ancillary steps that ensure precise alignment of strata in the manufacture of layered products.
[B32B 38/1841] during laying up -- This CPC subclass covers auxiliary steps carried out while a laminate is being built up, such as applying adhesives, consolidating layers, or handling materials during the lay-up stage of layered products like honeycomb or cellular structures. It addresses ancillary operations that support the primary laminating process.
[B32B 38/185] combined with the cutting of one or more layers -- The CPC subclass B32B 38/185 covers ancillary steps that are performed together with laminating operations, specifically when one or more layers of a laminated structure are cut as part of the process. It applies to methods where cutting of the individual sheets or the composite product is integrated with the bonding of the layers.
[B32B 38/1858] using vacuum -- This CPC subclass deals with ancillary operations in laminating processes that involve applying a vacuum to consolidate layers or remove air. It covers the use of vacuum during bonding of flat or non-flat layered structures such as cellular or honeycomb components.
[B32B 38/1866] conforming the layers or laminate to a convex or concave profile -- The CPC subclass B32B 38/1866 covers ancillary operations used to shape a laminate or layered product so that its surface follows a convex or concave profile, typically after bonding the individual layers together. It falls under layered products and related laminating processes.
[B32B 38/1875] Tensioning -- Tensioning involves applying a controlled pulling force to a sheet, film or laminate during or after a laminating operation to align the material, eliminate wrinkles and improve adhesion between layers. This ancillary step is used in the production of layered products such as honeycomb, cellular or flat-strata structures.
[B32B 38/1883] Detensioning -- B32B 38/1883 - Detensioning covers ancillary operations used during lamination of layered products such as cellular, honeycomb or other stratum-based structures. The process relieves tension in the material to improve bond quality and dimensional stability before or after the main laminating step.
[B32B 39/00] Layout of apparatus or plants, e.g. modular laminating systems -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The layout of stations in a manufacturing line.
[B32B 41/00] Arrangements for controlling or monitoring lamination processes -- **Definition:** This place covers:
[B32B 41/02] Safety arrangements -- B32B 41/02 relates to safety arrangements applied to lamination processes used to produce layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures. It covers devices, systems and methods for monitoring and controlling hazards during the formation and handling of flat or non-flat strata.
[B32B 43/00] Operations specially adapted for layered products and not otherwise provided for, e.g. repairing -- **Glossary:** - Specially adapted for layered products: The layered structure of the product governs the operations or the apparatus structure.
[B32B 43/003] Cutting -- B32B 43/003 covers cutting operations specially adapted for layered products such as cellular, honeycomb or other striated structures. The code includes methods for separating or trimming these strata when repairing or shaping the material, where general cutting techniques are insufficient. It falls under the broader categories of performing operations on layered products.
[B32B 43/006] Delaminating -- The B32B 43/006 entry defines operations that intentionally separate or peel apart the strata of layered products, such as cellular, honeycomb or other flat or non-flat constructions, to facilitate repair, recycling or re-assembly. It covers methods specifically adapted for delaminating these multi-layered structures and not otherwise classified.
[B32B 5/00] Layered products characterised by the non- homogeneity or physical structure -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Layered products comprising at least one layer that is a fibrous, filamentary, particulate or foamed layer (see definitions in B32B subclass glossary). A layered product can include:  Layered products characterised by a layer differing constitutionally or physically in different parts, e.g. a synthetic resin layer that has greater crosslinking near its faces; a cementitious layer with different density from core to outer faces.
[B32B 5/02] characterised by structural features of a layer -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Layered products comprising a fibrous or filamentary layer, e.g. woven; non-woven; knit; nets produced from fibres, filaments, yarns, threads; ribbons or tapes; or a layer formed by regularly laid parallel cords or filaments, which may be bunched, flat or slightly separated, e.g. juxtaposed-side-by-side.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Layer formed of metallic wires -> B32B15/02 - Layer formed of natural mineral fibres -> B32B19/02 - Layer formed of wood fibres -> B32B21/02
[B32B 5/022] Non-woven fabric -- B32B 5/022 covers non-woven fabrics, which are layered products formed from fibers, filaments or webs that are bonded together by mechanical, thermal or chemical means rather than by weaving or knitting. These materials display a non-homogeneous physical structure and are used in applications such as filters, medical textiles and composite reinforcements.
[B32B 5/024] Woven fabric -- B32B 5/024 designates woven fabrics, which are layered products formed by interlacing two or more sets of yarns at right angles to create a non-homogeneous structure. The classification covers manufacturing methods and characteristics of flat or three-dimensional woven textiles such as plain, twill or satin weaves.
[B32B 5/026] Knitted fabric -- B32B 5/026 pertains to knitted fabrics, which are textile structures created by interlooping yarns to form a flexible sheet. The classification includes single- and multi-layered knits with various stitch patterns and is applied to apparel, technical textiles, and composite material applications.
[B32B 5/028] Net structure, e.g. spaced apart filaments bonded at the crossing points -- B32B 5/028 covers net structures formed from spaced-apart filaments or strands that are bonded together at their crossing points, used to create layered products such as cellular, honeycomb or other non-flat configurations.
[B32B 5/04] characterised by a layer being specifically extensible by reason of its structure or arrangement -- B32B 5/04 covers layered products whose individual layers are designed to be especially extensible because of their specific structure or arrangement, such as honeycomb or cellular sheets that can stretch or open out under load. The classification applies to any non-flat or flat strata where the extensibility is an intrinsic feature of the layer's geometry or material composition.
[B32B 5/06] characterised by a fibrous layer to another layer, e.g. of fibres, of paper -- Group B32B5/06 is impacted by reclassification into groups B32B5/067 and B32B5/073 . All groups listed in this Warning should be considered in order to perform a complete search.
[B32B 5/067] characterised by the fibrous or filamentary layer being mechanically connected by hydroentangling -- Group B32B5/067 is incomplete pending reclassification of documents from group B32B5/06 . All groups listed in this Warning should be considered in order to perform a complete search.
[B32B 5/073] characterised by the fibrous or filamentary layer being mechanically connected to another layer by sewing, stitching, hook-and-loop fastening or stitchbonding -- Group B32B5/073 is incomplete pending reclassification of documents from group B32B5/06 . All groups listed in this Warning should be considered in order to perform a complete search.
[B32B 5/08] the fibres or filaments of a layer being of different substances -- The CPC subclass B32B 5/08 covers layered products whose individual layers contain fibres or filaments made from different substances, creating a non-homogeneous structure. Such composites are used in cellular, honeycomb or other stratified forms where varying material properties within a single layer enhance performance.
[B32B 5/10] characterised by a fibrous layer reinforced with filaments -- The CPC subclass B32B 5/10 covers layered products whose structure includes a fibrous base layer that is reinforced by filaments, such as composite panels or honey-comb structures where fibers are embedded to improve strength and stiffness. It falls under the broader category of layered products characterized by non-homogeneous physical structure.
[B32B 5/12] characterised by the relative arrangement of fibres or filaments of -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Layered products characterised by a particular arrangement of the fibres or filaments of the layers, e.g. fibres or filaments of the different layers being parallel or perpendicular to each other. The layers may be next to each other or separated by other layers.
[B32B 5/14] characterised by a layer differing constitutionally or physically in different parts, e.g. denser near its faces -- B32B 5/14 covers layered products whose individual layers vary in composition or physical properties across the thickness, such as a core that is denser near the outer faces than in the middle. It falls within the CPC hierarchy under Performing Operations - Layered Products.
[B32B 5/142] Variation across the area of the layer -- B32B 5/142 covers layered products whose individual layers exhibit spatial variations in composition, density, thickness or other physical characteristics across the surface of the layer. This includes designs where gradients, patterns or localized modifications are intentionally introduced to achieve functional or aesthetic effects.
[B32B 5/145] Variation across the thickness of the layer -- B32B 5/145 covers layered products whose properties change through the thickness of the sheet or panel, such as gradients in composition, density, porosity or mechanical strength. The classification is used for items like honeycomb cores, cellular foams or composite panels where each stratum differs from the next. It falls within the CPC section on performing operations for layered products.
[B32B 5/147] by treatment of the layer -- B32B 5/147 pertains to layered products with a focus on those characterized by the non-homogeneity or physical structure, specifically involving modifications through treatment of one or more layers. This classification is used for inventions that detail processes or methods applied to alter the properties of individual layers within composite structures.
[B32B 5/16] characterised by features of a layer formed of particles, e.g. chips, powder -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Layer formed of natural mineral particles -> B32B19/00 - Layer formed of wood fibres, chips or particles -> B32B21/02
[B32B 5/18] characterised by features of a layer foamed material -- B32B 5/18 covers layered products whose individual layers are made from foamed material and are defined by the specific characteristics of that foam, such as cell size, density, or expansion method. It applies to items like honeycomb, cellular or sandwich structures where the foam layer's properties determine the overall performance.
[B32B 5/20] foamed -- **Definition:** This place covers:  In-situ foams include a foamable layer that is assembled or installed and then foamed in or within the laminate or installation, e.g. a foamable polymer layer between two exterior layers, wherein the polymer layer is converted to foam after assembly between the exterior layers. The foamable layer can be preformed or can take the form of a layer while or after being brought into combination with another layer, e.g. casting, extrusion or molding of a melt material.
[B32B 5/22] characterised by the presence of two or more layers which -- B32B 5/22 covers layered products that consist of two or more stratified layers, such as cellular or honeycomb structures, where a non-homogeneous physical structure is a defining feature. It falls under the Performing Operations section of the CPC, within the subclass for layered products.
[B32B 5/24] one layer being a fibrous or filamentary layer -- This subclass covers layered articles in which at least one of the constituent strata consists of a fibrous or filamentary material, such as fabrics, mats or non-woven webs combined with other layers like foams, honeycombs or solid plates. It falls under the CPC group for layered products characterised by non-homogeneous physical structure.
[B32B 5/245] another layer next to it being a foam layer -- B32B 5/245 covers layered structures in which one of the adjacent layers is a foam material, typically combined with another solid or cellular layer to form a composite panel or sandwich component. The classification applies to products built from discrete strata of flat or shaped layers where the foam layer provides lightweight cushioning, insulation, or structural support alongside the neighboring layer. It is used for inventions involving non-homogeneous, multi-layered constructions such as honeycomb-foam panels.
[B32B 5/26] another layer also being fibrous or filamentary -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Layered products characterised by the adjacency of more than one fibrous or filamentary layers, i.e. woven, non-woven, knit or net layers, which are adjacent at least one or more woven, non-woven, knit or net layers. For example, a woven layer adjacent a non-woven layer; a knit layer adjacent a non-woven layer; a woven layer adjacent one or more non-woven layers.

Groups B32B5/26 , B32B5/262 and B32B5/263 should be considered in order to perform a complete search.
[B32B 5/263] next to one or more woven fabric layers -- B32B 5/263 covers layered products, such as cellular or honeycomb structures, that incorporate one or more woven-fabric layers within the strata. It is a subgroup of the CPC class for layered products characterised by non-homogeneous physical structure, falling under the broader category of performing operations. This code is used for inventions where woven fabrics are combined with other layers to form a composite, multi-layered product.
