All groups listed in this Warning should be considered in order to perform a complete search.
[B32B 5/266] next to one or more non-woven fabric layers -- B32B 5/266 covers processes in which a material is applied or joined directly adjacent to one or more non-woven fabric layers, forming a composite structure. Typical operations include lamination, bonding, or coating that create layered products with heterogeneous physical structures such as honeycomb or cellular cores.
[B32B 5/267] characterised by at least one non-woven fabric layer that is a spunbonded fabric -- The Cooperative Patent Classification code B32B 5/267 pertains to layered products with a specific focus on those containing at least one non-woven fabric layer, particularly when this layer is a spunbonded fabric. This classification is used by the European Patent Office and the United States Patent and Trademark Office for organizing patent documents related to such materials.
[B32B 5/268] characterised by at least one non-woven fabric layer that is a melt-blown fabric -- B32B 5/268 covers layered products whose structure includes at least one non-woven fabric layer formed by melt-blowing, a process that creates fine fibres from molten polymer. The classification is used for items such as filtration sheets, protective liners or composite panels where the melt-blown layer provides specific functional properties within the multilayer construction.
[B32B 5/269] characterised by at least one non-woven fabric layer that is a melt-blown fabric next to a non-woven fabric layer that is a spunbonded fabric -- B32B 5/269 classifies layered sheet products that incorporate at least one melt-blown non-woven fabric layer placed directly next to a spunbonded non-woven fabric layer, producing a composite structure whose individual layers differ in type and physical characteristics. The entry falls under the CPC hierarchy for layered products characterised by non-homogeneity or distinct physical structure.
[B32B 5/271] characterised by separate non-woven fabric layers that comprise chemically different strands or fibre material -- B32B 5/271 covers layered products in which the layers are separate non-woven fabrics, each layer being made from strands or fibres of a different chemical composition. The classification is applied to constructions such as cellular, honeycomb or other stratified structures where the heterogeneity of the fabric layers is a defining feature. It falls within the CPC hierarchy of performing operations on layered products.
[B32B 5/273] including a separate net structure layer -- B32B 5/273 pertains to layered products that incorporate a distinct net-like layer, such as a mesh or lattice, within a composite, cellular or honey-comb structure. The separate net layer serves functions like reinforcement, filtration or structural support as part of the overall build-up.
[B32B 5/275] characterised by one woven fabric layer next to a non-woven fabric layer -- Groups B32B5/275 and B32B5/277 are incomplete pending reclassification of documents from group B32B5/26 . Groups B32B5/26 , B32B5/275 and B32B5/277 should be considered in order to perform a complete search.
[B32B 5/277] including an additional non-woven fabric layer -- B32B 5/277 relates to layered products that incorporate an additional non-woven fabric layer, such as composites where a non-woven sheet is bonded to a cellular or honeycomb core. The code falls under performing operations for layered products and addresses structures with a non-homogeneous physical form.
[B32B 5/279] characterised by a knit fabric layer next to a non-woven fabric layer -- Group B32B5/279 is incomplete pending reclassification of documents from group B32B5/26 . Groups B32B5/26 and B32B5/279 should be considered in order to perform a complete search.
[B32B 5/2795] characterised by a knit fabric layer next to a woven fabric layer -- Group B32B5/2795 is incomplete pending reclassification of documents from group B32B5/26 . Groups B32B5/26 and B32B5/2795 should be considered in order to perform a complete search.
[B32B 5/28] impregnated with or embedded in a plastic substance -- B32B 5/28 relates to layered products such as honeycomb, cellular or other striated structures that have been impregnated with or contain a plastic material. The plastic fills the voids or coats the walls to enhance strength, stiffness, sealing or chemical resistance.
[B32B 5/30] one layer granules, powder -- The code B32B 5/30 covers layered products formed by a single stratum of granules or powder, where the layer consists of discrete particles instead of a continuous sheet. It applies to manufacturing or processing methods that create or use such one-layer particulate structures, often for cellular or honeycomb-type applications where the material's non-homogeneous physical arrangement is a key feature.
[B32B 5/32] layers being foamed -- B32B 5/32 pertains to layered products in which one or more layers are produced by foaming, creating gas-filled cells within the material. It covers manufacturing methods that generate foamed cores or panels in honeycomb, cellular or other stratified structures to obtain lightweight, structured products.
[B32B 7/00] Layered products characterised by the relation between layers -- **Definition:** This place covers:  This group covers layered products in which the relationship between the layers is important. The relationship could be, for example, the differences between physical or chemical properties, patterns of connection, and the orientations of features.
[B32B 7/02] Physical, chemical or physicochemical properties -- **Definition:** This place covers:  This group covers layered products characterised by having two or more layers, one of which differs from another with respect to a physical property, e.g. density, melting point, refractive index. Examples of this type of product are those comprising layers of:
[B32B 7/022] Mechanical properties -- B32B 7/022 covers the measurement and analysis of mechanical properties of layered products such as honeycomb, cellular or other stratified structures. It includes testing strength, stiffness, elasticity, impact resistance and related behavior of the layers and the assembled product. The code is used for patents dealing with methods or devices for assessing these characteristics.
[B32B 7/023] Optical properties -- B32B 7/023 relates to the optical characteristics of layered products, including transparent, reflective, light-guiding, scattering and colour effects of structures built from flat or non-flat strata such as honeycomb or cellular assemblies. The code addresses how the arrangement and composition of the layers influence these optical properties.
[B32B 7/025] Electric or magnetic properties -- B32B 7/025 covers layered products such as honeycomb, cellular or other strati­fied structures whose electric or magnetic characteristics are relevant, including conductivity, dielectric behavior, magnetic permeability or shielding effects. The code is used to classify inventions that exploit or modify these properties in the layers, for example for electromagnetic shielding, inductive components or energy-storage devices built from sheet-like or non-flat strata.
[B32B 7/027] Thermal properties -- B32B 7/027 covers the study and measurement of thermal behaviour of layered structures such as cellular, honeycomb or other stratified materials, including heat conductivity, insulation, expansion and temperature resistance. It pertains to processes for evaluating or improving the thermal performance of those products.
[B32B 7/028] Heat-shrinkability -- The code B32B 7/028 covers layered products whose layers are designed to become heat-shrinkable, i.e., they contract when heated to change shape or size. It pertains to the relationship between the strata of flat or non-flat materials such as cellular or honeycomb structures that give the product this heat-induced shrink behaviour.
[B32B 7/03] with respect to the orientation of features -- **Definition:** This place covers:  This group covers layered products characterised by having two or more layers, one of which differs from another with respect to the orientation of features, e.g. the direction of one layer's corrugation or joints differs from that of another layer. The layers may be next to each other or separated by other layers.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Direction of fibres or filaments -> B32B5/12
[B32B 7/035] using arrangements of stretched films, e.g. of mono-axially stretched films arranged alternately -- B32B 7/035 covers the use of layered structures formed by alternating arrangements of stretched films, such as mono-axially stretched sheets, to obtain specific mechanical or functional properties. The classification applies to products where the relationship between the layers, rather than the material composition, defines the performance, for example honeycomb or cellular panels.
[B32B 7/04] Interconnection of layers -- B32B 7/04 relates to the means of joining or linking the individual strata that form a layered product, such as honeycomb, cellular or other multilayer structures. It covers techniques for mechanically fastening, adhesively bonding, interlocking or otherwise interconnecting the layers to achieve structural integrity or functional continuity.
[B32B 7/05] the layers not being connected over the whole surface, e.g. discontinuous connection or patterned connection -- B32B 7/05 covers layered products whose individual layers are only intermittently joined, such as structures where the layers are linked in a discontinuous or patterned manner rather than across the whole surface. This subclass is applied to honeycomb, cellular or other stratified materials in which the inter-layer bonds are selective, allowing tailored mechanical or functional properties.
[B32B 7/06] permitting easy separation -- B32B 7/06 pertains to layered products engineered so that the individual strata can be separated easily, such as panels, sheets or honeycomb cores that detach without harming the remaining structure, typically achieved with releasable bonds, snap-fit connections or intentionally weak interfaces.
[B32B 7/08] by mechanical means -- B32B 7/08 designates the manufacturing of layered products, such as cellular or honey-comb structures, by mechanical methods. It addresses processes that mechanically join or shape flat or non-flat strata to achieve a specific inter-layer relationship.
[B32B 7/09] by stitching, needling or sewing -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Fibrous or filamentary layer mechanically connected, e.g. by needling, sewing, stitching, hydroentangling, hook-and-loop fastening to another layer, e.g. of fibres, of paper -> B32B5/06 , B32B5/067 , B32B5/073
[B32B 7/10] at least one layer having inter-reactive properties -- **Definition:** This place covers:  This group covers layered products in which a pair of interconnected layers is bonded by one or both layers having inter-reactive properties, wherein neither layer of the interconnected pair comprises an adhesive – whether a coated adhesive, a tie layer, or a layer described as acting as an adhesive.
[B32B 7/12] using interposed adhesives or interposed materials with bonding properties -- **Definition:** This place covers:  This group covers layered products comprising an adhesive – whether a coated adhesive, a tie layer or a layer described as acting as an adhesive – inserted between two layers to bond them.
[B32B 7/14] applied in spaced arrangements, e.g. in stripes -- The subclass B32B 7/14 covers layered products in which the layers are deposited or arranged with regular spacing, such as in stripe patterns, creating alternating material and void zones. It pertains to the relationship between layers where gaps or spaced intervals are deliberately introduced for functional or structural purposes.
[B32B 9/00] Layered products characterised by particular substances used -- B32B 9/00 relates to layered articles whose individual strata are defined by the particular material employed, such as polymers, metals, ceramics or composites, and where the choice of substance imparts distinct functional or structural characteristics to the product.
[B32B 9/002] comprising natural stone or artificial stone -- **Glossary:** - Artificial stone: Material made by crushing and grinding natural stone and then re-constituting it, e.g. with cement mortar or with a resin binder

This classification is specific to structures featuring at least two ceramic layers, emphasizing the composition and arrangement of these materials within the product.
[B32B 9/007] comprising carbon, e.g. graphite, composite carbon -- B32B 9/007 classifies layered products - such as honeycomb or cellular structures - where the individual strata incorporate carbon substances, for example graphite or carbon-fiber composites. The carbon component is used to impart properties like high strength, conductivity or thermal resistance to the layered material. This subclass falls under the broader group for performing operations on layered products.
[B32B 9/02] comprising animal or vegetable substances -- B32B 9/02 pertains to the manufacture of layered articles-such as honeycomb, cellular or other striated structures-in which at least one layer is formed from animal or vegetable substances, including proteins, polysaccharides, fats or other natural biomaterials, and covers the associated processes and resulting products.
[B32B 9/025] comprising leather -- The CPC subclass B32B 9/025 covers layered products in which leather is used as a constituent material, such as laminated panels, honeycomb or cellular structures that incorporate leather skins or cores. It pertains to inventions involving leather-based strata within composite or sandwich constructions.
[B32B 9/04] comprising such substance as the main or only constituent of a layer, next to another layer of a -- B32B 9/04 relates to layered products in which one stratum is composed mainly or solely of a specified substance and is positioned adjacent to another layer, covering constructions such as flat, cellular or honey-comb forms where the constituent material defines the layer.
[B32B 9/041] of metal -- B32B 9/041 pertains to layered products-cellular, honeycomb or other strata structures-where the layers are formed from metal. The code is used for metal-based laminar or honeycomb components employed in engineering, construction, aerospace and related fields.
[B32B 9/042] of wood -- B32B 9/042 covers methods for producing layered structures in which wood is the principal material, such as wood-based honeycomb, cellular or other stratiﬁed panels. The classification applies to processes that build up flat or non-flat strata from wood to create composite panels, cores or sandwich components.
[B32B 9/043] of natural rubber or synthetic rubber -- Subclass B32B 9/043 covers layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures that are made from natural rubber or synthetic rubber. The code applies to manufacturing processes and applications where these elastomeric materials form the striated or foamed core of the product.
[B32B 9/045] of synthetic resin -- B32B 9/045 pertains to layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures in which the individual strata are formed from synthetic resin. The classification, within the CPC hierarchy under Performing Operations - Layered Products - Layered Products, i.e. products built-up of strata, identifies the material used to create the layers.
[B32B 9/046] of foam -- B32B 9/046 pertains to layered products where one or more layers consist of foam materials. This classification is specific to the composition and use of foam in multi-layer constructions, addressing its properties and applications within the broader category of built-up strata.
[B32B 9/047] made of fibres or filaments -- B32B 9/047 covers layered products such as cellular or honeycomb structures whose strata are formed from fibres or filaments. It falls under the CPC section for performing operations on layered products, specifically those characterised by the use of fibrous or filamentous substances.
[B32B 9/048] made of particles -- This CPC subgroup covers layered products whose individual layers consist of discrete particles, such as honeycomb or cellular structures where the struts or walls are formed by fusing, sintering or otherwise assembling particles of a specific material.
[B32B 9/06] of paper or cardboard -- B32B 9/06 covers the manufacture and processing of layered articles whose individual strata are made of paper or cardboard, including honeycomb cores, sandwich panels and corrugated boards. The classification addresses methods for forming, bonding, shaping or treating such paper-based layered products.
[B33] ADDITIVE MANUFACTURING TECHNOLOGY -- B33 covers technologies for fabricating three-dimensional objects by adding material layer by layer, including methods such as laser sintering, material extrusion, vat polymerisation and powder-bed fusion. It encompasses equipment, process control, feedstock handling, post-processing and related software used in additive manufacturing.
[B33Y] ADDITIVE MANUFACTURING, i.e. MANUFACTURING OF THREE-DIMENSIONAL [3D] OBJECTS BY ADDITIVE DEPOSITION, ADDITIVE AGGLOMERATION OR ADDITIVE LAYERING, e.g. BY 3D PRINTING, STEREOLITHOGRAPHY OR SELECTIVE LASER SINTERING -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Technologies involving the use or application of processes or apparatus that produce three-dimensionally shaped structures by selectively depositing successive layers of material one upon another. In particular it covers processes, apparatus, materials, and other aspects of additive manufacturing, i.e., making, repairing, or modifying articles of manufacture by the selective application of multiple layers of material. The applied layers may be applied directly, as in a printing process, or by selective solidification of material onto a substrate or previously developed layers, for example, by selective sintering of a particulate.  **Glossary:** - 3D printing: Additive manufacturing where the buildup of successive layers of material includes the use of a printer-like device having a servo controlled head for dispensing materials that form the layers, similar to that used by inkjet printers - Stereolithography: Additive manufacturing technique where the successive layers of material are formed by selectively hardening regions of polymeric material successively applied to the structure, typically by the use of laser light.
[B33Y 10/00] Processes of additive manufacturing -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes and methods for manufacturing objects using additive manufacturing techniques. Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group:  (US 2010/0255213)
[B33Y 30/00] Apparatus for additive manufacturing -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group:  (US 2007/0023977)
[B33Y 40/00] Auxiliary operations or equipment, e.g. for material handling -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The handling or treating of materials used in an additive manufacturing process, or the subsequent treating or handling of objects produced by an additive manufacturing process. Also covered are ancillary components or process steps not directly involving the additive manufacturing process or apparatus, per se, such as cleaning raw materials used in the additive manufacturing process, or recycling residual material from the manufacturing process.  Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group:  (US 2013/0075957)
[B33Y 40/10] Pre-treatment -- B33Y 40/10 Pre-treatment covers auxiliary operations that prepare a material or substrate before an additive-manufacturing process, such as cleaning, surface conditioning, heat or chemical treatment, or other steps that enhance adhesion, flow or bonding of the feedstock.
[B33Y 40/20] Post-treatment, e.g. curing, coating or polishing -- This subclass covers processes applied after an additive-manufacturing build to improve properties, such as curing, applying protective or functional coatings, and mechanical finishing like polishing. It includes auxiliary equipment used for these post-treatment steps.

Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group:  (US 2013/0053995)
[B33Y 70/00] Materials specially adapted for additive manufacturing -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Subject matter related to the composition, structure, or other properties of the materials used in an additive manufacturing process to make an object.  Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group:  (US 2008/0122141)
[B33Y 70/10] Composites of different types of material, e.g. mixtures of ceramics and polymers or mixtures of metals and biomaterials -- B33Y 70/10 in the Cooperative Patent Classification concerns composites that combine different material types for use in additive manufacturing, including mixtures of ceramics with polymers or metals with biomaterials, enabling tailored properties in 3D printed objects.
[B33Y 80/00] Products made by additive manufacturing -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Products obtained by additive manufacturing  Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group:  (US 2014/0033538)
[B33Y 99/00] Subject matter not provided for in other groups of this subclass -- This group gathers patent subject matter relating to additive manufacturing that is not covered by any of the more specific groups within subclass B33Y. It serves as a residual category for any process, equipment, material or product feature of 3-D printing, stereolithography, selective laser sintering, or other layer-by-layer fabrication that does not fit elsewhere.
